The Rayne Syndicate

by MelissaIreneBurrowes

Archer is lost.

The last thing he remembers is being at a Team Rocket soireé. Now he's marooned on a semi-deserted island, with wildlife as familiar as they are distinct and a population that lives by the law of kill-or-be-killed.

He's starting to think he shouldn't have drunk that third martini.

Meanwhile, an urban redevelopment plan in Lumiose City unveils a beautiful new vision...with mega-secrets, which might have more to do with Archer's exotic island than anyone could begin to imagine.

Updates weekly. Pokémon Legends Z-A x Palworld crossover.

This fic was written during pre-release of Pokémon Legends Z-A and early-access of Palworld.

My website

Chapter 1 - The Kidnapping ✅

Archer Verdi swirled his drink around in the martini glass, so the festive lights decorating the parlor danced across the liquor, and decided it would be his last for tonight.

That was before they started talking about the damn woodchuck.

"There I was," hissed Meowth, the cream-furred cat arching his back for emphasis, "with my carton of milk, trapped between a stone wall and a savage Bidoof..."

"Oh Meowth, we've heard this story ten-million times," Jessie interjected.

"Yes, let me talk about my bottle cap collection now," James concurred.

Meowth bared his fangs at his two human friends in a little hiss. "Wait your turn."

Archer poured himself another drink. Beside him, his younger sister Kris chimed in excitedly, "I haven't heard the story about the Bidoof! What happened then, Meowth?"

Meowth continued regaling the tale with enthusiasm, while Archer excused himself and slipped away from their storytelling gathering to the rest of the party.

The soireé set an elegant stage for their organization's upper echelon and their high-society invitees to mill about in both business discussions and frivolous conversation. Archer did not want to be here. He probably wouldn't have come at all were it not for the request of his godfather, Team Rocket don Giovanni Delavita.

He could see Giovanni a distance away, talking with one of the planetary councilmen. Team Rocket was the world's most powerful crime syndicate, as influential as they were feared. The planetary council oversaw inter-regional government, yet the economy was Team Rocket's backstage, and Rocket Enterprises' recent monopoly in the manufacture of Poké Balls – the spherical pet carriers allowing trainers to shrink their animals down to size, and carry them about with ease – cemented their hold inflexibly. Pokémon were as essential to human civilization as they were invaluable companions, and practically everyone had one of the element-wielding animals if only for self-defence.

Archer himself was about twenty-nine in age. He was fairly easy to pick out from the crowd, with neatly combed teal-blue hair, tailored vest-suits, and refined manners that only hid deadly expertise as one of Team Rocket's admins; an elegant danger one might imagine of a high class thief or assassin. Working as one of Team Rocket's elites, of course, meant both descriptions were true. To that extent his colleagues James and Jessie could claim the same distinction, but they were casual in their way – by design, they'd told him, preferring to be more down-to-earth and catch their enemies unaware when they showed their true natures.

Perhaps the experiences Archer kept to himself had bestowed on him a more incisive way of approaching things, though he personally felt nothing good could have come out of past traumas.

"Must be an enigmatic thought that you're swirling in your mind," a feminine voice broke his thoughts. Archer looked up.

Standing before him was Mrs. Jett Silph from the Kalos region. She was at least fifty, blonde and fair with sky-blue eyes; the picture of old money through and through. Her husband had been the former CEO of the Silph Company, though upon his passing she had left Kanto and moved to Kalos, where she'd invested into acquisition of a then-fledgling land development company known as Quasartico Inc.

An unfailing prim and proper bearing belied sharp business sense. Jett had shown herself to be an astute investor, as well as shrewd in widening her connections, and had grown Quasartico's prominence and profit alike since she'd become its head. Her latest project was ostensibly less for profit and more of "giving back to the community" as she ostentatiously put it; Quasartico had gotten the contract for an urban redevelopment plan for Lumiose City, the largest city in the Kalos region, with the goal of bringing more wide swathes of parkland into civic areas for Pokémon to thrive. Archer didn't know much about it. He presumed it was one of those philanthropic gestures intended to make her company look good to the public.

"Some things need to be thought over," was Archer's reply; frankly he was not motivated to talk to a person who was almost a stranger about his personal issues.

"Don't think too much, honey," she said amicably, "sometimes one gets stressed out."

Archer gave her a slight smile back as protocol but answered nothing.

Jett stepped away and walked over to a group of people mingling around the buffet table; she immediately put on a bright smile and immersed herself in whatever conversation they were having. She sure has her socializing technique perfected, he thought.

He felt a sudden boredom, and stepped away from the parlor.

Archer retreated out to the veranda. The faraway hooting of a Noctowl lent charm to that rural area where Giovanni's elegant mansion was located; from here he could see the distant high-rises and glittering lights of the city proper, as well as the shimmering neon sign of Rocket Game Corner, their syndicate's flagship casino. Above an array of stars decorated the night sky with constellations, amidst which resided the crowning glory – the moon with its crescent-shape.

He stood and gazed up at it reverentially. A soft dusting of snowfall gently floated down to meet him. It was that early point of winter when the temperatures would only get colder from that point forth and the weather would eventually decide to blanket everything with white.

Suddenly, there was a flash as a Pokémon teleported in front of him – a little, letter-shaped creature with an eye, which floated before him with psychic ability. It was an Unown.

As he watched, more Unowns joined that one and squeaked at him in a chorus.

"Unowns? Here in Celadon City? Don't tell me you're the same group we've met before," Archer remembered. "What are you doing here?"

They responded with insistent squeaking, like they were all clamoring to talk at once. Archer, of course, could not speak Unown. However, the last time he'd met them they communicated by positioning themselves in the form of words.

"Can't you write what you're trying to say?" he prompted.

They all looked at each other. "Oh, there aren't enough of you here," Archer realized. He scrutinized the group and noticed a pattern in which Unowns were missing. "Where are all the vowels?"

More squeaking ensued.

Jessie and James emerged from the party, in each other's arms and whispering sweet-nothings like if they were the only people in the world. When Archer cleared his throat they looked up at him, the mood dampening considerably. "Archer. We didn't see you there." James sounded rather disappointed. "Hey...are those Unowns?"

"What are they doing here?" Jessie remarked.

"No clue. Where's Meowth?" inquired Archer.

"Having a fight with your sister's Eevee."

"Oh for the love of...is there another Pokémon here who can communicate with humans and could translate for us? Where's the boss' Persian?"

"Cheering on Eevee."

"Can't they write?" asked James, as the couple walked over.

Archer shrugged. "No vowels."

"That's no trouble," Jessie dismissed airily. "It's like playing a game of hang-man." She turned to face the Unowns, which were floating about ambivalently. "Spell what you can; we'll figure out what letters are missing. Now...where are the vowels?"

The Unown shifted their positions in mid-air to spell:

PLPGS SLND

"Do we have a...U?" guessed James.

One of the Unown gave a couple of sharp squeaks.

Archer watched this with skepticism. "Why can't one of you go interrupt the battle and bring Meowth out here?"

"Because he has sharp claws," Jessie replied straightforwardly.

To which Archer whirled about and headed towards the parlor. "I'll get my Houndoom to chase him out here."

The Unown drifted after him.

A small crowd had ringed around where Meowth and Eevee were facing off in a Pokémon battle.

Meowth pounced at his opponent, claws unsheathed, as the fluffy creature sprang fleetly back. Eevee was agile enough to dodge each one of Meowth's strikes; it angled one of its long ears back at its trainer for a directive.

"Eevee, Swift!" called Kris.

With a cry, Eevee let loose a barrage of gleaming energy shards. They went flying towards Meowth – and Archer, who had accidentally walked up at the precise moment and position to be in the line of fire.

"Archer look out!" Kris cried.

"Shit...!" Archer exclaimed, ducking aside.

The Unowns surrounded him at the same instant; there was a flash of light, and Swift shards pelted empty ground as all the spectators' attention diverted immediately from the battle.

The Unowns had vanished.

So had Archer.

Bright tropical sunlight hit Archer instantly, so sudden it caused him to flinch his eyes away. What had happened? One second he'd been at the party; the next...

There was the sound of the seashore, and the murmured noises of wildlife. He opened his eyes blearily and was met with three rotund sheep Pokémon standing about him as if in awe of his appearance.

Wooloo.

They stood on their hind legs.

"Wait a sec..." Archer gave a double-take, and the three bipedal Wooloo, startled, bleated loudly and ran away. They scattered into the distant tall grass and trees.

Since when did Wooloo walk on their hind legs?

Maybe they taught themselves, like Jessie and James' Meowth, reasoned Archer, who thought no more of it as he glanced around the beach and the shimmering ocean horizon. The sun was unbearably hot, especially in comparison to the snowy climate he'd been in mere moments ago.

Nothing there looked familiar at all. "Those damned Unowns," he muttered.

His first guess was he was somewhere in the Hoenn region. He'd based it on the tropical foliage and distant mountain peak which he presumed to be Mount Chimney, yet the moment he turned round he realized there was no way this was Hoenn.

It was a tall spire hewn of stone, atop which was inscribed a single, glowing Unown letter I – for international? interconnected? He couldn't imagine why an I.

There were no other manmade structures anywhere in sight, let alone architectural marvels such as this skyscraper in the midst of nowhere. As he neared the building, he could see something had been scrawled on the side wall like graffiti; it looked like it had been painted recently, yet it was written in Unown lettering:

THE TOWER IS THE KEY
THE TREES HOLD THE TRUTH

Archer stared at it in wonderment.

On his belt, Houndoom's Poké Ball began shaking, and Archer pressed the center button to let the Pokémon out of the red-and-white sphere. Houndoom emerged in a flare of white light; it was a lean attack dog with black fur and antelopine horns, and a tapered tail that flared into a tufted arrow point of fur at the tip. It looked around at the unfamiliar surroundings, then at its trainer with a quizzical whine.

"I don't know where we are either," Archer answered what he presumed it was asking him.

He began looking around the tower for an entry, only to halt when he heard a sizeable group of people coming up the trail.

In the same way as he'd been quick to presume his location, his first instinct now was relief. People meant answers and a way to contact home. Once again, that first impression of his was totally subverted.

They were shouting in a language Archer didn't recognize at all. Their attire was some strange mix of handmade boots and fingerless gloves, and a more modern-styled jumpsuit with a cowl.

They also had guns.

The latter part didn't escape notice, least of all when they began shooting at him. Archer ducked down as Houndoom bolted in front, sending out a shimmering energy barrier to shield them both. The bullets struck the force field and harmlessly bounced off.

Houndoom's Protect was successfully blocking the gunfire; however, Archer knew it couldn't be sustained for long. The moment the men stopped shooting, both out of bullets and seemingly confused, Archer sprang to take the advantage.

"Inferno!" he called, and Houndoom dutifully unleashed an explosive wave of fire. It burst from its jaws towards the ground spreading outward and their enemies yelled and haphazardly tried to evade. A few fell to the ground, trying desperately to put out flames that now clung to their clothes.

Archer's vengeful delight at having the upper hand was short-lived. He could see them reloading their guns.

"Houndoom, return," ordered Archer, recalling his Pokémon to its capsule in a flash of red light. Then he ran.

The jungle was not too dense; there were paths between the trees, and creeks narrow enough to bound over easily. Training kicked in from years back, when he was newly rising in Team Rocket rank, and he might have been able to maneuver deftly about the landscape for some time were it not for a poor twist of fate.

A sharp pain pierced his arm; Archer stumbled and ducked behind a tree. Almost immediately he started to become faint, and he realized it was a poison dart.

"Fuck..."

He could barely curse his pursuers, or his ill fortune, or those blasted Unown again for teleporting him here, before darkness quickly overtook his vision and he collapsed into unconsciousness.

Chapter 2 - A Piece of Cake ✅

Archer stirred gradually, unsure how long he'd been asleep and not feeling rested at all. On the contrary, he felt ill. Talk about a hangover. What a horrible nightmare...

Then he heard the sounds of people and activity around him.

His eyes snapped open and immediately he'd leapt to his feet, nearly reeling over from vertigo. He was in a large metal cage, with barely a couple of paces to walk in either direction, in the center of an encampment.

It hadn't been a nightmare. He really was God-knows-where and a captive.

Captive. It brought back memories; awful memories, which sent a shiver coursing through his body with the horrifying thought of having to possibly re-experience a past ordeal.

Calm down. You've got to figure out a way to escape; you can do that better if you're not in a turmoil. Getting terrified will get you nowhere, he told himself, as if it could somehow convince his frantic mind to cooperate. At least he was determined not to show his fear, that much was a given, however it made internalizing it all the worse.

His captors were scattered about the site, some guarding the periphery with their rifles, others milling about a campfire discussing something in the unknown language Archer had heard them speaking before. That was a further frustration to his plight. If he only knew what they were saying, at least he wouldn't feel at such a disadvantage – beyond, of course, the general indignity of being trapped in a cage.

He couldn't quite get over their duality, either. These people appeared both ancient and modern, as if contemporary attire and weaponry had met a primitive lifestyle and manner and adopted the worst characteristics of both. He caught a glimpse of red and noticed a couple of them examining a Poké Ball, which they tossed onto the ground. Being locked, it rolled without opening, and they snatched it back up with evident confusion.

They don't seem to realize how to unlock Houndoom's Poké Ball, Archer thought with satisfaction, With a little luck that'll keep them busy till I can break out of here. Assholes, stealing my Pokémon...especially when I'm the one from Team Rocket.

No one was really paying attention to him, or at least they seemed not to be. Archer began trying to devise a way to unlatch the door. He'd soon determined the lock needed a special key, and was trying to figure out who among these barbarians might have it – if he could lure them close on some pretense, maybe he could pickpocket it – when he startled at a motion that came into view in the edge of his sight, outside of the cage bars.

She was perhaps only a couple of years younger than he, and wore a black, hand-sewn leather jacket and skirt, as well as a cloth shirt painted with a jagged pattern. She had pink hair with a swath of ebony she'd combed off to the side, soft features he thought far too delicate for the savage ways of her peers, and violet eyes he could easily have likened to amethysts – they had the same translucency and brilliant depths.

The woman said something to him in the strange language. To Archer it was unintelligible.

"I really wish I knew what you were saying. Please get a translator," he grumbled with annoyance, "or a key to unlock the fucking cage."

Her eyes flew open wide. "You speak the ancient language?"

Archer immediately glanced up at her, gratified to hear her speaking as he did. "Finally, someone who understands me! Look, there's got to be a misunderstanding. I was teleported here by a bunch of wild Pokémon."

"Pokémon?" echoed the woman.

"Pokémon. Animals."

"Oh – Pals!"

"Well, they can be pals, I guess," Archer conceded, "The point is they sent me here, then your group ambushed me and stole Houndoom..."

"Houndoom," the woman interjected, "is that your Rayhound?"

"My dog," Archer replied.

"I've never seen a Rayhound that uses fire attacks. None of us in the Syndicate have."

They call themselves a syndicate? thought Archer skeptically, reflecting on how the pressed suits and uniformed attire of Team Rocket agents would stand in contrast to these guerillas.

"None of us have seen a red and white Pal Sphere either. Or one that won't open whenever someone throws it," she went on, apparently referring to the Poké Ball.

"It's locked by magic," he said, half as a joke, half in a genuine attempt to bluff them into thinking he was a sorcerer or something and letting him go, like he'd seen in an old film somewhere where the hero was captured by natives.

She didn't bat an eye either way. "I'm the tower guardian. Besides that my father was the Syndicate boss," she told him. "Before that, his father was boss, and his father's father..."

"You said 'was'..." Archer interjected, "Who's the boss now?"

"No one yet. I was an only child so I'm next in line, technically..." Her reply trailed off a bit.

"If you're the heir apparent you can let me go, can't you?" Archer pursued.

"It isn't so easy."

She spoke tersely, yet before Archer could say a word in response an idea appeared to alight in her eyes. "Wait right here."

Sure, why not? Where else would I go? Archer thought, leaning against the bars of the cage as he watched her sprint away to talk to some of the elders.

They had a vociferous discussion. Archer couldn't understand any of it, but it was evidently contentious. Finally, the woman returned.

"They won't let you go."

Archer pressed his head against the bars.

"They say you're an outsider," the woman added. "Unless you're part of our Syndicate, you're an enemy."

"Can't they make me an honorary member of the Syndicate and let me go? Honestly I don't want to start any kind of trouble; your group attacked me, not the other way around. I'd just as soon take my Pokémon and get out of here."

"Where will you go?" asked the woman.

"Home."

"Where is your home?"

"Away from here," Archer said, "that much I can tell you! What are they planning to do with me, anyway?"

"Feed you to Faleris."

"Of all the fucking... What the hell is a Faleris?"

"The great fire-falcon that belongs to the island ruler. In return for not destroying our encampment and providing us with grain, he demands tribute every month in the form of a meal for Faleris. Hunting has been bad for us this season... You know, you can't get out that way," she added with nonchalance when she saw him tugging desperately at the bars.

"Well I don't exactly intend to sit still and be Poké-food," he snapped.

"Are you alone?" she asked.

What the fuck is that supposed to mean? What's she getting at? "There's no one else with me," Archer replied. "If there was, I can assure you, your ragtag group of guerrillas would all be in deep shit right now." A thought occurred to him and he glanced back up at her. She was still watching him with those doelike violet eyes. "Look, if you're asking would anyone miss me, that's not the point. Is there a reason why you can't find some other shmuck to feed to the bird?"

"You're not part of our Syndicate."

"If you make me part of the Syndicate, I'll find a way to drive off Faleris and his owner so you won't have to worry about them anymore."

"Drive them off?" she exclaimed, astonished. "Centuries ago, many tried to overthrow the island rulers and none ever succeeded. In modern days no one's ever dared. We've never seen any Pal strong enough to defeat Faleris."

"You'd never seen a fire type Houndoom, either. I'll handle them, but you people have to let me out of here first. Capisce?"

She gazed at him quizzically, and he clarified, "Understand?"

"I understand," she said tentatively, "but I'll have to convince the others."

"Please try. As soon as you can," Archer urged her. He didn't want to spend a minute longer there.

Archer tried every possible manner he could think of to get out of the cage by himself. He was about ready to give up when around sunset the cage was suddenly unlocked and his captors motioned him out at gunpoint.

He was led to a long wooden table they'd placed in the middle of their encampment, around which it looked like the entire group was congregated as if in expectance. The woman with the pink hair was here too, fidgeting with unease. Great, Archer thought pessimistically, it's not enough they want to feed me to a man-eating Pokémon, they actually set a table for it.

When he got nearer he noticed that in the center of the table was...a cake.

It was a rather plain cake, but it looked rather out of place there nonetheless. A berry was placed atop it, of a variety he didn't recognize, and the frosting looked more like thick cream. Before he could make some kind of sarcastic comment about whether the dessert would pair well with the intended main course, the lady whispered to him with urgency.

"If you wish to live, cut a piece of cake and offer it to me."

He looked first at her, then at the stern faced militants all clutching their weapons and glaring at him as if this was their ultimatum. What the hell, Archer decided, and proceeded without comment to cut a slice of cake.

It was only when she accepted the piece from him that a jubilant cry rang out across the whole group, and Archer gave her a worried, questioning, look.

"Welcome to our Syndicate," she said with a coy smile.

He smiled back, a little nervously, but at least they didn't seem to want to kill him anymore.

The rest of the evening was spent in a happy party, with everyone there dancing and singing into the lateness of night, and Archer went along with it, even when he was shoved towards the pink-haired lady so they could dance together. He realized he still didn't know her name, but figured it hardly mattered, considering he just needed to find a good moment to grab Houndoom's Poké Ball and discreetly slink away now that she'd gotten him free. They didn't let him out of their sight, to his chagrin.

There was still something amiss going on; Archer couldn't place it, but he could sense it in the way the group regarded him – and her.

He started to realize what was going on when they pushed them together into a tent alone and shut the door flaps tight, while the rest of the people continued their revelry outside.

Archer looked at the woman expectantly.

She was seated on the elaborately decorated bedding that had been laid out on the ground, bearing an almost apologetic look. "We're a little bit married now."

Archer stared at her, only stared, till he finally blurted out:

"What do you mean 'a little bit married'?"

"I couldn't take over the Syndicate as boss unless I married," she explained, "and as the tower guardian I could only marry someone who spoke the ancient language. You were going to be killed unless you were accepted into the Syndicate, and the only way an outsider will be accepted is if they take a spouse from within..."

"I get it," he cut her off tersely.

She said nothing else and he sighed, deciding he'd been a bit too caustic with her when, all things considered, at least he was still alive. He sat down beside her.

"If I've got a wife, I ought to know her name."

"Zoe Rayne."

He imagined from the islanders' language she'd have a name unpronounceable to him, or at least something overly exotic. Her name sounded like something he'd easily have heard back home.

"I ought to know my husband's name too," Zoe ventured.

"Archer Verdi."

"I'm sorry Archer, pretending you were my secret suitor visiting me from the nearby town and that we wanted to get married was the only way I could think of to get us both out of a bind."

"The problem is, I'm not going to be staying around. I have a life outside of this island."

"You said you were alone."

"Unattached, yes. But I have friends and family and property that I'm not about to just up and forget." He glanced at the bedding and pillows; they all had a uniquely bohemian design, with jagged lines interspersing mandala patterns, and depictions of a rare kind of lizard Pokémon probably a little too risqué for the Kanto region. "Why is everything here painted with well-endowed pink Salazzle?"

"What are Salazzle?" inquired Zoe.

He motioned to the fabric. "The lizards."

"They're symbols of fertility throughout Palpagos Island."

"Is that where we are? ...Palpagos Island?" He'd never heard of the place.

"You have different names for things," Zoe observed. "Like referring to Pals as Pokémon. The Pal Spheres you have are different...even your Pal is different."

"Because I'm not from this island. I need to get back home."

"Legends say there are people just like us across the ocean, who use different tools than we and live in harmony with Pals."

The way his heart leapt to hear that was immeasurable. It was the first good news he'd heard yet. She quickly stifled his joy.

"That's all they are," Zoe told him. "Legends."

"How can you be sure?" Archer asked.

"There is nothing beyond the sea," she insisted. "Those who have tried to make the voyage never return. The ocean is said to plummet into red fire."

"You're talking like the planet is flat. No one's believed that since prehistoric times. Haven't you ever flown up high on a bird Pokémon – er, Pal – and seen the horizon?"

The blank look on her face spoke volumes.

"No bird is strong enough to go that high! If you try, you'll both perish in the sun," she replied, echoing a tale Archer recalled having once heard as a prehistoric myth from some faraway region. "Besides, in any event, trying to fly beyond the sea is outlawed."

Outlawed? Now we're getting somewhere, thought Archer, who was cynically starting to piece together something about the island's state of affairs. "Who outlawed it?"

"The island rulers...the PIDF."

"The PIDF?"

"The Palpagos Island Defense Force. Colonel Marcus' men."

Archer smirked at such a trite name for their army. It seemed to him Team Rocket had a better ring to it. At least it was more honest in its way of implying lofty aspirations than acting like they were actually there to defend anything. "They must have a leader. What's the guy's name?"

"Marcus Dryden."

Again, the name sounded unexceptional. "Who appointed him leader?"

"The commission."

"Who appointed the commission?"

"Marcus Dryden."

"So Mr. Dryden is basically the island king because he decided to be, and he tells you he'll destroy your village unless you feed his bird a snack every month, and on top of that no one can leave the island."

Team Rocket could probably mow down this banana republic and take it for ourselves, thought Archer, as they deferentially settled down on opposite sides of the bedding for the rest of the night.

The idea of Team Rocket seizing an island territory that it seemed not even the planetary council knew of was entertaining yet inconsequential at present. He had worse problems at hand; he had to find a way off said island to get home. Zoe had mentioned a 'nearby town' hadn't she? If there was a town somewhere, and a ruling government – even if they were some kind of dictatorship – then perhaps they had the means to travel to or contact other regions, if only for themselves.

After all, they wouldn't prohibit leaving the island unless they knew what lay beyond the sea to begin with.

Chapter 3 - The Quasartico Connection ✅

Civilization held no finer regency than in historical Lumiose City.

Quaint shingled businesses and ornate two-story apartments lined boulevards that stretched in a wide, circular pattern towards a meeting point in the center plaza, where the graceful pillar of Prism Tower stood. At least half of the city's buildings bore historical designation, dating all the way back to the region's renaissance period. They were a peculiar blend of aristocratic charm with casual beauty, distinctly Kalosian in their architectural design.

For Jett, whose company had been tasked with bringing about a new renaissance period for the region, they were abhorrent. Privately, of course; she would never say so or admit it in public. It was less fault she found with the design as it was the fact her development project had to work around them. Many of the landowners could not be prevailed upon to sell, but even when they did, getting permits to demolish buildings with historical designation was next to impossible.

From her penthouse office in the modern-styled headquarters of Quasartico Inc. she could see most of Lumiose City at a glance. Her plans had already taken shape, to develop sprawling parks that would wind like miniature wild routes through the city, and by nightfall organize a vibrant battling tournament to take place on rooftop stadiums. With the city council's approval, she already had free rein for this much at least.

All of this would turn a profit, one way or the other. If the cost of planting a tree was one-hundred dollars, they would charge five-hundred. The proper maintenance of routes for wildlife habitat and easy hunting could be costly, and if Quasartico Inc. was appointed to oversee it within city limits that amount would be funneled accordingly. Pokémon battle tournaments always drew a gambling crowd, too.

Now only if she could get the damn demolition permits.

However, Jett was not one to accept no for an answer, nor one who would hesitate at what necessity wrought.

All these things swirled like a tempest in her mind as she gazed out her office window that drizzling morning. She would give them one final opportunity.

Within the hour, Jett was arriving to a meeting at City Hall. All the members of the city council were eager to discuss the various agendas they had. Before long, however, they were all embroiled in argument.

"This happens every time I bring up my points of discussion!" Jett argued, "I have plenty of money to turn this old, decrepit town into something marvelous and breathtaking, and the lot of you refuse to step into the future."

"It's not that we refuse to 'step into the future'," interjected a council member, "it's that we don't agree of your vision that this town is decrepit. It is old because it is historical, and that is reason enough to fix whatever is broken but not tear down buildings that have historical significance."

"Nonsense," Jett interrupted, "Look at Prism Tower...it supposed to be one of the town's newer structures and even it has to be reinforced." Jett was getting noticeably irritated as she went on, "You can't even open the top of Prism Tower to tourists anymore, the top floor is one misstep away from a collapse and the rooftop garden is growing wild."

"Your company already has the contract for the largest-scale urban redevelopment project Lumiose has seen in years," a second councilman spoke, "Granting demolition permits for historically irreplaceable buildings should be off the table, because let's be frank, you may wish to reinforce Prism Tower but you've already stated less prominent structures should be bulldozed in the name of progress."

"In the name," said Jett emphatically, "of making a city that truly encapsulates both modern life and coexistence with Pokémon."

The head councilman struck his gavel to the table. "Enough! This argument is getting old. Time to vote on it... Show of hands please, who agrees with Mrs. Silph's position?" No one raised their hands in support and Jett felt her face flush. It was not from embarrassment but rather from intense anger. She was seething with fury.

"My apologies Mrs. Silph," said the head councilman, "but it looks as if you have failed to convince the members of this committee..."

He never got to finish his statement. Jett got up abruptly, gathered the papers she had brought with her and stuffing them into her briefcase, stormed away from the table. "You are all a bunch of idiots!" she yelled as she exited the room.

The others at the meeting looked at each other and said nothing, but the head councilman simply shrugged his shoulders and dismissed the situation. "That's been settled; let's discuss more urgent matters."

For Mrs. Jett Silph, however, it had not been settled. If they wouldn't oblige her in her request, then it would fall on a backup plan she'd already arranged for. The minute she returned to her office, she picked up the telephone on her desk and began dialling a number.

"...yes, I'm calling to ensure this week's shipment is ready to fly out. ...The same coordinates as always. Your discretion will be well paid."

The drizzling rain subsided by mid-day and she left the office. She opened two Poké Balls and sent out two of her Pokémon: the poodle-like Furfrou, and a Clefable. They followed her cheerily as she strolled outside.

There was a white-and-red food truck that perpetually parked in a plaza off on the south side of Lumiose City, with a few tables scattered around for people to eat, and a beautiful view of a pond ringed with trees.

For all it looked like a casual eatery, it really wasn't. The food was gourmet and the prices matched. It did, however, create an outdoor gathering-place for Lumiose's executives and top citizens to get away from their office desks and meet informally at lunchtime.

Jett bought a croissant and went in search of the person she'd come here to meet. She spied him quickly, sitting at one of the furthest tables to the side of the little crowd.

Corbeau was thirty-five, always dressed in tailored black suits that complemented his lean physique, with round glasses framing sharp amber eyes and aubergine hair he kept short and combed to one side. He had taken over the Lumiose gym from the prior gym leader, Clemont, one year ago. Unlike his predecessor, Corbeau specialized in raising poison type Pokémon and presently ran the gym from within his private company headquarters.

It was his off-duty work that was questionable; as boss of the Rust Syndicate, he was a gym leader with underworld ties just like Giovanni in the Kanto region, and he likewise fancied his organization as powerful and as sinister as Team Rocket, however Jett knew that Corbeau's influence barely extended outside of Kalos. Still, Corbeau was someone the people of Lumiose knew to get along with, or at least not to fall afoul of if they wished to continue living, and as Jett was an artist in both tact and cordiality it was easy for her to cultivate a friendship with him.

They saw each other, and Corbeau motioned to the other seat at the table. She walked over and sat down.

"Heard you had a little jaunt to the Kanto region the other day," Corbeau mentioned.

"Networking opportunities. You know how it is."

"Yes, I know how it is. Of course, you still impress me. Taking up with the folks who murdered your late husband is something I didn't envision you as cold-blooded enough for."

Jett hesitated. "My marriage into the Silph family was more a matter of society...and it's not like Mr. Silph ever tried to pretend it wasn't."

She frowned pensively, for just a moment, yet shook away the recollections with her usual aplomb.

"I don't think Team Rocket would hold any disagreements they had with my late husband against me," she went on. "Giovanni owns the Silph Company now, and I haven't gotten in his way."

Corbeau nodded and replied, "Well, I have no dispute with Mr. Delavita. Our families have been on neutral terms for years, and so long as his Team Rocket stays out of Kalos it will remain that way. By the same token, my Rust Syndicate can't protect you on their territory. If it's up to me I'll keep the peace we have with them."

"I don't want war with them any more than you do," she said.

"I guess those supply shipments you're chartering out of the airport don't have a link?" Corbeau asked.

Corbeau's piercing amber eyes were watching her straightforwardly, and Jett briefly averted her gaze towards her food. She had her own topics to bring up and things to request, and here she now was trying to field his questions. When did he ever find out about my chartered flights, anyhow?

"The one thing Giovanni was unable to get from the Silph Co. acquisition was what my late husband left me in secret," Jett tentatively confided, "a business connection far from any known region. They quietly provided Silph Co. with low-cost tumblestone and ore for Poké Ball manufacturing, and as payment they were quietly sent return shipments of certain items. I took over the business arrangement upon my husband's passing."

"Except you aren't in the Poké Ball business. No one except Team Rocket is since they monopolized the market," Corbeau replied.

"You have my word it has nothing to do with Team Rocket at all," Jett assured him. "The business liaison, in fact, is not even in Team Rocket territory. It's my own little business enterprise I have on the side...certainly you would be the last person to go against that?"

"I only care that it doesn't affect my own interests. So long as it doesn't, you have my every wish that you profit."

"On the matter of profit," Jett said, redirecting the conversation, "you're aware of my land development project with the city."

"Yes, although from what I heard you had a small disagreement with the city council this morning."

"Is there any way that your people can get me those demolition permits?"

"Not a chance."

"Mr. Corbeau, I know financial matters are as important to you as they are to me. If you're worried about the cost involved..."

"It's not that I don't want to help you. But even I know what we can and can't achieve."

"And Lumiose is so sacrosanct?" Jett replied.

When Corbeau's sole response was to give a disinterested shrug, Jett pursued the topic further:

"You can probably testify to the fact that Prism Tower needs work done. The gym was traditionally one of the establishments on the ground floor, and from what I understand the League approved your request to move from there on the spot when you showed the inspectors around."

He took a pensive sip of his coffee. "It's good business sense to welcome more wild Pokémon into the city. It means trainers hang around Lumiose longer, they spend money at the local marts, restaurants, Pokémon groomers... I know that means having to expand the park areas, and maybe we could do without some of the city's smaller structures, but I doubt they'll give you Prism Tower. That's a landmark."

Jett shook her head, allaying his concerns. "It's the outlying buildings that Lumiose doesn't need, in the historic and lower-class areas. Prism Tower can be renovated. We could probably finish that project in a year and a half, easily, so I really don't know what the city council want."

"It's just as well," replied Corbeau, "the city's only back-up power switch is atop Prism Tower. They probably don't want attention drawn to that."

This took her a moment to sink in. "Do you mean the entire Lumiose City power grid can be shut from the top of that crumbling building?"

"When the power plant outside Lumiose had that Magnemite problem some years back they thought it best to put a safety switch up somewhere that couldn't get hijacked by wild electric Pokémon. After all, what can get up there?" he smirked, "A Zapdos?"

"I shudder to ask how good the power lines are, then."

"Oh the electric infrastructure is fine. It's just the building that needs work. But you have your heart set on fixing that, I guess."

She returned a polite smile, and Corbeau glanced at his watch and stood. "I've got to get back to the gym. Good luck with the redevelopment plan."

"Thanks," she said as he left with his cup of coffee. She watched the gym leader stroll away down the sidewalk and turn the corner.

Jett went home afterwards, packed a bag and headed off to the ocean pier that housed her personal yacht. Her captain was waiting for her when she arrived, and the vessel sailed out of the harbor quietly.

Fisherman's Point was a seaside town as ramshackle as the island's main settlement, with huts and narrow docks alike hammered together haphazardly out of wood. The smell of fish was inescapable here – be it cooked seafood, or freshly-caught, or drying out – though most of this bounty was handed off to the island leadership, leaving the residents to survive on berries, or catch food for themselves in secret. One of the town's saving graces was that it sporadically had electric power, due to one of the inhabitants having a couple of electric type Pals and a crude setup of transformers, and the PIDF guard assigned to oversee the town being willing to overlook it provided his house could siphon some electricity too. But this was only available during a couple of hours in the afternoon, due to the Pokémon only being able to exert themselves so much with their attacks and needing to recharge their energy.

Jett disliked how rustic it was. At least she had the yacht to provide her with the creature comforts she was accustomed to from the Kalos region, and two PIDF guards posted on the pier to keep curious locals at bay. She understood that they told the islanders this elegant and unusual boat was a government matter, and unless they wanted to fall afoul of the great commander Marcus Dryden they should keep a good distance. She never had any trouble, the few times she'd visited Palpagos Island.

For years her husband's family had quietly been sending shipments of crude oil and materiel to Palpagos Island in exchange for cheap tumblestone used in the manufacture of Poké Balls, and other such accoutrements; how the Drydens managed such cost-effective labor, the Silphs were astute enough not to ask, though they certainly availed themselves of it across generations.

Jett had consequently been introduced to Marcus Dryden, so he knew her already when she reached out via the usual channels. He'd expressed sincere condolences when Jett told him of her husband's passing, and been more than gracious when informed she would take over the shipments. When he heard that what she wanted in return was not material for Poké Balls, but something he'd been planning to do anyway – well, that made their alliance all the better.

Marcus arrived punctually at the agreed time. "Nice to see you again, Jett; hope you're well," he said.

Colonel Marcus Dryden was a tall man. Sandy blond hair complemented rugged features and brown eyes. The military coat he held over his shoulders as a cloak was partly woven of some kind of gold thread, and the ruff made of black fur.

"I am fine," she replied, "I did want to let you know the next drop is later this week."

"Good. I have the Pal you left here on your prior visit running a little task for me elsewhere, so that's why I didn't bring it along. ...I guess everything's uneventful over in Kalos?" he asked.

Jett smiled slightly to herself. "You have no need to be concerned over that. I assure you, there would be no difficulty at all, so long as you start at the southeastern side of Lumiose City, and aim straight at its heart."

Omission was a matter of expediency here, she reflected, a key to her unspoken strategy. A military strike on the mainland would surely lead nowhere, except maybe to Marcus Dryden's own demise...but it would get half of the city razed. And then Quasartico Inc. could rebuild Lumiose from scratch, and launder billions in the process.

"Yes, you've told me the southeast has the weakest defenses," said Marcus, returning her smile with a smirk of his own, "I still intend to launch my invasion of the Kalos region, but I'd like to make up for the wait you've endured. I have something new to show you; that is, if you're up to it."

"Oh, yes, I am. What is it?"

"It's best if I show you in person."

He led the way out onto the ship's deck, with Jett recalling her Pokémon to their Poké Balls before following him. With a toss of a Pal Sphere, Marcus sent out his Faleris, which crowed loudly and flattened itself so they could both get on its back.

Faleris was a Corviknight. The bird was as imposing as its master, with the height of a dragon Pokémon and equally sharp yellow eyes, displaying brilliant red plumage instead of the black feathers Corviknight was known to possess. However, Jett knew all the island's wildlife were in some way unique in comparison to the Pokémon on the mainland, and the locals here referred to them by different names too.

Faleris took wing, towards the Astral Mountains; Jett hung on for dear life, but the flight was shorter than she'd expected. They landed amidst a desolate city on the mountainside.

Marcus helped her down and then led the way a short distance, eventually halting at what once had been an intersection with a decorative archway overhanging the street. He turned and gestured to the exotic red flowers growing in profusion along the cracked sidewalks and trying to climb the buildings.

They were small and scarlet, with three triangular petals tapered to a point adorned by black accents, and bearing what one could easily presume to be the stamen of the flower rising in the center like a steep pyramid. Leafy, dewy vines spread out around the blossom, covering the earth with green foliage; some of the flowers seemed to be trying to climb the walls, and those had grown as big as the palm of one's hand, though none had succeeded in the endeavor of scaling the buildings completely. Large herbivorous Pals in the area were grazing on them, keeping them in check.

"Well then, I recall you saying you needed something to beautify the road verges in Lumiose," said Marcus. "What do you think?"

Jett took one look at the flowers and gave a delighted gasp, exclaiming, "Marcus, they're beautiful!"

"I had a feeling you'd be pleased."

"What are they called?"

"Called?"

"Well the islanders can't merely call them 'beautiful flowers' can they? They must have a name."

He relented. "I believe they're known as Eternal Flowers. They're said to represent eternity...in one way or another."

"How do you care for them? Is there any specific amount of water or sunlight you have to provide them?"

"Not at all. They're hardier than they look. Plant them anywhere you like, and I guarantee they'll grow bigger than you expect."

She gladly accepted fifty pots of the flowers, and returned cheerfully to her development project in Lumiose City.

Marcus, in turn, left for his office at the island's main settlement, to wait. The horse had been delivered to Troy.

Chapter 4 - Island Customs ✅

The next morning, bright and early, the Syndicate members dragged Archer out of bed, returned Houndoom's Poké Ball, and half-guided half-shoved him to the exit of the camp. Archer couldn't believe his good fortune. They were really letting him go? Well, they were making Zoe come with him, anyway, but they were really letting him go?

"Technically we're on our honeymoon," Zoe explained, dampening his enthusiasm only a little. "We're expected to dwell for a time on the outskirts of the encampment, living off the land. On the new moon, we return."

"You have an awful lot of customs," remarked Archer, who was secretly scheming. The sooner he was out of their sight the sooner he could make a proper break for it.

Zoe was unusually quiet as they made their way across the landscape. She waited until they were reasonably far from the camp and Archer hesitated on a grassy hill, trying to figure out where to go next, before she spoke up.

"I suppose you'll be heading on your way now."

He glanced sideways at her. "What happens if I do?"

"Well...I can't return to the encampment alone. If I did, we'd both be screwed."

"Both of us?"

"Me because they'd think I was defiled, you because they'll hunt you for sport."

"Zoe...dear..." he said hesitantly, "was there no other way to get me out of that cage other than your brilliant plan to get us hitched? You couldn't steal the key or maybe, I don't know, pick the lock?"

"None that'd solve both our situations at once," she replied blithely. "I always think the best thing is to kill two Chikipi with one stone."

Archer didn't know what the hell a Chikipi was, nor did he have any particular interest at this point in the island dialect – they evidently, he'd concluded, renamed half the Pokémon species and common items merely to spite him. He arbitrarily picked a direction and set off walking down the slope with Zoe in tow.

"You said you were the tower guardian," Archer remarked, when it became plain that she wouldn't leave, "Is that the same tower where your group found me?"

"It is."

"What's the place supposed to be for, anyway?"

"No one knows."

The response made him halt in his tracks. "Yet you guard it."

"We guard it, but no one remembers why we guard it," Zoe answered. "It's just there, and we're just here, so at this point why not?"

"God, I need to get back home," Archer muttered, and continued trudging across the grass. "Which direction is the nearby town?"

"A little less than two day's travel towards the sunrise."

"Two days?" he echoed. If that was the nearby town, he couldn't imagine how long it would take to reach the faraway ones. Figuring he'd best hurry his pace, he veered his course to head east. The sooner he reached the town, the sooner he might find some way to get home, or so he presumed.

The landscape was as beautiful as any route from the territories he knew of, only different. The tropical foliage bore countless unknown flowers, and familiar berries were painted with peculiar colors that made Archer stop and second-guess if they were the same kind of fruits at all. The animals, however, were the most striking. He caught a glimpse of two albino Eevee scampering into the bushes, a creature stretching in the sun that he thought at first glance was a Clefable before noticing its shorter Jigglypuff-like ears, and more of the bipedal Wooloo clustering in a herd.

At some point he stopped on a grassy hill to watch two wild elephants in a battle; what he knew as Copperajah, except these beasts were covered in a thick coat of leafy green fur. They were locking tusks and blasting each other with gleaming energy attacks and cascades of sharp-edged leaves.

"We call them Mammorest," Zoe explained, coming up to stand beside him, "they're grass types."

When the sky started darkening, they decided to set up camp for the night. They found a flat clearing partly ringed by trees, with enough space to easily lie beneath the sky, and collected branches to make a small campfire. Archer unlocked Houndoom's Poké Ball and threw it onto the grass, sending out the Pokémon, which gave a happy bark and spun about to light the pyramid of dry branches into a crackling blaze.

He then watched with interest as Zoe retrieved some Poké Balls of her own.

They were of the antique models that had a gold spire on either end, yet seemingly brand-new; the capsules appeared to be made not of apricorn but of tree bark, allowing the peculiar glow of the tumblestone lining that made all Poké Balls functional to permeate outside. When the light passed through the bark it appeared to be light blue, as opposed to the warmer tone he knew it emitted within.

Zoe gave the spheres a small toss into the air, and the creatures they held emerged when they struck the ground. One was a little blue penguin, which hopped over to Archer's ankles and gazed up at him; the other was a small green monkey with a leaf-tufted tail and a sprig of leaves on its head – pointed leaves, as opposed to the more rounded leaves Archer had seen this kind of Pokémon with in the past. He observed both animals skeptically.

"These are my Pals, Pengullet and Tanzee," Zoe introduced.

"That's a Piplup," commented Archer, "and that's a Pansage with a haircut."

"Pengullet's a water type. Tanzee's a grass type."

"So are Piplup and Pansage."

Piplup, or Pengullet, returned a happy cheep; apparently it didn't care what its name was one way or another. The Pansage, Tanzee, gave a screech as if offering its own views on Archer. He half-wished he could understand whether what it said was complimentary or disparaging; he had a feeling it was the latter.

Zoe spent time cooking some kind of meat over the open flame, which she had brought along from when they'd left the encampment and called 'broiled Dumud'. Archer wondered what the hell a Dumud was; when the food was done, he hoped the flavor would offer some insight. Instead, it tasted like a strange blend of Slowpoke with Krabby, something he didn't think he'd ever eaten before.

"It's good. Honestly with what little we've got for utensils and to season with...I'm impressed! You're a great cook." He continued eating. "What's a Dumud, anyway?"

"They look kind of like a blob with fins and a wide mouth," replied Zoe. "They live in the swamp mud around here. I don't know what you call them."

That sounded like...a Gulpin. Archer forced himself to swallow, having momentarily lost his appetite, before he forced the image away from his mind and resumed picking at the food. Evidently they weren't poisonous around here, but the thought of the slimy, muddy creatures wasn't palatable in the least.

"We have to make sure we avoid the wild Pals, the closer we get to the town," Zoe told him, "they can get very territorial around these parts."

"Houndoom can take care of them," dismissed Archer without a second thought. "I'm used to coming across wild Pokémon. They're commonplace where I come from."

"The world you came from must be far more dangerous than our island, then."

"Dangerous?" Archer quipped. "Only if you cross the wrong people. ...To tell you the truth there's not much to fear from the wildlife. You should always have an animal of your own before venturing into tall grass; however if it were that big a deal it wouldn't have become a rite of passage to set out travelling and collecting gym badges..." He realized what he was saying must sound unquestionably foreign when he noticed the perplexed yet interested look on her face, and he asked, "Isn't there anything similar here? Any kind of journey people usually go on with their pet upon coming of age?"

She shook her head. "We learn to hunt and forage; however not even the townsfolk go on any sort of journey."

To Archer it seemed like a somber existence. He said nothing as he watched the sparks flicker off the campfire, the flames dancing in the night wind, and allowed his eyes to follow their graceful peaks upward to the sky and the familiarity he thought for sure he'd find there.

The stars were different, unrecognizable. The moon's crescent lay in the opposite direction.

Archer only stared at the sight, and Zoe might have said something to which he didn't answer, because the next he heard was her prompting him, "...Archer?"

"People say Unown have strange abilities..." he said at last, "some that defy current understanding. I think they sent me through some sort of space or time warp or something."

Zoe gazed at him quizzically. "I don't understand."

Archer was briefly quiet. "It means I'm probably never getting back home."

Archer and Zoe passed the night undisturbed at the campsite, though it had been hard for the former to get to sleep. His thoughts were awhirl with concerns about likely having been stranded out in another dimension or time, and he only slept finally when he became exhausted.

They set off again the following morning and reached the settlement by mid-day.

Archer had told himself not to expect anything any more. Certainly his encounters with the island wildlife had taught him that. Still, he found himself surprised just how behind the town was. It was a ramshackle place, with lumber strewn in areas and houses built out of thatched roofing and sheet-metal, and a timidity among the residents easily perceived in the atmosphere. The roads were dirt paths traversed by both animals and humans alike, and there seemed to be no electric lighting; everything was lit with hurricane lamps and gas-lit street lamps, and with even these being sporadic Archer imagined nighttime here would get very dark indeed. It wasn't enough he'd always been partial to large and modern cities; now he'd been fated to a place so backwards it didn't have proper anything.

He did spy a few other townspeople carrying antiquated Poké Balls like Zoe's. Back home practically everyone would have a pet; here it only looked like a handful of tough trainers did.

The more Archer saw, the more unhappy he began to feel. He'd held onto a sliver of hope that maybe, just maybe, there would have been a telephone or communications system somewhere here where he could get word to Giovanni and sort out the whole situation. The lack thereof was a sobering validation to his mind that he'd been flung dimensions away from the time and space where Team Rocket headquarters were. Was he in a future time, or in the past? At this point he wondered if Giovanni had even been born yet.

But Zoe said I was speaking an 'ancient' language, Archer recalled, and then he just felt confused again.

"You'll find more people here who still speak the ancient language. That said, it's not predominant," Zoe said, as if he'd spoken his thoughts aloud. With a glance at Archer, she then asked, "How are you planning to get the island ruler to stop demanding tribute?"

It took Archer a moment before he remembered, Oh, right. She thinks I'm here to shoo away this Marcus guy for them. "Well, first I have to locate him." That much was true regardless of what he intended to do. In reality all he wanted was to get ahold of transportation to the mainland, however the longer he could get these Syndicate shmucks to believe he had their interests in mind, so much the better.

"The PIDF aren't pushovers," Zoe told him. "They're the most well-trained fighters on the island. That's why they've been in power for so long."

When they came in view of the town square, he could see an open-air marketplace lay to one side with people haggling over wares as varied as fruit, fine cloth, and Pokémon, and in the center was a clearing where some people were trying to scrape away blackened marks on the concrete as if there had been a great fire. Houndoom, which Archer had let out of its Poké Ball so it could pad alongside him, was sniffing the air with interest as if it could still smell the remnants of smoke there. Zoe made a beeline for the flea market, and Archer inquired of one of the people trying to clear the cinders:

"Why are there scorch marks on the ground?"

"The Colonel fired the entire commission this morning."

"That doesn't explain the scorch marks on the ground."

He didn't get any reply to this except a suppressed smile and their eyes to avert, as if they thought he was making a joke yet didn't want to be accused of having found it amusing. Houndoom cocked its head to one side, displaying the same dubiousness its trainer felt.

Leaving the people to their work, Archer wandered over to where Zoe was and saw she had purchased some jerky meat, as well as a bag of flour. "Coming into town is the only way to get flour for baking bread without having to harvest the wheat yourself," she explained.

He was less interested in the hassles of day-to-day island life and more on the Pokémon being offered for sale. There were many species he'd seen on the way here, as well as a few other kinds he was familiar with, and even strange ones he'd never seen before. He was debating asking the purchase price and attacks of a particularly powerful-looking stag – the violet deer honestly reminded him of a Legendary Pokémon, yet they were seemingly offering it here like a common breed – when someone called out from behind him and Archer looked up to see another person walking over.

The newcomer was evidently a trainer, judging from the glistening blue capsule hanging from his belt. The man pointed at Houndoom and said something in the island language; when Archer gave Zoe a hopeful glance, she responded for him, and the man accordingly translated what he'd been saying:

"So you're a Pal tamer too, huh? That's kind of a unique Pal you've got there."

"This is my Houndoom," replied Archer.

"I take it you're a rookie then."

"...and what, perchance, makes you say that?"

The man was smug. "Your Pal is puny."

Archer frowned. "My Houndoom is strong enough to beat the best trained animals. We won plenty of battles back on the mainland."

For reasons he could not yet comprehend, Zoe looked awed by his statement. Even the man looked impressed.

"It still couldn't take on the Dancer of the Plains," he asserted.

"...It's a big weasel," Zoe explained to Archer. "It's cute from a distance but it's extremely agile and dangerous. You can recognize it when you see one because you can't tell where its body ends and its tail begins."

"That sounds like a Furret," Archer considered.

"We call it a Chillet," Zoe said.

"Furret aren't dangerous," dismissed Archer. "In fact they're commonplace where I come from."

"I caught the Chillet that made its nest across the bridge. I can guarantee your Pal wouldn't stand a chance against it," the other trainer insisted.

"As much as I'd like to dispute the point with you, I'll only be in town for a while and would rather not waste time comparing the strength of a Houndoom to a common Furret."

Archer and Zoe had started to walk away. But the other trainer, not willing to let it go, shouted after them:

"I challenge you to a battle!"

The words made Archer turn with interest. It had been among the last things he'd imagine to hear in this place. However the idea the island people had Pokémon battles at all provided a coveted sign of normalcy. It had been a while since he'd had a chance to battle for sheer fun of the sport and not in a business-related context.

However, after all he'd observed till now, part of him believed there had to be a catch. "You do mean a match between two trainers, each commanding a Pokémon in a fight?" he said.

"That's exactly what I mean," declared the man, "according to the island customs."

Zoe, inexplicably, was tugging at his sleeve. "Come on, let's go Archer."

The man grinned. "Unless you and your scrawny mutt have the souls of Cattiva."

Archer narrowed his eyes and whispered to Zoe. "What the hell is a Cattiva? It sounds like he's trying to insult us."

She reluctantly explained, "You called it a Clefable when you saw a wild one earlier. On this island they're known for cowardice."

"I accept," Archer snarled at him.

Yet as they strolled to the clearing in the center of town, which was now cleared of the charred blaze-marks, Zoe was still visibly concerned. "Archer, are you sure you've been victorious in many battles?"

"Plenty." A throng of interested people were now forming a wide ring around the intended battlefield to see the fight. It was common practice on the mainland too, but with such a rudimentary civilization here he imagined that watching and betting on Pokémon battles were one of the few entertainments the islanders had. "I really don't see why you're so worried. We'll just have our battle and once we see who's raised the stronger Pokémon we'll both go on our way."

"According to the island customs, a Pal battle is a fight to the death."

Archer spun around right at the same instant the man hurled a Poké Ball to the ground, unleashing his prized Chillet.

The blue ferret stood upright.

It was huge. It towered over Archer, easily ten feet high and growling.

"Fuck," he muttered.

"Get out of there!" cried Zoe.

Chillet pulled back at the same time Archer rolled out of the way, and it fired an ice beam right where he'd been. A cloud of condensation filled the air as the ice froze over the grass spreading outward in a jagged star-shape and the Chillet whirled after him in a snarling vengeance.

Before it could strike again, it yelped and sprang back, twisting on the grass to evade as Houndoom shot a stream of fire at it.

The creature now directed its attention to Houndoom, firing its ice attack at the dog in retaliation. Archer scrambled to his feet.

"Keep it up, Houndoom!" he called. "Inferno!"

Once again, he had to fall back on Team Rocket's militia training. He directed the fight, using Houndoom's attacks to keep Chillet at bay, while keeping watch on the opposing trainer's actions across the way waiting for when he'd make a move. When he pulled out a hidden dagger, Archer was expecting it.

He threw himself to the side as his opponent lunged at him; the two men fought like animals, struggling and punching on the ground. It ended with Archer holding the dagger to the man's throat.

"You're lucky..." said Archer, breathless, "that I see Pokémon battles as a sport. Consider this a favor, because the next time I'll take tanning your hide as the sport."

Without a second remark he tossed the dagger aside onto the ground and got up, yet he'd only gotten a few paces before Zoe shrieked:

"Archer look out!"

He ducked aside right as his opponent, not to be outdone, hurled the dagger at him; Archer quickly snatched the blade from where it embedded in a wood pillar and instantly flung it back. It struck the other man in the chest, and he collapsed dead.

Archer scowled as he turned and walked over to where he'd been heading before having been so uncouthly interrupted. Houndoom had Chillet pinned down with its forepaws.

The Chillet gazed at him with fear. Archer gestured towards the hills.

"Go," he told it.

Houndoom released Chillet, which backed away before turning and running off as fast as it could.

Zoe came over to where Archer was. "You're letting it go?"

"I don't need an overgrown Furret," he answered. "In any case it was only following its trainer's orders."

At least they're partial to Team Rocket's ways: eliminate the trainer, steal the Pokémon. Half of these islanders could be useful minions if their civilization could be modernized, Archer thought as he and Zoe strolled away. Callously indifferent to the deadly duel they'd witnessed, all of the spectators were also returning to their errands as if the battle had merely been a public show. It's pretty lawless around here.

They didn't get very far before being faced with four burly soldiers. They wore helmeted armor with uniforms bearing a starred shield-like insignia, belts holding at least three or four Poké Balls each, and carried machine guns.

"You." One of the soldiers gestured brusquely to Archer and then down the path. "You're under arrest."

"Don't tell me I am in trouble for that fucking fight back there," Archer presumed. "That was self defence if nothing more."

"No one cares about the battle," dismissed the soldier. "You're a new Pal tamer here?"

Without giving him a chance to ask or dispute further, they all aimed their weapons point-blank at him. He lifted his hands in a disarming way; Zoe stepped back with worry across her face.

"You're coming with us," reiterated the soldier, and his tone was so stern and emphatic that Archer figured he'd better.

Chapter 5 - Marcus and Faleris ✅

Archer was escorted to a building on a marble platform overlooking the village square, the most well-kept of all the town's structures. Whereas the townspeople dwelt in huts pieced together by whatever they could find, this was a two-story residence with a concrete façade and the interior of fine wood. Relatively modest if one used the mainland as a reference, when compared to its dilapidated surroundings it was downright elegant. It reminded Archer somewhat of the houses in Lentimas Town of the Unova region, known for their squarish architecture.

Upon entering the building through the double-doors, he was immediately met with a wide office, with an ornate tapestry rug spread across a hardwood floor, and a formal desk as large as the one in Giovanni's own office at Team Rocket headquarters. Directly behind the desk, the wall bore the same insignia emblazoned on the soldiers' uniforms – the jagged shield with the star in the center – and seated here was a man who Archer immediately deduced, upon seeing the soldiers halt at attention and salute, was their commander.

One of the soldiers said something to him in the island language; the colonel retorted with irritation, whereupon the soldiers saluted again and left. He then turned towards Archer, and in perfect command of the mainland tongue, said:

"You must forgive my soldiers, they have a tendency to be suspicious of all newcomers to the town. Especially those who show themselves to be experienced Pal tamers." He extended a hand to Archer, who shook it. "Colonel Marcus Dryden," the commander introduced himself. "I am the head of the PIDF."

"Archer Verdi," reciprocated Archer.

"I haven't heard the surname Verdi around this area. What part of the island do you hail from?" he asked.

"To tell you the truth, Colonel, I'm not even from this island," said Archer. "I'm from the Kanto region."

Marcus regarded him with an inscrutable expression, and Archer added, "I'm trying to find passage back to the mainland. Do you have any boat or aircraft I could charter or buy from you?"

"We have transports, but I'm afraid they're only for PIDF usage and not for charter or sale." Appearing pensive, Marcus then added, "How did you happen to arrive on Palpagos Island?"

"Wild Pals teleported me here." At least he was accustoming himself to the nomenclature, although it still sounded odd to his ear when he said it.

"What about the girl you came to town with?"

"Zoe?"

"I presume you know," Marcus emphasized, "that she's part of a criminal organization on this island."

So am I, elsewhere, but let's see where this goes, Archer thought. "I didn't know anything about that," he replied, each word measured.

He still seemed to evaluate him, but arbitrarily then Marcus gave a small shrug as if he'd decided something and his demeanor remained genial. "If you are new here, might I present my Pal Faleris."

It perched on a gold stand on the side of the office, preening itself with nonchalance. Archer admired the creature. "You must raise it well. I've never seen one with such glossy plumage."

"I must thank you for the compliment, Mr. Verdi. I credit its diet," replied Marcus smoothly.

"Regarding that..." Archer ventured, getting curious, "Zoe claims her group is hunting to feed your Faleris, and if they don't provide enough of a tribute every month or so their village will be destroyed."

Marcus scowled. "I don't know what you've been told by her, but the Rayne Syndicate are a notorious band of poachers. Those brigands have been a thorn in the side of all decent people on this island, slaughtering wild Pals wantonly and stealing livestock from the townspeople. The sooner the Syndicate is wiped out, the better."

Sounds like the kind of thing they say about Team Rocket, and if Zoe's Syndicate is actually a crude version of our own enterprise then even more reason to be on their side, reasoned Archer, but the discrepancy in Marcus' assertions versus Zoe's begot more questions than answers.

"If that's so," asked Archer, "why haven't your men attacked them already? I'm sure your machine guns are stronger than their hunting rifles."

Archer could see Marcus' brow tighten into a frown, but it was brief. "They excel in evasion. Sometimes they move camp."

He strode to his desk and sat down behind it. "Sit down," he told Archer as he motioned to an armchair in front of the desk. Archer sat and glanced briefly at the paperwork there, all of which was written in elegant penmanship with Unown letters. They apparently use Unown hieroglyphs as their form of writing here on the island, Archer observed.

Marcus did not seem to notice his interest in their writing, and went on, "In any event, I can personally tell you my Faleris eats far more gourmet meals than what the Syndicate ever traps." He didn't elaborate. "So I take it your sole interest, Mr. Verdi, is returning to the Kanto region?"

"Yes," Archer replied.

"I'm afraid I can't help you. As leader of this island, I'd be irresponsible if I allowed such a perilous excursion, knowing there is no territory outside of this island and the vast sea," Marcus continued. "You'd do best to forget such nonsense tales of another land."

"Except I came from there," Archer insisted. "I can tell you firsthand the region exists. I was born and lived my whole life off your island till just about two days ago."

"You've been here two days? Have you told anyone else about this Kanto region?"

Archer hesitated. He was starting to get the uneasy feeling this was the prelude to an interrogation of some kind. Marcus drummed his fingers once on the desk, and when it became evident neither man intended to break the silence, Archer relented and went first.

"Does that matter?"

"A curiosity. Nothing more."

As he spoke, Marcus reached into his desk drawer, and suddenly Archer was face-to-face with a revolver.

"One that determines just how fast you'll die."

Tension made Archer grip the armrest of the chair, and he replied, "I have no intent to stir up anything here. All I want is to get off Palpagos Island and go back to the mainland and you'll never see me again."

Marcus gave a cold half-smile. "If I permit you to return, no doubt you'll tell the entire mainland about this island. And that wouldn't be very helpful to me."

Reacting quickly, Archer struck Marcus' hand. The revolver fell to the floor as he swung back at him; Archer stumbled under the force of the blow but succeeded in yanking Marcus' backward with him, and they both collided against the desk.

The struggle scattered documents from the desktop to the floor. Most were technical papers of some kind bearing a modernistic, semi-circled starburst symbol in one corner, which Archer only vaguely noticed in the chaos of the moment. Among them however was a single photograph that made him halt.

It was a black-and-white photograph, yet it clearly displayed a glass pillar within which dozens of unhappy Unowns were crammed.

They were all vowels.

In that instant, Marcus took advantage of the distraction. He snatched the photograph out of Archer's hands, and just as quickly made a gesture to the air.

"Well, Mr. Verdi, now I believe you've seen too much."

Before Archer could realize what the signal meant, Faleris swooped down from its perch with a screech, its talons colliding like daggers with his back and slamming him to the ground. Archer wrested aside as it tried to peck at him, and unable to get loose from where he was pinned to the floor he ended up grappling with the huge falcon. Faleris pulled back, smoke and fire building in its throat.

"No, Faleris!" ordered Marcus, envisioning the small office going up in flames. It was enough for Archer to break free, darting out of the way and escaping outside.

Immediately several PIDF soldiers were upon him; with a calculated punch, Archer hit one of the men in the ribs and snatched away a machine gun, whereupon he fired a line of bullets across the ground at their feet.

Marcus lingered at the entrance, staring at the sight with incredulous fury at how this newcomer had more combat training than his soldiers.

Archer smirked as the group of his enemies now hesitated, having been placed on the defensive. "You're supposed to be the island's most well-trained army...?"

A short distance away, Zoe had been waiting for Archer to return and had let both her pets out of their spheres in the meantime to feed them; she saw when this confrontation occurred, and so did her grass monkey, Tanzee.

Zoe couldn't stop the excited monkey before it leapt with a shriek and grabbed the weapon away from Archer. It was so unexpected that he fell to the ground ungracefully as Tanzee whirled about screeching and firing wantonly. Archer ended up scrambling for cover, and ended up crouched on the ground behind a water trough with Zoe and the frightened Pengullet.

"What the fuck is up with your monkey?" he asked, as they ducked down to avoid gunfire.

"Tanzee likes noisy things," Zoe justified.

"We need to get that gun back before it wastes all the ammunition," Archer scowled.

She peeked out from behind their hiding place. "Tanzee, come back," she ordered, and tried to recall it to its sphere. Tanzee hopped aside quickly, avoiding the recall beam yet still hanging on to the machine gun.

Across the way, Marcus recalled Faleris to its capsule and pulled back as bullets showered across the area. Townspeople screamed and ran for cover, and one of his soldiers gave an outcry as he dropped dead in the hail. Marcus bit back a curse as he glared out at the town square, now a miniature war zone due to the trigger-happy monkey.

Meanwhile Archer cast out Houndoom's Poké Ball, which opened with a flash of white light, and the dog appeared snarling.

"Houndoom, distract Tanzee!" he called.

Houndoom shot a thin ember at Tanzee to get its attention. The monkey screeched a protest, but the natural competitiveness of Pokémon or Pals or whatever they were called rose to the forefront fast and it tossed its deadly toy aside to engage in a battle with Houndoom. As Tanzee shot a barrage of leaves at its opponent, and Houndoom nimbly bounded around to evade them, both Archer and the PIDF soldiers ran out of hiding at the same time.

It was Archer who reached the discarded weapon first. He took the machine gun, aimed at the soldiers and pulled the trigger.

It clicked harmlessly, out of bullets.

"Shit," muttered Archer.

Zoe had now managed to recall Tanzee, as well as Pengullet, and she hurried to Archer's side as he turned, slinging the gun over his shoulder with a strap, and dashed away. "Where are we going?" she cried.

"Away from here!" he shouted back while running.

He then caught a glimpse of a large animal tethered off to the side. When it lifted its majestic head to face them, as if displeased with all the noise, Archer instantly turned and headed directly for it.

"The ice type Rapidash!" Or at least it was the closest thing he could compare the horse to; it had no horn, and ice and frost encrusted around its hooves and mane where a typical Rapidash would have fire.

He didn't notice the wings folded alongside its body.

Archer grabbed Zoe's hand and helped her onto the animal before urging it on with a flick of the reins. With a neigh, the horse whipped around at a signal and galloped off.

When Marcus saw this, he was doubly furious. "Our Frostallion...! After them!" he called.
