Archer glanced back; he could see they had sent out wolves, which were such massive creatures the soldiers were astride them as they aimed their rifles and gave chase down the forest road.

"They're riding...Lycanroc? They're riding giant Lycanroc?" Archer's eyes widened.

"The Direhowl?" Zoe questioned.

"Run faster," he urged the horse. Frostallion, the horse, immediately picked up its pace.

They raced around the winding trail, leaping fallen logs and craggy ditches and bracken of all sorts, till suddenly they came to an abrupt halt before two fierce-looking birds – perhaps half the size of Marcus' Faleris, but still impressive creatures in their own right – fluttering up ahead. They appeared to be protecting their aerie in a tall tree beside the path.

"Pidgeot?" Archer guessed.

"Galeclaw," Zoe replied. The look on her face was enough to tell Archer that coming across them wasn't a good thing.

The Galeclaw screeched and with a slash of their wings, a sharp gust spun at Archer and Zoe like a whirlwind. Frostallion reared on its hind legs and Archer swiftly turned it around to run in the opposite direction.

Emboldened, the Galeclaw swooped down in pursuit; Frostallion narrowly bolted aside to evade their talons. Archer could see the soldiers gaining on them as well, and without a second thought he pulled the reins in the direction of the underbrush.

They were now being chased by both the detachment of PIDF soldiers and the two territorial Galeclaw, both with the same viciousness in mind.

"Why does everything here want to kill us?!" exclaimed Archer.

"That's just how the world is, isn't it?" inquired Zoe.

Archer clenched his teeth. "Screw this damn island—!" He turned yet again to address the running horse. "Go as fast as you can!"

The horse flattened its ears. Archer nearly lost his balance when it suddenly jumped, extending its wings and swooping into the sky with a delighted whinny.

This did nothing to dissuade the Galeclaw, which dove at them in spinning tackles. Frostallion was faster, and flew around the energy flares the birds let loose in their wake. So preoccupied with parrying these attacks, both Archer and Zoe failed to notice one of the soldiers below aiming his rifle at Frostallion and firing.

Frostallion lurched as the gunshot struck one of its wings, and its riders nearly fell out of the saddle as the Pegasus tumbled to the ground, one wing outstretched and stumbling painfully but quickly regaining its footing and returning to a gallop.

They ran on horseback to a cliff peak overlooking the whole island with the mysterious tower in the distance. Miles below Archer could see a river rushing to a waterfall. There's nowhere to go, he realized.

"We're dead," said Archer.

"No, we're prisoners," Zoe replied.

Archer turned first to her, then spun around to look back at the approaching enemies, who had slung their rifles back over their shoulders and were reaching for the shining blue Pal Spheres.

Of course. If the Poké Balls are hand-crafted, there's no safeguard to stop them from catching human beings... Terrible memories of a former captivity raced through his mind again, melding with old feelings of terror till he could almost relive them, and in a split-second decision Archer pulled back on the horse's reins.

"Archer, what are you doing?" asked Zoe, eyes wide.

"Better dead than a slave!" Archer declared, and before she could stop him he gave a cry and urged their mount to jump. Frostallion bolted off the cliff, beating its wings in a futile effort to go airborne; Zoe screamed and hung on for dear life as they hurtled down to crash into the water.

The Direhowl skidded to a halt and even the Galeclaw gave a surprised screech as their prey was lost to the waves.

The current was not as unforgiving as Archer had imagined. They washed up on the opposite shore, soaking wet but very much alive and free.

Archer coughed as he hauled himself onto dry land. Beside him Zoe was helping the horse trot onto the rocks; its injured wing was still outstretched, but Archer could see the wound was just a graze.

He glanced back at the cliff, where the party of PIDF soldiers and their Direhowl were now embroiled in a skirmish with the wild Galeclaw. It seemed they were trying to catch the birds so they could use them to fly down and pursue Archer and Zoe further; the idea evidently did not appeal to the two flying Pokémon.

"We'd better get out of here," said Archer, and leading Frostallion by the reins they retreated quietly into the cover of the forest.

Up on the clifftop, Marcus had arrived riding Faleris. His men gave a salute as he dismounted and strolled to the cliff's edge.

"You say they survived?" he demanded, his eyes searching the woodland.

"Yes Colonel," replied one of the guards.

"Ten-thousand pieces of gold to the man who brings them back, alive," growled Marcus, raising his voice so that all his soldiers could hear. "Faleris likes his meat fresh."

Chapter 6 - Jett's Flowers ✅

Over the next few days, the urban redevelopment project took hold of Lumiose, unveiling Jett's ideas for a modern and thriving city and bringing them into action. They began with a marketing strategy to boost the residents enthusiasm about the project. News broadcasts started announcing the progress of the city's revamping on an almost daily basis; and whenever Jett showed up to see how her workers were laboring, a crowd of onlookers would gather around to gawk at the renovations. Jett saw people's interests were peaking so she started handing out flyers with drawings of what she envisioned the redevelopment would look like. Old buildings got a new coat of paint, broken sidewalks were cemented, and new parks were created with trees being planted abundantly.

Of all these things, the most minor yet the most marvelous were the flowers. She had them planted along the road verges and in the new wild zones to accent the stretches of parkland. The flowers were so exotic, they received compliments by practically everybody who saw them.

She didn't admit where she'd gotten them from; certainly the city council had no need to know of the quiet little island that lay isolated in the middle of the ocean, forgotten by history and all except the few who had some business there. All she said of the flowers' origin was that they were tropical blossoms, and made up some tale of having purchased them in a Hoenn greenhouse where they'd bred a hybrid of bougainvillea and lilies that she'd procured at a discounted price, and everyone concurred that it was one of the best investments of taxpayer finances Quasartico Inc. could have made.

One day, in the midst of Jett overseeing workers plant some of the flowers, Corbeau showed up.

"Well, hello Corbeau," she greeted him.

"Hello Jett," he replied, "I have some news for you. I was able to get the approval for the renovation of Prism Tower. I have no doubt you will repay the favor in time."

"I always have," she concurred.

Corbeau glanced over at the flowerbed. "My, what striking flowers."

"They also have the most delightful perfume..." said Jett with a smile.

"Are they poisonous?"

"What kind of a question is that, are they poisonous?" she said with good-natured humor.

His eyes twinkled slyly. "You know I'm a poison type gym leader. They have a certain look about them; it's hard to explain. Some pots might do well in the gym lobby for show."

Jett could easily imagine him using poisonous flowers for a myriad of other things as well, probably very illegal things, but as she was involved in a series of dubious affairs herself it hardly mattered. "I don't know if they're toxic, however you're welcome to take some if you would like."

"Indeed I will," Corbeau said as he picked up a couple of the potted plants. "Talk to you later," he added as he walked off with the plants.

Actually, keeping one of these for my desk might not be such a bad idea, Jett considered, and decided to take a flower pot back to her office as well. She'd been looking for a suitable workplace plant for a while, and these rare flowers seemed like a perfect accent for the desk.

A day later, Jett went to see if the flowers were taking root and adapting well to their new environment, but what she found was an exasperated gardener shaking his head as he looked at the plants.

"Mr. Seymore, what is the matter?" she asked.

"Mrs. Silph...the flowers are not in the place where we left them! They moved."

Jett scowled. "They couldn't have moved themselves. They're plants."

"Ma'am... I've been doing this type of job for 40 years... The plants are not where we placed them yesterday."

Jett looked around the area where the workers had been planting the flowers, the gardener followed her pointing out the various places where the ground had been moved around during the process. Sure enough, Jett was convinced that the flowering plants were not in their original spots.

The gardener's own Pokémon, Bellsprout and Oddish, were watching the conversation, and now glanced at each other without saying anything. Jett noticed and gave them an askance look. "They're plants," she reiterated, "not plant Pokémon. ...I wonder if your Pokémon saw anything."

"Maybe so," said Seymore, "but they're staying quiet about it."

"Well, they're not totally gone, considering they moved...or were moved...only a few feet, it should be okay. Anything else I should know about them?"

"The fertilizer seems to make them wilt," added Seymore, "It appears that they fare better when allowed to grow wild without aid from man."

"Alright. Keep me informed." Jett turned and left.

The Pokémon Research Lab was a prestigious institute on Lumiose's South Boulevard, a three story converted estate that was almost as iconic a location as Prism Tower.

Jett really didn't expect to be contacted by the institute's top scientists – the acting director Professor Mabel, and the director emeritus Professor Sycamore – since it wasn't as if she had any business with them, but when she heard from the two anyway she was pleasantly surprised by what they had to say.

"Ever since the urban redevelopment project began, we've seen an unusual uptick in the amount of wild Pokémon coming into the city," Mabel told her. "It's almost like they're drawn to something."

"Evidently," said Jett, "they like the new parks and grassy spaces. This is wonderful to hear!"

She certainly thought that way, at least till Quasartico's top construction foreman walked into her office looking in total disarray.

"Johnston what the hell happened to you?" exclaimed Jett.

"I'm turning in my resignation," he announced.

"What?"

"We got attacked by a wild Pidgeot. The whole construction site we had near Jaune Plaza is destroyed."

She was so surprised at this, it left her momentarily speechless. He went on relating what had happened:

"We were at our work when suddenly we all look up and see this giant bird flying straight towards us, shrieking like it wanted to declare war. It knocked out all the Drilbur and Machoke we had working on the site and then turned its wrath on the crane. The entire thing came crashing down on our bulldozers..."

"A Pidgeot," she echoed incredulously.

"But this was one hell of a Pidgeot. It had a longer crest than usual and feathers tipped with blue."

Jett couldn't care less what it looked like; the fact that it was a rampaging Pidgeot at such a high level was enough for her. "Where did it go?"

"No one knows; it just sort of flew off. Once it finished demolishing the entire construction site, of course."

"This is unbelievable," Jett griped, "Incidents like this could turn people against the redevelopment project. It will cause us bad publicity if someone decides that it's dangerous to let high-level wild Pokémon nest within Lumiose."

She wouldn't have initially thought it to be a problem; after all, more wild Pokémon for trainers to catch meant more revenue, and many things could be overlooked for revenue, were it not for the fact that she knew there was a limit to what even the most practical-minded government officials were willing to tolerate.

Jett recalled that off in Kanto, in Cerulean City, the region made an effort to cordon off an outlying cavern where high-level Pokémon could naturally be found. It was considered so dangerous for the average traveller that only trainers who owned extremely strong Pokémon themselves were permitted in. Bribery and blackmail could only do so much if the council thought they could get more votes from appearing to take a stand for public safety.

"You didn't do anything that might've angered this Pidgeot?" Jett pursued. "You didn't destroy its nest or anything like that?"

"We know better than to harm Pokémon eggs," Johnston protested, "As far as we can tell, the attack came out of nowhere. At least five of our people quit on the spot, saying they feared for their lives. It's one thing to see a Hyper Beam from the safety of your seat in a stadium. It's another thing altogether to see that Hyper Beam aimed towards you, and from a wild animal besides."

"Look, Johnston...I understand, really, but you've got to understand my position too," said Jett. "Would you stay on for an increase in salary? This was clearly some sort of a fluke; since when have you known a wild Pokémon to go rogue like that?"

"Well..."

"More practically, it will look strange to people if they see so many on Quasartico's construction crews resigning out of nowhere. I don't want this getting out."

Jett succeeded in convincing the man not to quit, and as soon as he left the office she scowled to herself.

Why couldn't this rogue Pokémon go somewhere else? Or better yet, if it had to go on a rampage in Lumiose City...at least raze the south-eastern side that I can't get the demolition permits for.

Chapter 7 - Team Rocket's Search ✅

During all this time, Giovanni had been trying to find out what had happened to his godson Archer.

When he was told about the Unowns and how they had seemingly teleported Archer away somewhere, Giovanni's first reaction had been an indifferent shrug and orders to keep an eye on the telephones for when his godson invariably called from wherever he was, so that they could send a helicopter to pick him up. Wild Unowns were notorious mischief-makers and he imagined Archer had been sent to one of the adjoining regions, or perhaps deposited in one of the nearby forest routes where he'd have to walk home. It was when afternoon of the next day arrived and there had still been no communication from him that Giovanni started to think something amiss. He called James, Jessie, and Meowth to his office, located on the basement level of the casino he owned in Celadon City.

"I need you to find the Unowns that appeared at the party yesterday and ask them where they sent Archer." As Giovanni spoke, he stroked Persian; the large cream-furred cat lounged on his lap, purring. "We currently know of two locations where wild Unown live: the Ruins of Alph outside of Violet City, and the Tanoby Ruins in the Sevii Island archipelago...Be careful you don't get spirited away yourselves."

"On it, boss," purred Meowth, and with that the trio headed off on their mission.

The first place the trio headed was to Violet City in the Johto region. Johto neighbored Kanto and was but a train trip away; the Ruins of Alph, in turn, was easily accessible from Violet City on foot.

Once the site of an ancient civilization, today the majestic temples and dwellings had become something of a tourist trap. Visitors snapped photographs and milled about gawking at crumbling limestone architecture and reading small plaques that had been set up around every possible landmark and statue, detailing the area's historic significance. To one side was a trailer where archeologists worked out of, trying to piece together the ruins' remaining mysteries; to the other, in a similar trailer under the canopy of a cherry blossom tree, was a gift shop.

While the majority of people visiting the site were tourists, there were also trainers, most of whom were on their badge-collecting journeys, having made a pit-stop here to try their luck catching some of the wild Natu or Smeargle only found in the tall grass behind the temple ruins. They could be seen intermittently, searching through the reeds, sometimes accompanied by a Pokémon either perched on their shoulders or following at their heels.

And then very rarely there were people like the Team Rocket trio.

"You know it woulda been easier if you guys were in civilian clothes instead of your uniforms," Meowth criticized, as James and Jessie peered down from a rocky ledge with their binoculars. "We could've gone down there and mingle with the tour guide group and be welcomed in through the front entrance. Just a couple of tourists and their Meowth."

"Oh come on Meowth, where's your sense of adventure?" replied Jessie, her blue eyes glittering.

"Back at headquarters, where you two's left your brains," hissed Meowth.

"The Unown live in the cordoned-off section of the ruins," James pointed out, "the same part they don't let tourists explore. For all we know they don't even have a way to access it through the main entrance."

"...so if we're sneaking in," added Jessie, "we may as well do it in full Team Rocket flair."

The uniforms worn by all Team Rocket admins were white and bore a bright red letter R, as well as gloves and boots of black patent leather. On their belts they carried their organization's signature armaments of coiled whips and Poké Balls, both of which they could wield with deadly surety if it came to it. It was undeniably flashy attire, however Team Rocket was notorious for spectacle; that much was true.

Meowth still saw little justification for it now. "All these old temples have secret passageways and tunnels that lead everywhere," meowed the cat, "You just gotta poke at the stones in the wall and see which one opens up."

"Okay, the tourists went inside the gift shop. They're distracted...now's our chance," grinned Jessie, lowering her binoculars. With a quick motion to her companions they all leapt down from the ledge and darted across to the buildings on the far side of the site.

These structures looked no less impressive than those the tourists were being shown, but they were surrounded by overgrown grass. They were separated from the rest of the site by a glistening, winding creek, which nature fed via a freshwater spring from nearby Union Cave. A wood sign posted beside the creek read:

DANGER – WILD UNOWN
MANAGEMENT WILL NOT BE HELD LIABLE FOR CONSEQUENCES

"What is that supposed to mean?" asked Meowth skeptically, tipping his head to one side.

Seeing James and Jessie trudge ahead uninterested, he sprang to his paws and chased after them without a second thought. "...hey, guys! Wait for Me-owth!"

It was a simple matter for the trio to get into one of the crumbling temple ruins. They followed a main passageway straight down until they reached a large chamber enclosed by smooth walls inscribed with Unown hieroglyphics. A gash on the ceiling, from which flowering vines were trying to creep, allowed sunlight to filter in and illuminate the otherwise windowless interior.

The trio stepped into the sunlit area and stood in silence for awhile.

"What now?" asked James.

"Maybe if we just hang around a bit..." Jessie replied, "Unowns might sense us and show up."

"That's a big if," Meowth said, not at all convinced.

They waited for about five minutes nonetheless and suddenly a large glittering ball of light appeared before them, it looked like a bubble with something inside. They were Unowns. As they came clearer into view, the bubble light dissipated and the Unowns began squeaking with excitement.

Meowth began translating. "Guys, they recognize the uniforms. They're desperately trying to inform us about something but they're all talking at once!"

"Tell them to take turns talking," Jessie said.

"Yeah Meowth," added James, "We've got time, as long as we get the information that Giovanni wants, and needs."

Meowth spoke to the Unowns and they immediately lined up to take turns speaking, as the cat translated.

"This is their main residence," he began, "The Tanoby Ruins is one of their island retreats."

"One of?" asked James.

"That's where the trouble started," Meowth continued translating, "they were visiting one of their other seasonal escapes and discovered people had taken over the inside of their high-rise."

"It's not unheard of for archeologists and explorers to start charting forgotten ruins and monuments of the sort you letters hang out in," stated Jessie. "Half of the Ruins of Alph are used as a tourist attraction."

"Except the humans here coexist with the Unown," replied Meowth, as the Unown began squeaking a response. "They leave a portion of the site undisturbed to be a habitat for the wild Pokémon. But apparently these humans didn't want to share." Twitching his tail, the cat added, "The Unown say the vowels were all kidnapped by a foul-tempered man with a giant bird."

"You mean 'caught'," specified James.

"They mean kidnapped," Meowth emphasized, with a growl, "after they tried to communicate with the intruders. They say not only was their group ambushed and trapped in an unfair fight by this guy, but they haven't been able to sense where their friends are being held. So they went to get help."

James and Jessie exchanged a glance. When it became clear neither knew quite what to say, Jessie turned back towards Meowth. "Ask them where they sent Archer."

Meowth looked over at the Unown, which squeaked. The cat flattened his ears.

"Well Meowth?" prodded James.

"What did they say?" added Jessie.

Meowth sighed. "You're not gonna like this, guys..."

"Palpagos Island?" Giovanni echoed.

The three Team Rocket agents had gone back to headquarters straightaway after having spoken to the Unown. They met with their boss in his office, where he was seated at his desk with his pet Persian ever-present beside him.

Giovanni listened with inexpressive silence as the trio recounted everything they'd been told, but when they told him the name of where Archer had supposedly been teleported, there was no masking his confusion.

"Do you know the place, boss?" Meowth asked hopefully.

"I've never even heard of it," Giovanni replied, frowning.

"The Unown say it's somewhere in the middle of the ocean, in an area they call the Sea of Wonders, far from most colonized regions," explained Jessie. "But they wouldn't give us specifics."

"They don't seem to understand the concept of map coordinates, unfortunately," James added. "They offered to warp us there, though."

"Which we immediately declined, saying we needed to speak to you first," Jessie finished.

"But why the hell did they take Archer?" asked Giovanni.

"They like him."

Right as Giovanni was shaking his head and about to answer this, there was a flash of light and a small cluster of Unown teleported into the office.

"If it isn't our bevy of clever consonants," Giovanni proclaimed, though he took pains not to annoy them too much. Not even the don of the Team Rocket empire wished to make an enemy of Unowns; the fact someone out there had evidently already done so, and flagrantly, only spoke to that person's lack of intelligence in Giovanni's considered view.

The Unowns began squeaking in unison. Meowth translated, "The Unown all want to apologize because they say in retrospect they weren't very clear on where the island was."

"I'm glad to hear that," Giovanni said, clasping his hands expectantly on the desk in front of him.

"They say it's really easy to find," continued Meowth, as one of the Unown began chirping adamantly. "It's the same place where Temporal Tower stands."

"...and what is Temporal Tower?"

"A big tower they say has stood the test of time."

Giovanni just stared at the Unowns, his expression wholly unreadable. It was his Persian who gave an opinionated meow. The Unown that had been chirping before answered the large cat's comment with a series of squeaks.

"Can't they simply teleport Archer back?" Giovanni spoke again.

Meowth glanced at the Unown, which gave another squeak. "They can't do that," the cat translated.

"Why not?"

"They say he's not where they left him. Maybe someone took him." Meowth turned back to the Unown with a hiss. "...what do ya mean, 'someone took him'? That's the lamest excuse I ever..."

"Meowth..." mollified Jessie, patting the cat on the head in a dissuading way when one of the Unown retorted with an angry chirp. "Maybe we shouldn't be so hasty to accuse these cute little Unown."

"Especially when we haven't made our hotel reservations or bought return-flight tickets yet," James emphasized.

"Ffftt," Meowth replied noncommittally, his ears now lying flat and tail lashing.

Giovanni, meanwhile, rose from his desk and stepped over to a bookshelf on the side of the office, where he retrieved an atlas from the tomes placed there. It was hardbound in brown leather and looked antiquated.

"Many regions were renamed when their leaderships decided to merge into world government," said Giovanni, walking back to his desk. "The Sinnoh region, for instance, used to be called Hisui. It's possible the island the Unown are referring to is known to us in modern time by another name."

He opened the book and began sifting through the maps, the Unown crowding around to look over his shoulder.

After a while, Giovanni spoke. "I've found it on the map...in the southern hemisphere. It has been largely abandoned by our government for many years; I recall them saying it simply dropped off radar many years back. I also recall something else interesting...there is a law that states the regional council can sell land that is languishing from development."

Jessie and James looked at each other and smiled.

"Are you thinking of a new development, boss?" asked James.

"Might be," Giovanni said as he placed the book back on the shelf. "Another interesting thing is that the regional councilman in Kanto is none other than a man who has an uncollected debt with Rocket Enterprises." He sat down at his desk and picked up the phone.

"Time to collect," he said.

Mr. Lear had a not-so-flattering reputation as a chronic partygoer and perpetual snob, but with a fine lineage dating back to the era of Kanto royalty and his abundant social connections, he could afford the risk of squandering his good name for a hedonistic lifestyle – even considering he was the eminent regional councilman for Kanto.

So when Giovanni telephoned him at his office, Lear's usually standoffish manner towards most people was immediately cast aside and he rushed to be as complaisant as he was expected to be towards the don. Team Rocket had maneuvered the election behind-the-scenes to his favor, after all. He owed them.

Giovanni told him he wanted to converse in person so within a half hour, the head of Team Rocket was sitting across a desk speaking with the regional councilman for Kanto.

"How may I be of service, Mr. Delavita?"

"Simple, Mr. Lear." Giovanni began, "We have come to collect the debt you have with us."

Lear felt his throat go dry and sat forward in his chair with his hands clasped together. He cleared his voice and spoke up. "What is your request...sir?"

"It shouldn't be much of a problem for you Lear," the Team Rocket don answered, "As I understand it, you have the authority to sell off regional land that remains undeveloped by our government."

"Well, yes. Yes indeed," Lear sighed and sat back in his chair as he began feeling a bit more at ease.

Giovanni looked him straight in the eyes and replied:

"I want to buy an island."

Chapter 8 - Bamboo Groves ✅

"Just over this hill," Zoe was saying, as she and Archer traipsed through the forest. "My family had a cabin in these parts. No one's lived in it for years, but we'll be able to hide from the searchers till the furor blows over."

The Hoenn region back home was infamous for its long and grueling ocean routes, a bane for trainers who were voyaging without a flying type. Archer decided that if Hoenn had too much water, Palpagos Island had too many cliffs. They had climbed at least five different cliffs, and then an equal amount back down to get to their present location. He was exhausted.

They were on foot again. With Frostallion injured, Archer used the last empty Poké Ball he had with him to capture it so they could carry it instead of the other way round and the creature could rest. He was lucky the islanders' Pal Spheres did not register captures in the same way as mainland Poké Balls, or else he would not have been able to 'recapture' Frostallion so easily.

Weariness with the terrain was yet one more reason Archer felt eager to get back to Team Rocket as soon as he possibly could. Presuming the Unowns were being held somewhere on the island, Archer simply had to find them and free them so they could teleport him back to Giovanni's mansion and he could laugh this whole nightmare off like a fever dream. He only wished it was a dream. Their near-capture and narrow escape from the PIDF army still unnerved Archer, who didn't want to imagine being taken prisoner, let alone captured in a Poké Ball.

He'd already had that experience once, back home on the mainland, at the hands of an enemy of Team Rocket.

The mere idea of it happening again sent shivers though him even now, especially in this no-mans-land where hope of rescue would be slim. Of course the idea of capturing humans in Poké Balls like one did wild Pokémon was uncommon, at least on the mainland; not only was it explicitly outlawed there as a human rights violation, it was prevented by safeguards on all factory-manufactured Poké Balls, so Archer realized he might have been letting his imagination get the better of him back at the cliff.

Nonetheless, he mentioned the possibility to Zoe. Circumspectly, of course, since he didn't exactly want to tell her anything about his life story, but he did want to feel out the likelihood of what might happen here so he knew what to possibly prepare himself for.

"Throw Pal Spheres at us? I don't know about that. We'd certainly have been surrounded and marched back to town," Zoe replied, and then added, "You know catching humans with Pal Spheres is considered inhumane on our island. It's seen as the most humiliating way to be taken prisoner... Then again I wouldn't put it past the PIDF; they're as apt to accuse others for things that they freely do themselves if they claim it's to further the community interest."

"No one risks calling out the double-standards, I guess."

"Dissidents are all either publicly executed or disappear."

Disappearing was exactly what worried him. Uncertainty of fate was worse than certain death.

"When we get to the cabin," Archer commented, hoping to distract himself, "we're going to have to find medicine to heal this horse...you called it a Frostallion?" He realized he hadn't seen anything at the town that looked like a Pokémon Center. "Do you have any kind of a veterinary clinic around here?"

She didn't quite know what he meant, so he explained further, "Somewhere that heals injured animals?"

Zoe shook her head. "If your Pal is hurt, you can find berries and healing herbs in the forest, but other than that you're on your own."

He supposed in that case they let their Pokémon heal whatever mild bruises they got by themselves, like wild ones did when they fought. That's greatly inefficient, Archer thought with disapproval.

"I'm just surprised we have a Frostallion," Zoe said.

"It wasn't that hard to steal."

"No... what I mean is, they're extremely rare Pals. They're what we call a Legendary Pal; they're extremely powerful, and so rare they're practically endangered."

"We call our endangered species Legendary Pokémon too," remarked Archer appreciatively. "It seems that for every difference this island has to where I come from, there's a similarity too."

It was the kind of thing that had been an enigma for Archer till now. But if the Unown were here, and Marcus knew of the mainland regions, then Archer had assurances he hadn't been tossed through some time portal or into a parallel dimension. He was on the same planet and time, he just wasn't familiar with this tropical region. He couldn't understand how an entire island could be hidden from the rest of the world however, and he still couldn't figure out the unfamiliar sky with its strange stars and upside-down moon either.

Archer tried to make memory of anything he might've read at one point or other in a school textbook about why the latter would be. Maybe it was some kind of astronomical mirage...?

Zoe seemed to have something else on her mind though, which she at last voiced straightforwardly. "Now that you see how strong Marcus and his Pal are, are you still going to fight him off for us?"

"We made a business deal, and a deal is a deal," Archer assured her. "I'm not going to go back on my word. Where I come from, I worked as a businessman...of sorts. Our business deals were matters of life and death."

"So you were an assassin."

Damn, she read him so easily. He half-wondered what had given away that his remark was less figurative and more drastically literal. Something in his tone maybe, or the furtive half-smile he'd futilely tried to suppress, or perhaps she was naturally perceptive? "...I was a businessman," he said tersely.

"The way you fought at the town was more like a warrior," Zoe observed, "What was the name of the place you worked?"

"Rocket Enterprises," he replied, "but to our enemies we are known as Team Rocket."

"I thought so," Zoe shrugged, "It sounds sort of like our group...it's okay...it's a way of life."

Archer decided he wasn't going to discuss the intricacies of Team Rocket training or missions with her quite yet.

"I've got my own reasons for going after Marcus," Archer redirected the conversation. "He has those Unowns, and I need the Unowns to teleport me home. And even if I can't find the Unowns for whatever reason, I know his army has transportation at his disposal, because he admitted so; I just have to get ahold of one or the other."

They soon came to a short cliff overlooking an idyllic covert. A spring of fresh water rippled from the rock face into a small pond, around which grew a thicket of tall bamboo amidst mossy grass, and to one side was a small wood cabin with overgrown ivy cascades.

"This part of the island is known as Bamboo Groves," explained Zoe. "That said, only certain secluded areas in these woods have bamboo...this is one of them."

It reminded Archer of Verdanturf Town in the Hoenn region; the grass was as green and the air as fresh and easy to breathe. They walked over to the cabin and went inside.

For somewhere that had not been dwelt in for some time, the interior was surprisingly well-kept and cozy, with windows overlooking the pond, and plush furnishings in excellent condition. To the side was a fireplace, evidently more for cooking than for having to keep warm on a tropical island. There was only one bed in the cabin, but there was a loft too, which was accessed by a small ladder and stocked with extra blankets and pillows, and which Archer immediately offered to take so as to leave Zoe the bed.

If he had to hide out somewhere, this was a comfortable place for it, and they had enough food for a while.

The next couple of days were about as peaceful as they could be.

Here they were seemingly isolated from the rest of the island, safe in their own secluded little oasis, and it was easy to forget they probably had a bounty on their heads elsewhere by now. If he hadn't still had the urgency to return back home, Archer might have even been satisfied there.

Nonetheless, Archer imagined what must be happening back home and what they must think of his having vanished. He'd now been absent for a week or so; Giovanni and the rest of Team Rocket had to be searching for him.

Archer had always been the impatient sort. He was cold enough to analyze things first, but once he decided on a course of action he quickly sprang to fulfill it. Now he was currently in a state of pending, where he knew he wanted to return home yet had no way to do so, and he knew the Unowns were being held somewhere yet had no idea how to figure out where they were. This fact made him antsy.

At least the animals were content. It was tranquil here in Bamboo Groves and the only other wildlife they'd encountered so far acted friendly towards their pets. It struck Archer though that any time they saw him or Zoe, they bolted.

That particular morning he'd been watching a cluster of wild Bellossom – apparently here they were called Bristla? and they had thorns? – happily playing with Houndoom, Pengullet, and Tanzee near the pond. The moment he stepped into view, the little flower-like creatures startled and scattered into the bracken.

"I don't know…" Archer remarked, as he watched one of the Bristla peek out from where it was hiding in the bushes and then duck back down when it saw they were still there, "it seems like every wild animal on this island is either extremely frightened of humans or overly eager to run us off."

"All Pals are like that, unless they have a tamer," Zoe shrugged.

"It's not like that on the mainland." And once again he chided himself for his own stubborn considerations. This was not the mainland; he needed to stop thinking it would be like the mainland. That's why he wanted to get back home.

Frostallion's wing was healing fast. Archer had found some medicinal herbs growing near the cliff, or rather Houndoom had found them after perusing the area and alerted him. By crushing the herbs it was an easy affair to make a salve that could be spread on the injury.

"Pretty soon you'll be able to fly again," Archer told it.

The horse gave a happy neigh.

"Then you can fly me up high so I can see what we've got around these parts," Archer added, thinking aloud. "With a little luck I'll see a boat or something that I can steal and get off this damn island. I'm going to take you with me."

To which Frostallion gave a displeased snort.

Archer considered the Pegasus. He couldn't understand what it was saying, but of all the animals they had, it made one of the most determined attempts to communicate, and he could hazard a guess. "Don't tell me you actually like living on this island?"

Frostallion gave a shake of its head and pawed the ground with a hoof. It nodded its head towards a direction, and Archer followed the gesture to see the faraway mountain peak rising beyond the bamboo trees.

"Is that where you lived?" he asked it.

"It makes sense…" said Zoe pensively. "The mountains rise so high that the top peaks can get snow, so its one of the only places that you can find ice types. There's also a great statue of a Frostallion erected in the depths of the woods. The ancient people credited Frostallions as powerful war-horses that helped them repel threats to our island."

The Pegasus seemed to like the story she was saying and was now strutting around, shaking its ice-encrusted mane impressively.

"So you want to return to living as a wild Pokémon on the mountain," Archer deduced, turning back to Frostallion.

Frostallion whinnied happily.

"Well…too bad," replied Archer flippantly.

To which Frostallion gave him a sideways look that could be described as nothing else but a scowl.

Archer was wholly indifferent. "You don't find an ice type Rapidash every day and I'm not about to let one go just because its homesick."

Zoe pointed out the irony. "You're homesick," she said.

"Maybe, but I'm from Team Rocket and we take our own interests into account," he declared, offering the Pegasus a berry.

Frostallion flattened its ears but accepted the berry regardless.

Just then another berry came careening out of nowhere, flying towards them in mid-air. Frostallion jerked back as Archer ducked, narrowly avoiding getting hit in the head as it hurtled past him.

He turned to see Tanzee laughing. The monkey was hopping up and down like a taunt next to a small pile of berries it had plucked from the bushes.

It seized another berry in its paws and flung it at Archer. This one landed squarely on its intended target, bouncing off Archer's head and rolling onto the grass.

"Damn monkey, creating chaos," Archer snapped.

He grabbed the berry and tried to throw it back at it but Zoe laid a hand on his shoulder and stopped him. "Tanzee's only playing," she excused.

"He's still annoying," replied Archer, shooting a glare at the grass type. Tanzee spread its mouth wide in a mocking grin. "There's enough trouble trying to plan our next move without having to deal with unnecessary joking around."

"All things considered, we've been rather fortunate," Zoe pointed out. "We just have to lay low for a while."

"Maybe," Archer conceded. "But I don't know how long our supplies will hold out. We're out of Poké Balls. Or Pal Spheres, as everyone here calls them."

"That's no trouble at all!" said Zoe, with a cheerful smile, "we can make more."

Archer blinked in surprise. Hand-crafting Poké Balls was a rare skill on the mainland, practised by so few it was something of a lost art. "You know how to make Poké Balls?"

"Yes."

"But how do you find the materials?" he questioned, "They're not that easy to get ahold of."

"Sure they are. They're as abundant as the soil," she laughed in good humor.

Once again, he'd forgotten he was on Palpagos Island – not the Kanto region. Or any other mainland region, come to that.

It turned out Zoe wasn't kidding when she said the materials were abundant as soil. Fragments of paldium, as Archer soon learnt was how the islanders referred to tumblestone, were easily found in the rocks, in the cliffside, and in the very ground. Digging not only provided more glistening tumblestone shards than they could ever need to make a bunch of spheres, it also unearthed shimmering dust that Archer dismissed as fools-gold before realizing with shock it was the veritable thing. The island, it seemed, was rich in natural resources.

"You mean to say," Archer said, as they walked over with a handful of tumblestone pieces to a wood bench beside the cabin, "that the soil has both tumblestone and gold in it?"

"That's just how the ground is," replied Zoe, who didn't see the big deal.

He thought about telling her that was special to the island before deciding it was information he'd best keep to himself till he could tell Giovanni. On the mainland, tumblestone was only found in special deposits, where it had to be mined. Gold was as scarce as...gold. And if he'd had any doubt whether seizing the territory away from Marcus Dryden would be profitable for Team Rocket, no more.

Besides the tumblestone, Zoe had gathered some strips of tree bark and reddish stones. Archer hadn't thought much of the stones before she asked if she could borrow Houndoom for its fire attacks, and then he realized the stones were red because they contained chunks of iron ore.

Smelting the iron was fairly easy with the help of Houndoom, and the amount needed to make a Poké Ball's clasping mechanism was so small it was easy for Zoe to hammer out its shape. The tumblestone was refined and hammered out in the same fashion to form a sphere, and the wood casing was layered atop it.

Archer watched her work with silent fascination, listening to all her explanations of the technique with genuine interest, and only speaking unprompted once. "How did you learn this?"

"The skill of crafting Pal Spheres has been passed down through generations in my family. Just like the task of guarding the tower," Zoe told him, and admitted, "I don't know how we came by the knowledge."

"So it's not something typical on the island?"

"Oh, it's not typical at all. Marcus knows too, but it's not something everyone on the island knows how to do. I don't know how he ever makes so many for his entire army, let alone to sell to the townspeople."

The completed Pal Spheres glistened beautifully, in the same remarkable way as all the antique-style Poké Balls he'd seen so far. They'd made about ten of them, enough in case of a drawn-out battle with a hard-to-capture beast.

Zoe handed Archer the spheres, and he took them gingerly; he was fully aware these had no safety fail-safe to prevent a person being taken by one, and the idea made him as observant handling the little capsules as when maneuvering a loaded gun.

"It's common practice in Team Rocket to always carry spare Poké Balls," Archer explained, "just in case a rare wild Pokémon appears that might be useful to the organization."

Even as he said this, he was starting to scheme, as any self-respecting member of Team Rocket would. He glanced up from the Pal Spheres to watch Frostallion drinking water at the pond.

Frostallion was, in Archer's eyes, not only rare but useful, and valuable – at the moment certainly, but it could no doubt be sold at a high price when he got home – and that would certainly be the case for all the creatures on this island, wouldn't it? Those shiny white Eevee for starters, and the short-eared Clefable, not to mention all the other regional forms with their different typing. He could imagine people in Kanto and Johto paying hefty sums for the rare Pokémon he'd seen here that, to the islanders, were commonplace Pals.

"Why don't we go out hunting later this afternoon?"

"For food?"

He shook his head, a glint of mischief in his eyes. "To catch some Pals."

Chapter 9 - Supply Drop ✅

Archer was annoyed.

For all the strange animals he'd seen from the time he'd first arrived on Palpagos Island, this afternoon they'd found not a single one. It was like they knew he was coming to catch them and they all hid. At least they saw none of Marcus' soldiers, either, so they were presently able to explore the entire area surrounding Bamboo Groves without fear of getting shot at.

When they didn't find anything on the meadow, they followed a grassy trail through the forest to see if any wildlife would show up there. Pengullet hopped along with them, keeping close to its tamer Zoe.

Eventually, Archer noticed something sifting through the thistles up ahead and he and Zoe hid behind a large boulder to observe.

It was a squirrel. Archer would have called it a Pachirisu, yet it had the light-green fur coloring of a Leafeon and a red gem on its forehead like that of a Persian.

He pointed at the animal. "What's that?"

"A Lifmunk," answered Zoe. "It's a grass type."

"Good. Houndoom's got the type advantage," Archer decided, and opened Houndoom's Poké Ball with the press of a button. The dog emerged beside him in a flare of light.

"Start off with Faint Attack," he ordered, "Draw it into a battle."

Houndoom sprang forward to tackle the Lifmunk. The squirrel lifted its head at the sound of the grass rustling under Houndoom's paws, and with a startled jump successfully dodged the attack. Houndoom turned about to try again, but instead of fighting, Lifmunk ran to flee.

"Don't let it get away," Archer called, and Houndoom opened its jaws and sent out a stream of fire towards the squirrel.

Lifmunk was surprisingly evasive, and bounded aside onto a rock before darting sideways, yet not once did Archer succeed in goading the squirrel to fight back. They ended up pursuing the small creature down the grassy path. It was about to outpace them and escape when Archer decided enough was enough of the foot chase and he hurled one of the Pal Spheres at it.

The capsule struck Lifmunk from behind, and pulled the little animal in with a flash of light. It fell to the grass and began shaking.

Never before did Archer fully appreciate the convenient simplicity of a modern Poké Ball's red indicator light. Here he had to go by the luminescence of the blue tumblestone casing. It alternated between its typical glow to being bright as a flame. He watched it intently and, right when he was sure Lifmunk had been caught, the sphere burst apart in two halves.

Lifmunk sprang out of captivity and, without a moment of hesitation, scurried away from Archer and Zoe into the bushes.

Archer grimaced as he watched the leaves settle where Lifmunk had vanished. My plan to impress Giovanni with a collection of rare island Pokémon doesn't seem to be panning out today...

"Lifmunk are hard to catch if they don't want a tamer," said Zoe, breaking into his thoughts. "The good thing is that they're fairly common Pals. We'll probably find more if we keep looking."

Her optimism was encouraging, even though he knew the afternoon would soon be growing late. As they continued on their way, Zoe inquired, "Archer, how did you train Houndoom to obey exact commands?"

"What do you mean?" asked Archer, perplexed.

"You call out attacks."

Archer recalled the fight back at the town, with the trainer and the Chillet, and how his opponent simply threw out the Pal Sphere and let Chillet choose what attacks to use. He hadn't thought much of it at the time, but now he deduced it must be the standard way of fighting on the island.

"Pokémon can fight by themselves, yet they fight better if they have a human to guide them," Archer explained. "At least that's what they always say back on the mainland. It's seen as a partnership for a reason."

Houndoom gave a happy bark; the dog was wagging its tail. Archer patted it on the head and added, "I've had Houndoom since he was a puppy. He was my starter Pokémon...a gift from my godfather, Giovanni. I'd like to think our training has helped him grow into a much stronger Pokémon than otherwise."

She seemed wistful. He cleared his throat and the air of deep recollection left her as he went on, "Anyway, humans know type matchups and strategy. We can also help Pokémon increase their attack power through more ways than one. You can certainly win in combat by letting them fight on their own, but it's supposed to be harder..." Archer hesitated here for a moment. "Why don't I teach you the mainland way of battling later?"

"...is it that easy?" Zoe remarked with surprise. "The truth is I rarely battle with my Pals anyway, except for self-protection."

"Yes, I know, it's seen like a duel to the death here or something like that. But what about battling for fun?"

"I've never heard of battling for fun," she said pensively, "though sometimes Pals run off by themselves and get into trouble. Especially Tanzee. It's just how Pals are; they're fighty. I guess Pokémon are the same?"

Pengullet was cheeping and bouncing up and down cheerfully. Zoe glanced down at the penguin and smiled. "Well, in any case Pengullet does seem to like the idea! I might take you up on that, then."

They recalled their pets and wandered back to the cabin, taking a scenic stroll by the coastline. It was a gorgeous day. Sun streamed through the trees, washing the sand in warm light and outlining the ocean horizon in a myriad of colors; waves rolled peacefully onto the shore, carrying with them the salty scent of the surf. Once or twice a Mantine – here known as a Celaray – could be observed to leap out from the sea at a distance. The creature caught the air under its fins, in a way Archer had never seen ray-fish do back home, and was able to glide on the wind for a short distance before splashing back into the water.

The beach on Palpagos Island was one of the most beautiful Archer had ever visited, and this was considering his past travels to many other known tropical regions. Every time they walked by the seashore, however, something never failed to catch his eye.

All along the beach there were fairly large rocks made of pure, shimmering tumblestone, carved into rough pyramids and placed in a line, at perfect margins of approximately four feet from each other and one foot from the water at high-tide, as if meant to mark where the sea began. At first Archer had not paid attention and discounted it as a curiosity of the terrain; however the more time he spent on the island, the more he started to notice how this was the case anywhere the land met the ocean, and the boulders were too precisely placed to have been naturally occurring. They had to have been put there by man. So today, when they stopped underneath some of the palm trees for a brief rest, he made a comment about them to Zoe.

She was ambivalent. "They're just there, I guess."

"Like the tower?" Archer prompted. "Someone had to have put them there."

"No one remembers," Zoe conceded.

"Aren't you the least bit curious who or why?"

"Whoever did it, it's lost to history by now."

If so, that's a loss, Archer reflected. The stones did look rather weathered from time, evidently having stood as sentinels here for many long years. Even though they all shared the same pyramid shape, some of them had blunt peaks because of the elements' erosion. Nevertheless, they were still tumblestone, and such massive boulders of the same mineral used in Poké Balls and all technology that manipulated properties of physics must surely contain high, latent energy within them. They must have had a reason for putting these here, and not just for looks. I suppose it's one of the island's mysteries.

Irrelevantly perhaps, Archer remembered the strange graffiti he'd seen scrawled on the side of the tower when he had first arrived to the island.

"Did the Syndicate write that saying on the side of the tower?" he asked. "The tower is the key, the trees hold the truth."

"No," she replied, with interest, "I didn't even know someone had painted something there."

"That's too bad," Archer said. "I was kind of hoping you would know what it meant." Though, he had to admit to himself, she and the rest of the people here seemed to know very little about the island they lived on; it perhaps was folly to assume she would know anything about even this.

Zoe frowned. "I'm just angry someone defaced our tower."

"But it sounds like it might mean something. You don't know what the tower is for, after all."

"I just know we have to protect it. Though I do think it's too bad we have no way inside," she said. "If we could get in, I think it would be easier to defend it."

"You can't get in?"

"The door is locked."

"Haven't you tried to break in?"

"It's the sacred tower." She looked affronted that he'd even considered it.

"The letter I on the top is glowing. How can it be glowing if there's no electric power going to it?" Archer pointed out. "If there's electric power going to the tower, then someone has to have access."

Zoe's eyes flew open wide. "Do you mean someone might be sneaking into our tower?"

He didn't answer, now searching the landscape with a focus on the trees. There was certainly some mystery to the island's tower, but it was only one half of the enigma. The tower is the key...the trees hold the truth...

He started with the palm fronds overhead, but when nothing there seemed out of the ordinary he continued to examine the other trees along the coast. His eyes drifted up to the forested cliffs bordering the beach, and then he froze.

The trees there were also in a perfect line, as if aligned with the boulders, and at the very top of each of the trees – only partially hidden by the upper branches – was what looked undeniably like cell tower antennas.

He motioned towards them. "What are those?"

Zoe looked completely indifferent. "Tree tops."

"Those aren't tree tops. They don't look like any other trees here," Archer pointed out.

"All the trees that grow along the edge of the cliffs look like that. ...Archer, where are you going?" she asked as he got up from where he had been sitting.

"I'm going to see what's up there."

They got up from where they were seated under the palms and ascended the cliff. Once they were at the top, he picked out one of the trees that had plenty of branches to get a foothold; then he started to climb.

Zoe lingered below, looking up. "Be careful you don't fall," she called to him.

"I won't fall," he replied, all attention on the mysterious contrivance at the topmost branches.

The closer he got, the more he could see they were antennas. Half of their faces were positioned towards the seashore, as if aimed at the stones, while the others were pointed inland. They looked either brand new or well-maintained, yet right when he was about to reach them they seemed to ripple as if behind a curtain of invisible energy and faded, as if all this time they had been a mirage.

Archer held back a curse. "The damn thing vanished right in front of me."

"I still see it from here," said Zoe.

The harsh sound of propellers cut through the air. He lifted his gaze to the sky right as an airplane flew directly overhead. It headed all the way to a midpoint between where they were and the distant tower; out from the hold came a large parcel of some kind, which plummeted to the ground. The airplane circled around once and receded into the clouds.

Archer frowned and made a mental note to investigate that next. But first he wanted to finish investigating whether the antenna was indeed still atop the tree.

He did little more than reach out to where it had been visible that a sudden jolt of lightning pierced his hand; electricity burned outwards and he lost his balance with a gasp and fell to the ground.

Zoe was immediately at his side. "Archer…! Are you all right?"

He sat up groaning and looked up at the tree top, where the antenna was once again visible.

"Did you see the airplane that flew by?" he asked her.

"Yes."

"It dropped something that way." He pulled himself to his feet, trying to shake away the disorientation from the shock. "Let's go see what it is."

Archer took the lead, hurrying his pace through tangles of bracken and ivy, as he and Zoe went to see what in the world that airplane had dumped on the ground. He hadn't voiced his suspicions, but he had a hunch about what it could be, and if he was right then it would help them enormously.

"Propeller airplanes come by pretty frequently, and they typically drop something," Zoe explained as they walked. "Everyone knows it's the PIDF, because only the island rulership is permitted to have airplanes. We've always presumed they're conducting training exercises."

"I call bullshit on that," declared Archer, "My guess is those airplanes depart from some mainland region and come here to make a delivery."

They came to a large clearing where a huge chest of some kind had struck the ground. There was no one in sight.

"I guess no one has arrived yet," Archer observed.

Archer quickly dashed out to the chest. A worried Zoe lingered behind in the bushes, keeping lookout.

It was a massive trunk with an elaborate numerical lock, one which upon further examination Archer didn't think there was enough time to pick. He retrieved and opened Houndoom's Poké Ball, sending out the canine.

"Houndoom," he addressed his Pokémon, "see if you can get this damn thing open."

Houndoom gave a rough bark in reply and complied, tacking the container headlong. Despite impressive looks, the locking mechanism snapped apart easily and Archer was able to open the lid.

Within the chest, Archer discovered a treasure trove of unusual items. What struck his attention first were several packages of ammunition, stacked one atop the other in the corner. Best of all, it's the ammunition used by the machine gun we've stolen, Archer realized, and immediately set to pocketing them. Jackpot!

The next thing that caught his eye were many small metal barrels, easily half the size of a can of soda, ringed with glowing tumblestone; he realized they were using the tumblestone as in a Poké Ball to shrink their size, so they would likely have been much, much larger and heavier had it not been for that. They looked like tiny oil barrels, and as he examined them he discovered that yes, they did in fact contain crude oil.

What the fuck do you need so much crude oil for? he thought, deciding to pocket them too for the hell of it.

The last things they had here were basic medicinal spray-potions, of the type commonly used on the mainland, and blueprints of some kind. Just the idea of having proper medicine for their pets was a boon, and he took them all; as for the blueprints he felt he didn't have enough time to figure out what they were for, so he figured he'd better take them as well.

That left the big chest empty, and as Archer stood up he could hear leaves rustling and people talking in the island language as a group approached the clearing. With a sly smile, he and Houndoom darted back into the bracken where Zoe was waiting for him.

"What did you find?" she asked with curiosity, but he motioned for her to stay silent and hidden.

Only a instant later soldiers wearing PIDF uniforms arrived. The moment they saw the chest open they ran to it and, seeing their bounty pilfered, readied their guns and set off to search for the thief, one of them shouting out angry orders to the rest.

Archer snickered to see the turmoil he'd instigated. "Come on, let's go."

As they fled through the forest, placing distance between themselves and the raided chest – even though the soldiers had no idea where to look for the culprit – Archer was laughing. He and Zoe headed off happily on their way back to the cabin, and as they did he told her about all the items being sent in the supply drop that were now in their possession.

"Crude oil?" Zoe had the same reaction. "Why do they need crude oil?"

"No idea."

"Why do we need crude oil?"

"Even less idea. But if they want it so bad then we may as well have it on our side. You said you've seen propeller airplanes drop parcels often?"

"At least once a week," she affirmed.

"Good. If we keep track of their supply shipments, we ought to have enough potions and ammo to survive comfortably and eventually launch an all-out attack on that asshole Marcus' stronghold so I can steal a boat."

"I thought you were also going to drive him off? Not just steal a boat?" Zoe prodded.

"If we kill him, that's just as good," Archer replied.

That logic seemed to satisfy her, and as Archer and Zoe turned a corner they could see some of the soldiers had looped around and were searching up ahead. A couple of them had sent out their Direhowl, which were now sniffing the air trying to get a scent.

Archer scowled. "Shit, they move fast don't they? Thank God we're downwind from them."

"This way," said Zoe, motioning away from the wolves and their tamers.

She led Archer towards a steep embankment and started climbing, with him following suit and his Houndoom clambering behind as well. They reached a cliff that connected with another one and they kept going. After several minutes of climbing, Archer was getting fed up and called Houndoom back into its Poké Ball so his dog could rest.

Eventually they arrived at a strange site that bore a sign that read 'No Trespassing' in Unown letters, with the PIDF insignia right below. It looked decrepit and about to fall apart.

"How far did we walk?" muttered Archer, gasping to reclaim his breath.

"I think we're at the base of the Astral Mountains," considered Zoe. "You know if they catch us here, we'll disappear."

"We'll disappear wherever they catch us," Archer dismissed, and pressed onward ahead of her. "Why don't they want people up here?"

"They say the ground is radioactive. No one really knows though...rumor has it the ancient people had a small settlement up on the mountain but it was destroyed by alien Pals from the sky."

Archer half-smiled disbelievingly at the idea; it sounded like something straight out of a science fiction film.

Cold wind carried itself down from the mountain peak, a sharp weather difference from the pure tropics of the lowlands. The foliage, in turn, gradually intermingled the trees with temperate pines as the ground began to slope upward. They eventually began to follow a stream upriver, all the way to a waterfall that gurgled down the rocks, and when they climbed this they encountered such an unexpected sight both Archer and Zoe halted in their tracks.

It was an abandoned city of some kind. Tall buildings, overgrown with ivy and moss, stood at attention alongside wide streets as monuments to a forgotten civilization. Antiquated traffic lights lay in disarray across grey cobblestone and at short distances on either side were the remnants of tethering-posts, calling to mind once-bustling thoroughfares traversed both by early automobiles and large Pokémon. It looked like a manmade waterway had, at one point in time, also meandered through the city beside pedestrian paths, but now the water was still and a thin layer of algae had taken form, while the sidewalks were interspersed with overtaking grass and cracking from disuse.

Animals still lived here evidently; every so often they spied a wayward Lifmunk or a bovine Mozzarina roaming around the landscape. Strange but beautiful flowers bloomed sparingly through cracks in the stone, their gentle fragrance carrying on the wind.

The flowers were so unique that Archer nearly stopped in his tracks to examine them. He came very close to picking one to get a closer look, yet Zoe stopped him. "Don't touch the plants."

"Why?"

"...I don't know. That type of flower is considered sacred, for some reason. I've never seen it in person."

Archer gave it a skeptical look but decided to let the flowers be.

As they walked around the site, staring incredulously at these remnants of a lost period in the island's history, Archer began to think about Zoe's earlier comment regarding rumors of alien Pals and the decimation of settlements. Eternatus, an alien Pokémon that nearly destroyed the entire Galar region, came fleetingly to mind. Yet Archer didn't think this was the case here.

In the first place this wasn't a 'small' settlement by any means; it was a large city that once upon a time might have rivalled Goldenrod or Saffron on the mainland. In the second, this city wasn't decimated; in fact it was too preserved, too unspoiled, for a catastrophe of that magnitude to have befallen here. There most certainly had been some kind of a war, as evidenced by fallen debris and possible shrapnel, but it appeared the invaders had quickly won – perhaps by the city's surrender. The rest of the damage looked as if it was nature's fault, as if both vanquished and victors had inexplicably departed the city soon thereafter and left it to be reclaimed by the elements.

Of course, like so many things on this island, the only people who would've known for sure are long dead and gone, Archer lamented silently as he and Zoe stopped at what once must have been a vibrant city plaza. But I can't help but think these alien stories were conjured up to keep the islanders from learning some secret.

Zoe was still gazing at the buildings, aghast. "I've never seen such a huge place. It's like every building is as tall as our tower. How many people must have lived here...?"

"The buildings are so high it's hard to see just how big the place is," said Archer, "or for that matter how far we've walked from the cabin. Hold on...I've got an idea."

He retrieved Frostallion's Poké Ball and opened it with the press of a button. The Pegasus appeared beside him and gave a neigh.

"Is your wing still hurting you?" Archer asked it, and Frostallion extended the wing for him to see. The graze was steadily getting better, but now they had a much faster way to treat it.

He took out one of the potions he had stolen from the supply drop and sprayed a couple of spritzes on Frostallion's wing. Immediately, the injury faded away before their eyes. Archer was used to seeing this kind of rapid recovery, however Zoe was not, and she gave a surprised gasp.

"The wound is totally healed!" she exclaimed. "It's like it was never injured."

"Chalk one up for modern civilization," Archer replied. "These are the same kinds of Full Restores they sell back home."

"You mean they've got medicine that can heal in the blink of an eye?" Zoe marvelled. "I can't believe they've been keeping it for themselves all this time."

"Funny how a vantage point makes such a difference," considered Archer, regarding the little spray bottle wryly. "On the mainland, tumblestone is scarce and potions can be bought for two dollars at the corner mart. Here precious minerals are everywhere and good medicine is a thing of fantasy." He then turned and addressed Frostallion. "How's your wing feeling now?"

The horse gave a happy neigh and flapped its wings.

"I need you to fly us up high so we can see where we are," Archer added, and he and Zoe got on the Pegasus' back and the horse stretched its wings and flew up.

They rose to the top of one of the tallest buildings there, and as Frostallion landed lightly on the rooftop, its hooves clattering on the smooth ground, Archer noticed that a large Unown letter H was painted in the center of the wide space. They were on an old helicopter landing.

That discovery, however, wasn't nearly as stunning as when they proceeded to dismount Frostallion and get a good look around at the view.

They stared in awe, mystified by the sight. There was the Syndicate's tower in the far distance, and from the very top radiated a glowing energy that rippled across the entire island, pulled towards the antennas on the trees before being sent, like a relay, down to the pyramidal rocks at the edge of the island on the seashore, and then outwards to the ocean. Far into the water, the energy flashed upwards like a translucent red curtain and dissipated into the sky.

"What the hell are we looking at?" Zoe asked.

"I'm not sure," replied Archer, "but I'm going to find out."

Chapter 10 - Tocotoco Raid ✅

On their way back to the cabin, Archer and Zoe talked. They discussed the energy field they had seen spreading outwards from the tower and questioned what it could be for; they also talked about Archer's original plan of stealing a boat.

"So, are you going after a boat or checking on this antenna? ...I won't even ask you at this point about fighting Marcus because it looks like there's a lot of new stuff turning up," Zoe said.

"First thing should be looking into this antenna atop the tower and what it does," Archer replied.

Investigating the antenna was less a matter of getting off the island and more of curiosity, and maybe even a bit of spite. No one kept a Team Rocket agent stranded and incommunicado on an island in the middle of nowhere. Since these people were making it difficult for him, he might as well stir up some trouble here and show them what the world's most glorious crime organization was capable of – even if right now it was just him. Oh, if I only had an entire squadron of our agents here, Archer imagined, I'd really give these fools a run for their money.

When they arrived at the cabin, Archer immediately spread the bounty taken from the supply drop on the table and went to load their gun with the ammunition. "It's always safer to be ready," Archer explained.

Zoe went outside to let all the animals out of their spheres, swiftly returning to Archer's side as he finished reloading the weapon. They then began looking over the rest of the items together. "It really is a lot," she remarked.

"Whomever's making these supply drops has to be from the mainland," Archer reasoned. "That means someone out there knows about this island."

He hadn't had a good chance to look over the stolen blueprints till now. They were schematics, seemingly outlining some kind of weaponry, but they were far too technical for him to understand. No doubt Team Rocket's scientists back home could interpret it.

Giovanni would be doubly impressed if he could see all this, he thought, only to get annoyed once again at being unable to get word to Team Rocket headquarters.

In the corner of each of the documents was a peculiar logo, which Archer thought looked incredibly familiar yet could not place at a glance. It was a horizontal semicircle with a star piercing its center, flaring outwards in either direction like the hands of a clock marking five minutes to the hour of five.

Damn, I know I've seen it somewhere, thought Archer, considering the insignia carefully; it was like a word held on the tip of one's tongue. Maybe it'll come to me eventually.

What completely stymied him however was whatever purpose the crude oil might serve.

"Zoe," asked Archer, "have you ever seen any kind of reverse shipments going out? If Marcus is getting all this stuff from someone on one of the mainland regions, then that person has to be getting something in return."

Zoe thought about his question for a long moment. "I'm not sure," she said at last, "I know we used to see airplanes taking off near the town, at least once a month, but that stopped quite a while ago. We weren't sure where they were going…again, we imagined it was just routine training or patrols of the island."

"I wish you knew more about the tower."

"So do I."

Somehow he hadn't expected that kind of sentiment from Zoe, or even that level of candor. He had taken her and the rest of the Syndicate as indifferent to their surroundings, so long as nothing overtly imperiled them or the tower they seemed to revere.

"The thing is, I feel I ought to remember…like there's something my people forgot somehow that would answer everything. Just because I don't know what's going on about the tower, or other things, doesn't mean I don't want to know," Zoe added. "On the contrary; I feel if I'm from the island, how can I not have answers to the questions you ask that seem so simple? But I'm starting to remember some things."

"Like what?" Archer asked.

"I once had a Pal…Grizzbolt…who was my close partner, like you and Houndoom."

"What happened?"

"I don't know. One day Grizzbolt vanished. I don't remember why or how…I just remember missing her a lot. I still do." Zoe glanced up at him and continued, "It was around the same time Tanzee appeared near our camp."

Before he could respond, they suddenly heard the guttural cry of some kind of animal off in the distance. Archer didn't recognize it, but pallor immediately came over Zoe's face. "Tocotoco."

"Toco-what?" Archer echoed.

"Tocotoco raid anywhere they think has food and leave the place obliterated." She turned towards him fearfully. "We need to get out of here. Now."

"That's nonsense. Can't we fight them off?" he questioned.

"Fight off Tocotoco? They're worse than a rampaging Mammorest," Zoe dissuaded.

Despite Zoe's concerns, Archer wandered outside the cabin with Houndoom loyally at his side. Pengullet and Tanzee were already standing at alert here, visibly eager for combat. The ominous cry sounded again in closer proximity and Archer turned his attention towards it, up to the slope beyond the bamboo leaves.

As he watched, a small creature appeared on the rise of the hill; first one, then a few dozen. They were short, squat dodo-like birds, with the green plumage of Xatu and the blank looks of Psyduck.

Archer took one look at the flock and burst out laughing.

"The way you said we were going to get raided I was expecting the cavalry, not the dodo brigade."

Zoe, standing at the cabin door, was serious. "They explode."

"They... explode?"

With a singular squawk of war, the Voltorb-birds raced down the hill much faster than Archer thought their chubby legs could have carried them.

They were making directly for the cabin.

Archer recognized the glow on their feathers as the precursor to the Selfdestruct attack. The air ignited around some of them in a fiery explosion, and the birds – knocked out by their own power – collapsed sideways onto the grass with exhaustion.

Pengullet blasted the invaders with an aimed torrent of water, which only succeeded in getting one of the Tocotoco to race up to it vengefully; its explosive attack flung the little penguin backwards. Tanzee, which had begun jeering at them, only narrowly saved itself by swinging up into the heights of one of the nearby bamboo stalks. Frostallion, evidently not in the mood for combat against exploding birds, simply fluttered into the air so as to get away from the problem.

"Everyone, get in the spheres!" Zoe cried, recalling both her Pals in a swift motion, although Pengullet looked like it wanted to keep fighting and Tanzee looked like it wanted to keep screeching insults from the safety of its new perch.

Houndoom meanwhile dashed from one side of the grassy clearing to the other on Archer's frantic directive, trying to halt the intruders with its fire attacks before they got any closer. Several particularly determined Tocotoco got past, and hurled themselves with a vengeance at the wood structure of the cabin. Archer grabbed Zoe's hand and pulled her away from the doorway, before the blast destroyed the wall surrounding it.

They watched from a safe distance as the place that had provided them shelter now burned. The remaining birds, seemingly satisfied with the chaos they had inflicted, dispersed.

Archer and Zoe spent the night in the only place that had not been affected by the explosion, which was the back end of the structure. The next morning they assessed the damage and decided that reconstruction was possible but it would be more efficient to use rocks instead of wood to rebuild.

Construction proceeded slowly, perhaps on account of how heavy the rocks were, but there was no denying how the losing battle against "those damned dodo birds," as Archer called them, had done a number on their little party's general enthusiasm.

They hadn't destroyed the entire cabin, but they had damaged a large section of the right half of the building, leaving the inside open to the elements. The turn of events had entirely derailed their earlier plans to go out and check on the tower's antenna, at least for the moment. However, with the effort it took to rebuild, something else important went overlooked; the Tocotoco had succeeded in running off with most of their provisions, and Zoe eventually pointed it out.

"We're running short on food. We still have a few berries, but we can't survive forever on that. And your dog will need meat too."

"You're right," Archer conceded. "Seeing there's no way of getting anything from the village, I suppose I'll have to go out hunting."

"I can go; that way you can finish up the base," she offered. "...besides, you can probably carry these heavy rocks better than I can."

"If you're sure..."

Archer's voice was drowned out by rapid gunfire and infernal screeching. He looked over to see Tanzee gripping a machine gun in its paws and firing it at the trees with wild glee.

Archer remained skeptical. "I'm sorry....why did we give the monkey our gun, again?"

"So it can protect our base," replied Zoe.

"I wouldn't trust that monkey to protect shit. Look, take Houndoom with you. At least you'll have some kind of protection."

It was late afternoon when Zoe returned, Houndoom trotting alongside her; she was carrying an armful of shiny blue capsules. "We've got dinner! ...and enough here for half the week besides."

Archer couldn't believe it. "You caught them...in Poké Balls?"

"Pal Spheres. Yes. How else?"

"If you're going to eat them you don't catch them in Poké Balls, damn it. No wonder the island animals don't trust humans...they have no way to know if they're destined to be pets or on the menu."

"Well, how do you get meat in your world?"

"We raise livestock on farms, like civilized people. Otherwise if you're out in the jungle you set traps."

"Spheres are traps," said Zoe blankly.

Archer sighed, pressing his hand to his eyes like if he was trying to fend off a bad headache. "Let me see what you caught."

She tossed the Pal Spheres happily and a flock of three or four small, white-plumed chickens emerged.

"They're..." Archer glanced tentatively at her, knowing by now they were probably called a different name than the species he'd been about to say.

"Chikipi," Zoe replied promptly.
