One of the chickens hopped over to Archer, looked up at him, and leant against his leg in a hug.

Archer glanced from the Chikipi back to Zoe. "We're not eating them. We now have an egg farm."

"...and you say you worked as an assassin?"

"I was a businessman."

"Right..."

"Later we'll go out to the forest again and I'll show you a better way to hunt food."

Archer did not disappoint, and not long afterwards he set out with supplies, Zoe following curiously to see what kind of trap he'd devise. He didn't go very far from the cabin, and the bamboo thicket with the pond was still in view when he stopped and began construction by the edge of the forest.

"Two of my old colleagues preferred pitfall traps," he recounted to her, trying to hide his wistfulness, "but I've always found they can be fickle when it comes to weight. The way this one works is...anything that crosses over here will get ensnared, causing the stone to drop and yanking it up by a leg."

"What are you planning to trap?" she asked him.

"I saw a wild hog near the tree-line yesterday. It looked like a Piloswine but leaner."

"A Rushoar?"

"Sure, why not. The point is I want bacon."

With the trap set, they strolled back to the cabin. The day had felt long and it vaguely surprised Archer that only now was the sun beginning to set. He could see some of the wildlife settling beneath trees and in nests to sleep for the night, while nocturnal species were beginning to emerge for their shadowy prowls. Were it not for the hardships of such an isolated life, the inability to contact headquarters, and maybe the people out to kill them, Archer imagined this island would be a veritable paradise.

The sun was bright this afternoon and Jett was in her office reviewing business papers regarding recently acquired properties that were to be developed under her orders. The telephone rang at that moment.

"Marcus? I'm surprised to hear from you. It must be midnight on your part of the globe," Jett remarked, with a glance first at her watch and then at the clock on the wall.

"I wanted to make sure I'd get you on the phone," said Marcus, "I need a copy of the schematics to be sent."

"You haven't received the shipment?"

"It was stolen from us."

"Stolen? How could anyone there steal it from your people?" Doubt filtered through her voice.

"There's an outsider who landed here. He's dumb enough to think he can cause trouble."

"An...outsider? Who, some castaway?"

He dismissed her worries without hesitation. "It's nothing to be concerned with."

"So long as it's not someone who can find his way back to whatever region he came from," she said.

"Not at all. You know I have my place isolated. He's as good as dead."

Jett narrowed her eyes thoughtfully. She wasn't sure if to fully believe Marcus about this, but he did sound certain of himself, so she didn't pursue the issue further.

"I'll see what I can arrange," she replied simply, "I'll call you once I have the second drop scheduled."

Jett hung up the telephone, and went on to make the necessary arrangements, but thought little more of it afterwards. She was turning back to her regular office work when Johnston, the construction crew foreman, walked in.

"Mrs. Silph," he announced, "There's been another wild Pokémon attack."

She stared at him incredulously. "Not again?"

"This one was an Altaria, but I'd never seen one so angry! It fluffed out its feathers to twice its size. The damned bird used a Twister attack that was so powerful it tore off half the new awning we'd installed on the shopping center we'd just about finished building."

"I imagine it put the progress on that construction back considerably," concluded Jett.

Johnston's grim features affirmed her suspicions. "A combined effort of our own Pokémon chased it off, but just barely," he continued, "No one outside of Quasartico employees has seen these rogue Pokémon, yet. But if this keeps happening someone in the public will."

Jett inwardly cringed. "That's what I'm afraid of. People will certainly make an issue out of it."

As Johnston left, Jett leant back in her chair pensively. Here I was hoping the situation with the rogue wild Pokémon wouldn't be repeated. I need to figure out what to do about this.

Chapter 11 - Ensnared ✅

The day dawned sunny in Lumiose City. Jett was in her office early as she did often and her dog Pokémon Furfrou was with her. She had placed a food dish for her pet on the floor next to her desk and the poodle was happily eating its breakfast, while Jett looked over some business papers.

The dog finished eating quickly. "All done Furfrou?" she asked.

Furfrou barked affirmation and wagged its tail.

She picked up the dish and placing it on her desk, remarked, "You have some leftovers; perhaps I should get you a flavor you like better." She recalled the Pokémon back into its Poké Ball, right as her intercom beeped and she pressed the button on the small console to answer it.

"Yes?" she said.

"Mrs. Silph, there is a gentleman here in the reception area...Mr. Corbeau...he requests a word with you and he says it is important."

"I will be right out," she replied.

Jett placed the papers she was reviewing into a small pile and placed them at the center of her desk. She briefly looked at the window and saw that sunshine was beginning to peek in, and at this point she looked at the plant that was on her desk.

Maybe I should put it near the window, so it gets some sun, she thought. She shook her head.

"No," she said aloud to herself, "I have no time for this now; Corbeau is waiting."

She left the office and found Corbeau sitting near the reception desk. He stood up when she entered the room.

"It's quite early Corbeau, is something the matter?"

"I've brought you the documentation regarding the acquisition of the buildings around Prism Tower. It's imperative that you sign it so that it can be notarized...that paves the way for you to take control of all of the surrounding area quickly and do what you will with it."

"That's excellent news!" she exclaimed, "That takes care of the entire center of Lumiose at once!"

A notary from an adjacent office was called in, and after Jett had signed the documents, it was official. Jett now was free to do as she pleased with both Prism Tower and the adjacent structures.

"This is a splendid turn of events, Corbeau!" she said happily, "We must celebrate! Perhaps a group dinner, a select group of your people and a few of my employees... I will pay the costs."

"Great idea Jett," he answered, "except it will have to wait, as I have plans for today. Nevertheless...remember you owe me two favors now."

She smiled, and he walked away, waving as he stepped out the office doorway.

Jett went back into her office with a spring in her step, but as soon as she sat down at her desk she noticed that some of the tendrils of the flower had entwined around the dish. The blossom had closed.

She took the dish away quizzically, and stared at the flower for a while. The leftovers on the dish were gone.

She shook her head and decided to just plow ahead with her work, so she picked up the potted plant and put it near the sunny window and didn't pay much attention to the plant for the rest of the day. By the late afternoon, she decided it had been a busy day and as she gathered her things to go home, she glanced at the plant and was stunned at what she saw.

The plant had grown another six inches in the time she had placed it in sunshine. Approximately an inch, an hour. That's impossible. she thought. But yet, there it was, undeniably larger than before.

"I'll just have it repotted," she mumbled to herself, "Tomorrow I'll talk to Seymore."

She picked up her things and shutting the office lights walked out closing the door behind her. The plant's flower opened and stretched its stalk so that it stood up straight.

Early at dawn, Archer and Zoe set off for the island tower astride Frostallion. The Pegasus galloped a short distance from the cabin before it took wing, soaring above the trees with its two riders.

This was the first time Archer had really gotten a chance to enjoy flying over the island. The landscape was beautifully pristine, with sprawling, palm-scattered beaches and unspoiled woodland that rivalled known regions' most splendid forest routes. As they neared the tower, they could see the small plume of smoke from the Syndicate's village campfire, and off in the distance was the town where they'd met Marcus Dryden.

Guiding Frostallion, Archer flew all the way to the top of the tower and circled the building. The strange energy field shooting upwards was invisible at this proximity, but the antenna was there – pointing up to the sky, itself radiating with an orange glow apparently impossible to hide.

Just then, he heard a small bleating sound and turned his attention to the small figure near the edge of the rooftop.

It was a bipedal Wooloo. Or rather, as Archer had found out they were called on the island, a Lamball. The little rotund sheep, objectively cute and innocuous-looking, was incongruently stationed next to a massive gatling gun.

"Shit!" Archer exclaimed, pulling back on the reins just as the Lamball struck the trigger with its hooves and fired at them.

Suddenly they were amidst a cyclone of bullets; Frostallion plunged down evasively and they dove below the gunfire. Its hooves clattered on the ground as they landed safely in front of the tower's locked door.

Archer glanced up as the gunfire ceased. "Zoe, if we had any question left, I think it's safe to say someone is inside that tower. That damned sheep wouldn't put itself up there, let alone with a war weapon."

They heard shouts and turned to see people from the Syndicate encampment come running. Zoe hopped down from Frostallion to meet them.

They spoke in the island language, which to Archer remained melodious but incomprehensible. Eventually Zoe turned towards Archer.

"They say we should avoid disturbing the tower lest we get cursed."

"Bullshit," Archer snapped. "Tell them that's a lot of stupid superstition."

Zoe started to turn but then hesitated and glanced back at him. "…I don't know if they'd take that the wrong way."

"Tell them there's a trigger-happy Wooloo on the roof."

She turned back to the group, speaking quickly. The response she got back from them was lacklustre, but they dispersed without much further discussion.

Archer and Zoe returned to the cabin feeling no less closer to any progress. The trap they had set for the wild Rushoar still hadn't caught anything, either.

"I guess we can't do anything for the moment," Archer said sourly, trudging ahead to the cabin.

Zoe, seeing his disappointment, held him back. "It'll work out. In any event, the day's still young… Weren't you going to teach me how the mainland people battle with their Pals?" she reminded him.

Archer – after considering the matter – figured some lighthearted Pokémon training might very well do him good. At least it was a way to get his mind off problems that had no solution.

They decided to use the grassy clearing outside of the cabin as their battlefield. Houndoom would face Pengullet in their first training session, while Frostallion lingered on the sidelines curiously. Tanzee was uninterested, preferring to go off gathering berries from some of the bushes outlying the cabin.

"So every Pokémon knows four attacks," Archer began. "The trick to battling the mainland way is to pick attacks that take advantage of your opponent's type weakness…or, barring this, to increase your own strengths and evasion."

"I think Pengullet only knows three skills," Zoe said, glancing at the little penguin.

"What are they?"

"Aqua Gun, Iceberg, and Bubble Blast."

"For the sake of this training, and if Pengullet agrees, we'll use the names those attacks are called on the mainland… Water Gun, Ice Beam, and Bubble Beam."

"How come?"

"Well, this is the mainland battling style. You may as well call out attacks by their mainland names. For that matter, Pengullet is a Piplup."

"I think Pengullet is a Pengullet."

"You know what? Piplup, Pengullet, it's all the same. As far as fighting technique goes, it's the sort of thing you can see better in practice." He motioned to the battlefield before them, ceding the starting play to her. "You have the first move."

Pengullet readied itself for the directive. It was visibly eager for the battle; the little creature usually fought so assuredly by itself, but now it was trying its best to follow Zoe's commands.

"Aqua Gun!" Zoe said.

"Houndoom, to the right; counter with Faint Attack," Archer called.

Pengullet aimed its attack, and Houndoom leapt aside towards the right, avoiding the stream of water that hit the ground where it had been standing. The dog then rushed forward, catching Pengullet off-guard in a tackle and sending the penguin tumbling headlong backwards.

"In a battle of this sort," Archer explained, "you not just have to account for your own offensive, but what your opponent might use as their counter-strategy." He turned back to his Pokémon.

"Faint Attack again. Try to pin Pengullet down."

The dog shifted its weight before the leap, and that was when Zoe saw a chance.

"Now…Aqua Gun! Direct at Houndoom!" she ordered.

The water attack struck Houndoom headlong in mid-pounce and the dog crashed to the ground, allowing Pengullet to bounce aside. Houndoom shook its soaking fur off.

"Like that?" Zoe tipped her head.

"Not bad," Archer complimented. "See, it's not too difficult."

The sound of rustling leaves and an unfamiliar man's voice drew everyone to attention.

"Hello! I'm selling wares! Perhaps you'd like to look at some of the merchandise I bring?"

The man had very pale green hair, upon which rested a tricorn hat with a single feather. He wore an ornately embroidered green overcoat with tall boots, and carried a large knapsack topped by a rolled-up sleeping bag, making him look like a unique cross between an adventuring trainer and a historical re-enactor trying to emulate the pirate days. Notably however, he did not have any Pal Spheres with him, so it ruled out at least one of the two.

Archer was leery, and as soon as the visitor wasn't paying attention, he whispered to Zoe, "I don't trust this guy."

"Wandering merchants are typical on the island," Zoe told him. "There are so many people who live far from town, travelling salesmen are often the only way for them to get supplies."

"As long as he really is a salesman...let's say he is...he might tell other people where we are," insisted Archer.

"I don't think it's a danger," Zoe insisted.

Archer glanced over at the wandering merchant, who was lingering around the pond interacting with their curious pets. Maybe he did just want to sell items and go on his way. There was no faulting a man who just wanted to make an honest living. But Archer, who did not make an honest living by any semblance of the saying, had a natural wariness that was difficult to put aside.

Houndoom, in any event, seemed to share his uncertainties. The dog distanced himself from the other animals, watching the newcomer with thinly veiled distrust. When the man walked closer, the Pokémon growled at him.

"Look," Archer pointed out to Zoe, "Even Houndoom distrusts him."

Houndoom's growls went disregarded. Tanzee had apparently returned from its berry-picking and was now scampering around the man, while the happy-go-lucky Pengullet looked open to make a new friend, and Frostallion was indifferent but otherwise willing to tolerate anyone interested in admiring its majesty. The merchant turned away from the animals as Zoe wandered nearer.

"Take a look, Miss" the salesman said to Zoe, "perhaps there is something that attracts your attention; we can bargain with the price." He smiled at her and immediately Archer felt irritation rise up inside. Why the smile? He's definitely up to no good.

Zoe perused his assortment of items; meanwhile Archer watched skeptically from afar, fully expecting enemies to descend on them at any moment. To his relief, he found everything remained as quiet and unassuming as ever.

She ended up buying some spices, and as the salesman went on his way, they returned to their battle training with little comment.

"Pengullet has to know a fourth attack," Archer considered, "it's probably something so basic that it's hard to notice. Does he ever have any unusual action, or any kind of sound or leer that seems to affect other Pokémon strangely?"

"He likes to launch himself off high places."

"Come again?"

"Local myths say Pengullet once knew how to fly, but they lost the ability, and ever since then they yearn to be airborne," she recounted seriously.

Archer stared at her, then stared at the penguin flapping its wings with a determined look on its face, and then turned back towards Zoe with boredom. "Okay, so Pengullet has three attacks…"

They heard a crashing noise somewhere in the bracken behind them, and Archer turned on his heel immediately. "We couldn't have possibly caught dinner that fast…?"

Zoe, along with their pets Pengullet and Houndoom, followed him to where they'd set the trap and lo and behold, they found not something but someone ensnared in the rope.

It was the wandering merchant.

His ankle had gotten entangled and he was suspended upside down, trying desperately to get free. Scattered on the ground were his hat and some other possessions he'd been carrying. The instant he saw Archer and Zoe standing there, desperation morphed into something bordering on embarrassment.

"Hello again…I'm sorry to mess up your trap like this. I didn't see it there."

If you had, I would wonder why you stepped in it, Archer thought with disdain.

"If you could cut me down, I'd be grateful."

Archer was about to do just that when Houndoom's rough bark drew his attention away. The Pokémon was pawing at a piece of tawny paper in the ground, one of the dropped items, and when Archer picked it up with curiosity the merchant's amiable demeanor instantly grew serious.

It was a wanted poster with an artist's rendering depicting both Archer and Zoe, calling for their capture and promising a reward of gold. Vindicated in his earlier suspicions, Archer turned back towards the merchant now fidgeting in the trap.

"I'm sure gratitude comes cheap. So which is it then…are you a wandering merchant or a bounty hunter?" confronted Archer.

"Try both," he retorted.

"Marcus must be getting desperate if he's willing to recruit mercenaries to hunt us down."

"Look, I'm way more involved with them than some average fortune-seeker," the man declared.

"You think your claim can buy you leverage? I doubt it can buy you time," Archer replied with indifference.

"I know where the colonel has the Unowns."

That was the fastest way to snap Archer to attention. He focused on him with interest, and the man smiled in a complacent show of importance.

"I'll tell you everything provided you let me down from here."

"Bold of you to presume you're in any position to make deals," responded Archer. "…but I'm willing to compromise."

At a motion from Archer, Houndoom aimed a stream of fire below the trap. It flared into a bonfire.

The smugness on the man's face quickly vanished. "Hey, what do you think you're doing?"

"Here's my deal," Archer spoke, his voice pleasant. "You tell me where the Unowns are, and I don't let you burn alive."

"If you let me roast here, you'll never find out what I know."

"Then if you really do know something, you'd better talk fast," replied Archer menacingly.

He kept shifting his attention from Archer to Zoe and to the hungry fire below. The rising smoke made him cough.

"He's got them in the Pal Essence Condenser," the man relented. "It draws energy from whatever Pals are locked inside. Alas, the Pals inside are incinerated in the process."

"They're going to incinerate them?" Zoe exclaimed. "The Unown did nothing to harm anyone!"

Archer was also outraged, for a slightly different reason. "That fucking asshole, those critters are supposed to be my ticket home!"

"Marcus considers their loss a noble sacrifice towards a lofty goal," their captive now sneered, rubbing it in. "He thinks he can power up some sort of an ultimate weapon that way. Besides, he didn't like that they came here and started talking with the islanders, writing messages about an outside world...that's why he specifically captured the vowels, so they wouldn't be able to form words."

The flames rose a little higher, and he began wriggling nervously. He glanced hopefully towards Archer, who far from displaying any sympathy was beginning to look irritated.

"You say he's got them in this Pal Condenser whatchamacallit," Archer said. "You still haven't told me where that is."

"It's in the tower."

"Congratulations – that's a big help. There's no way in the damn tower."

"I have a key!" he cried, and without waiting to be asked he tossed Archer a gold key from the inside of his coat.

On a motion from Zoe, Pengullet doused the fire. Archer studied the key; it was a large, antiquated style that certainly looked like it could fit the lock of the tower's main door. Yet he still didn't trust it; the whole thing appeared incredibly easy.

"How do we know it's not a trap?" he asked, glancing up to their captive.

"I want to live," said the man simply. "Please let me down from here."

At a nod from Archer, Zoe turned to Tanzee, which released a flurry of sharp leaves that sliced through the rope. Once freed from the trap, however, the man found himself placed at gunpoint.

"Walk," Archer ordered tersely, as he motioned with the gun.

His prisoner stepped ahead of him obediently, but he asked, "Where are we going?"

Archer was brutally honest. "I can't let you leave."

In a swift action, the man swung about. His fist collided with Archer's chin, and he would have knocked the gun out of his hands had Archer not held tightly. He struggled with Archer to steal the gun to no avail and in the midst of the fight crashed backwards into the fenced-off area where their little flock of chickens were pecking at the ground.

Without warning, the Chikipi squawked and rushed at the unknown man. Several of them pulled back as if charging energy, and before Archer had quite realized what they were doing there was a brilliant flash of harsh light and terrible, earsplitting screeches as multiple attacks were fired at once. When Archer opened his eyes his enemy was gone and there were only ashes remaining.

He stood and looked over at the Chikipi, which were now hopping around with indifference. A few of them were preening their feathers, looking completely innocuous.

"When was someone going to tell me the chickens could learn Hyper Beam…?" Archer asked.

There was something to be said even here on this island, it seemed, for those who treated supposedly inadequate creatures well; it reminded Archer of the fish Pokémon Magikarp, one of the weakest species back home, which with diligent training could evolve into a powerful Gyarados. He glanced at the spot where his opponent had been engulfed by the energy attack.

"Too bad we don't have a rose around here."

"A rose?"

"It's kind of a tradition."

Zoe thought for a moment and stepped away. She returned some moments later with a hibiscus she had plucked from a nearby bush. "Will this work?"

Archer looked at the tropical flower, shrugged his shoulders and took the flower without a word, tossing it to the cinders.

Chapter 12 - Fight for the Tower ✅

The strange tower with its imposing Unown letter I loomed before them, as ominous as it was impressive. Even more so, now that Archer knew what he sought was in there.

From the bracken where they hid, they could see some lights were on inside the building, something which Archer took note of.

"Zoe, to get inside this tower we've got to steer clear of whomever is in there." Archer was clutching the machine gun as he pointed to a side of the tower, "You see the lights in the window over there?"

"I see it."

"I should go myself," Archer decided, "It's safer if one of us stays out here as a look-out."

"No way; this tower is a mystery that my people have wondered about for a long time. I'm going too."

"Are you sure you're not better off staying out here? If they catch us sneaking in, we'll both be in dire straits," Archer answered.

"It's my tower," Zoe replied, taking the key from him. "I'm coming."

Archer gave a brisk nod and turned to Frostallion. "All right, you keep watch out here for when we emerge," he instructed it. "We'll whistle for you to come by."

As the Pegasus cantered off, Zoe questioned, "I don't understand why we'd bring a Pal along only to leave it outside."

"Just in case we get caught, there's at least one of our Pokémon free," explained Archer.

There he was going once again, envisioning the worst-case scenario just on the basis of his own traumas. I'm not going to get trapped and taken prisoner. That'd be as implausible as lightning striking the same spot twice, Archer silently assured himself, trying to push the persistent fear aside as he opened another Poké Ball and sent out Houndoom.

"Come on," he motioned to Zoe, and she followed him and Houndoom directly up to the tower.

Zoe easily unlocked the main door and pushed it open tentatively. It moved on its hinges with ease. "I sort of expected it to be jammed from disuse," she murmured to Archer with astonishment.

"More evidence someone's been using your tower behind your backs," Archer whispered in reply.

The inside of the tower was dimly lit and sparse. As their eyes adjusted to the gloom, they saw a wide area reminiscent of the lobby of an office building, with an old reception desk across as well as an elevator and a stairwell to the side, all made of ebony stone and wrought iron and, despite evident age, in excellent condition and fully functional. The wall behind the desk bore the enigmatic letter I insignia, glowing as brilliantly as the larger one on the façade outside.

They stepped in gingerly so as to not let their footsteps sound on the tile floor. Archer had fully expected to find guards stationed directly inside the entrance, but to his surprise there were none; everything here was completely still.

"Let's go up the stairs," Archer said grabbing Zoe by the arm, "We still don't know if there is anyone in this building right now and they could be monitoring the elevator."

Zoe did not argue the point. They climbed many steps up, searching for entry onto any of the upper floors, till they reached one that was unlocked.

Not far from the stairwell, they encountered a door with the gilded initials 'A.R.' marked across it.

They went in and found an office that looked as if it was stuck in a time warp. An old fashioned desk and armchair were situated near a window shuttered with blinds, while a bookcase with various books had been placed against the wall to the right, and a dead potted plant stood in forlorn vigil off to the side. There was dust all over the floor and it was evident no one had been in there for many years.

Countless papers were strewn all over the floor and on top of the desk. While Archer looked at the titles of the books on the shelves, Zoe scrutinized the documents that lay on the desk. "Look at this," she suddenly said.

Archer glanced at her. "They look like deeds to land and real estate."

Zoe meanwhile had taken an envelope in her hands and opened it, taking pains not to tear the letter inside as she pulled it out. The parchment was very old and yellowed, and upon it was handwritten in Unown lettering:

'To Whom It May Concern,

I was and am the owner of the Island Power and Mining Syndicate, which entered into a business partnership with the Silph Company of Kanto in the spring of last year.

I feel partly responsible for what has occurred to our region. My business with Silph Co. was in the Poké Ball industry. Silph sent apricorn hulls to serve as Poké Ball casings. We handled the mining of tumblestone and the manual labor required to manufacture the spheres according to Silph's specifications. Silph in turn, handled marketing and sale of the finished product across the mainland. We have always split the profits.

Mr. Silph has wanted for many months to buy out our interests in the land here, but I have refused to sell. The amount he offered for the property was not a fair exchange. Since tumblestone is far more abundant on the island than it is on the mainland, he wanted to appropriate the land and take the entire profit of Poké Ball sales for himself.

The island has been under a period of political unrest since the establishment of the planetary council. Leading the call for separation was Mr. Dryden, who claimed he could better manage the region under his rule.

Unable to convince us to sell, Silph financed a coup d'état and gave Dryden's army all the backing they needed to take over the island. In return for his assistance, Silph Co. receives tumblestone from the territory they seize at no cost. We have tried to appeal to the planetary council, but they do not wish to expend resources to save such a small region.

Our world was destroyed in the short time Dryden has been in power. They have appropriated all commercial ventures and private property, outlawed the Pokémon League competition to prevent any excuse for unnecessary travel, and forbidden access to the outside world. They have shut electric power to settlements across the entire island and I doubt they will return it any time soon. Those who try to oppose the new regime are publicly executed or taken into servitude, never to be seen again. It is also forbidden to speak of the regions beyond the sea.

My associates have all fled by now. My cousin is handling our properties in Kalos. He and many others have urged me to escape into exile, but I refuse to leave the island, or everything it means to us. Those closest to me feel the same. If opposing the dictatorship as an absolution means death then we will meet that fate here, fighting to retake our stolen property, starting with our business headquarters – the iconic tower that bears our company logo still.

Until that day, the entire syndicate will remain here protecting the tower, as well as the Pokémon by our side – our beloved pals.

…Mr. Alexander Rayne.'

Zoe stared at the letter mutely for a long moment.

Archer looked over her shoulder, read it quickly and commented, "That's an interesting story and would actually explain a lot of things. Isn't Rayne your last name also?"

Zoe remained silent and Archer noticed it. "Zoe. Is something wrong?"

"That name. Alexander Rayne. I remember my father telling me one day that his grandfather's name was Alexander Rayne. This man was my great-grandfather."

"So, then Marcus is descended from the guy who took over this island and established a dictatorship," reasoned Archer, "Somehow it's all starting to make sense."

Loud steps made Archer jerk his head upward, and he pulled Zoe to the floor. They ducked behind the desk right as two or three PIDF soldiers walked by, and remained hidden till the patrol receded into the shadows. Zoe was still clutching the letter, and when the guards had gone she folded it and stuffed it into her jacket pocket.

"Come on," said Archer with insistence, "Let's see what else there is in this place."

They proceeded down the hall, keeping their pace quick but soundless. Soon they came to another room; whereas all the offices they'd passed previously had been in disarray and abandoned, this one – despite being presently unmanned – was seemingly in current use. It looked like a makeshift cross between a laboratory and a security office, with the prestige of both and the certainty of neither. Bright electric lights illuminated the entire area from above, and several monitors on the wall displayed advanced charts and numerical figures Archer wasn't quite sure how to read, but they appeared to be measuring energy levels.

He immediately focused his attention on something else: the glass chamber he had first seen in the photograph in Marcus' office, within which were the trapped vowel Unowns.

A couple of the little animals squeaked at him from their prison, which was such a tight fit for them they barely had space to move. It was a tall glass chamber, in front of which was a panel with an analog meter of some kind and several buttons, one of which was a large black one, as well as an indicator light that shone a mild blue.

Archer hurried to the contrivance, scowling at all the buttons. I'm not going to risk pressing one of these and accidentally activating the device and incinerating them, he thought, wincing at the mere idea.

He tried striking at the glass with the stock of the gun, but when it didn't open he turned towards his Pokémon.

"Blast it with fire," he told Houndoom, jerking his head towards the glass.

Houndoom gave an acknowledging bark and unleashed a torrent of flame that lashed against the container. The glass did not appear to react in any way.

Archer frowned. "Why doesn't it work...?" He then noticed the tumblestone edge of the top and bottom of the container. "It must be using the same kind of energy barrier as a Poké Ball," he realized, "No wonder the Unowns can't teleport out and free themselves."

One of the Unown gave another sad squeak.

"Don't worry, I'm getting you out of there," he assured them.

"Look what I found over on the table," he heard Zoe remark from behind him.

Archer was tugging at the device in an attempt to force it open with brute strength when Zoe came over with a little booklet in hand. She pointed adamantly at the pages, and when he glanced over he saw a sketched diagram of the Condenser with several bulleted lines written in Unown lettering.

"I can't believe they actually wrote an instruction booklet for this shit." Without wasting any more time, he pressed a sequence of buttons on the panel; the glass door flung open, and then all the Unowns floated out en masse.

"All right guys, you're free. Thank God," added Archer, relieved, "now I can get off this fucking island."

The Unowns happily squeaked in a grateful chorus. They twirled about him in a circle, and in a brilliant flash of light...the little creatures teleported away, leaving an astonished Archer standing right where he was next to Zoe.

"What? ...No! Come back! You forgot to take me with you!" Archer exclaimed in dismay.

No sooner had he spoken, footsteps began hurrying down the hall towards them. Fuck.

"Someone's coming!" whispered Zoe. Archer had already spun around searching for an alternate way out. He spied his Houndoom pawing at a semi-concealed doorway beside the monitors, and without thinking twice he pulled Zoe aside and they hurried through it.

They emerged to a wide area, with a high ceiling held up by columns, and smooth stone flooring. A circular marking had long ago been etched in glowing light on the ground, as if this place had once been a particularly elegant Pokémon battlefield perhaps reserved for special event matches. On the farthest side of the stadium was a raised accent wall bearing the iconic letter I logo, and directly below this Archer caught a glimpse of motion.

It was Marcus, accompanied by an entourage of at least ten PIDF infantrymen.

"How did you get in here?" His voice thundered in the openness of the space.

"Through the front door," replied Archer, unfazed.

"So you think you're smart? If you take this for a joke, I'm not laughing," said Marcus, walking forward. "First escaping town with Frostallion...then running away with our supply drop...now getting into the tower... I've grossly underestimated you, Mr. Verdi."

"The one who doesn't belong in this place is you," Zoe spoke in a challenge, "This is the Syndicate's tower; it belongs to me."

"Yes, the tower was yours," Marcus answered her, "Just like Grizzbolt."

Her eyes widened at the name of her lost pet. But Marcus wasn't done, and he twisted the knife:

"...was, till I used it as fodder in the Pal Condenser."

"You killed her?"

"It's more accurate to say... distilled down to its essence."

Zoe took a step forward but Archer held her back. He could see the soldiers standing behind Marcus at the ready, guns trailed, waiting for an order to shoot. Marcus surprisingly lifted a hand, causing them to stand at ease.

"Of course you don't even remember when my men lured your Grizzbolt off the campsite and took it," Marcus went on. "We've been very diligent in drugging the grain we provide your Syndicate in return for the wild Pals you catch and supply us. I get Pals without having to expend resources on hunting, you get accused of poaching the wildlife, and I'm seen as the benevolent ruler protecting honest islanders from the barbarians outside the town gates. It's a grand scheme."

"Then all those Pals we hunted..." Zoe's voice trailed.

"...went into the Condenser, as power-ups," Marcus answered her unspoken question, "except for those strong enough to be useful elsewhere. My Faleris doesn't eat Pal meat, you see. Not while we have dissidents to serve as its main course."

He'd produced a sphere from his coat, and threw it up into the air. Faleris appeared in a flash, and Marcus jumped onto the hawk's back, a look of sheer delight and cruelty as he gazed down at Archer and Zoe.

"Faleris – get your dinner."

The giant hawk let out a fearsome cry and flames burst from its wings, morphing into tornadoes of fire. Archer stumbled back narrowly sidestepping the blaze as it roared towards him. The Fire Spin struck against the pillar.

He could hear Marcus laughing. Targeting the sound, Archer pulled out from behind the pillar firing his gun through the wall of fire.

As the combustion flickered away he saw the bullets ricochet off an energy shield protecting Marcus and Faleris, and as he lowered the gun Houndoom bolted ahead right as Faleris shot another fire attack from its open beak directly at Archer. Houndoom met its stream of fire with its own, the two moves colliding in an explosive ball of flame; Faleris' attack was more powerful, and Houndoom yelped as it was forced to spring aside. Smoke trailed in the aftermath of both attacks, carrying with it the ominous spectre of charred scent.

Zoe meanwhile had sent out Tanzee, which let loose a flurry of sharp leaves towards Faleris. They missed utterly.

Archer could see Zoe clench her fists in frustration as Tanzee started hopping around playfully, as if it viewed the whole fight as a game.

Enwreathed in fire, Faleris flew past Tanzee in a gale, aiming again at Archer and Zoe. They could only save themselves by jumping for cover; meanwhile Houndoom lunged at the opportunity, sinking its teeth into one of Faleris' wings. The hawk let out a shriek and Houndoom leapt away before Marcus could club it back.

Faleris vaulted about before slashing at Houndoom. It struck its target across the flank, knocking Houndoom out, and before Faleris could inflict the final blow Archer recalled his pet.

At a signal from its rider, Faleris screeched and swooped down in another fiery tackle, talons outstretched. Archer pulled Zoe to the side and the giant hawk struck against one of the pillars instead, where its claws got jammed into the stone. Squawking, it flapped its wings frantically as Marcus tumbled off its back.

He pulled out Faleris' sphere and recalled it from where it was trapped, only to find himself staring directly into the barrel of Archer's gun.

For the first time since Archer had met this man, he saw fear in his eyes.

Archer smiled maliciously, but the instant he pulled the trigger, vines wrapped around his arm and yanked his hand up. The bullet hit against the ceiling.

He turned his head in time to see Zoe exclaiming in shock, and suddenly he and Zoe were completely entangled in thorny tendrils. It was Tanzee that had unleashed its vine whip.

Zoe let out an astonished cry, "Tanzee, what are you doing?!"

Tanzee was chattering with laughter, its teeth bared in a wide grin.

They were now surrounded by PIDF soldiers. Marcus chuckled as he pulled himself up from where he'd fallen; he took the gun away from Archer, then swung back rapidly. Archer bent over in pain as he was pistol-whipped in the ribs.

"That's for thinking you could depose me." Marcus then glanced at the soldiers, and gave a single order.

"Put them with the others."

Chapter 13 - The Prisoners ✅

Held at gunpoint by PIDF soldiers, a somber Archer and Zoe were escorted down the way as prisoners.

"Fucking Unowns," grumbled Archer.

"Maybe it was an oversight and they'll return?" Zoe considered, trying to boost optimism.

"Unowns? Not a chance in hell."

Tanzee's cackling drew his attention to the grass type, which was jeering at them from the shoulders of one of the guards. "Actually, I take it back," Archer added. "At least you know Unowns are out to cause trouble. The traitor monkey is worse."

"Shut it," snapped the soldier, poking Archer roughly with the muzzle of the rifle he held. Archer bit back some unpleasant answer and fixed his eyes straight ahead as they walked.

They reached a holding area and were pushed unceremoniously into a barred jail cell containing three other people. The soldiers locked the door and then left, with Tanzee remaining atop a table with its leering grin.

The first person Archer noticed was a dark-clad figure sitting wearily to the side, half-leaning against the wall. He was of a fair complexion, with a black visor resting atop tousled salt-and-pepper hair and eyes a shade of magenta; the man was thin enough to imply he hadn't eaten well in more than a few days, though the way he rested his head on one hand was in a manner less evocative of exhaustion and more of boredom.

Nonetheless, out of the group of three other prisoners there, he seemed to be the most curious about them. To the other side was a younger man, his blue hair in cornrows, and wearing loose yellow attire, less interested in the newcomers and more in attempting a futile struggle to reach a key tauntingly out of reach.

The final person was a lady of about twenty, with light green hair cut to a bob, who looked perhaps the most jaded of all her cellmates. She wore a flowing green dress, in a style distinctively of the island.

It was the first of these three people who spoke. "My name is Professor Victor Ashford. I was the head of the Pal Genetic Research Unit." He observed them for a moment and then asked, "Are you Archer and Zoe?"

"You've heard of us?" remarked Archer.

"I heard Colonel Dryden complaining about the two of you."

"I didn't know we were so popular," Archer replied tongue-in-cheek.

Victor gave a disdainful half-scoff. "When the colonel falls afoul of something or someone, he makes sure everybody knows." He turned towards the others and named them in turn, "Might I introduce Axel Travers and Lily Everhart."

"Hey," greeted Axel; the younger man was still trying to get the key from beyond the bars, while the woman Lily, didn't even acknowledge them.

"We formerly headed different government agencies here on Palpagos Island," Victor continued explaining. "The PIDF commissioners were our supervisors."

Faint memories resurfaced of scorched ground seen when they'd first arrived in town and met Marcus. Archer narrowed his eyes. "Oh yes, I heard they decided to downsize."

"When the Unown arrived," —and here Victor glared with accusation towards the younger man in their group— "Axel decided to take it upon himself to leave messages everywhere to spread what they'd said. Colonel Dryden wasn't sure who was responsible, so he eliminated the whole commission and imprisoned their second-in-commands… us."

"You're the one who left that message about the tower and trees?" Archer asked, interested, as he turned towards Axel.

"Sure was," grinned Axel. "I knew there was something going on here because the Unown said so; if I'd understood exactly what, I would have been more blatant. Wasn't it clever, plastering that cryptic shit everywhere to make folks ask questions about this place?"

Victor spoke with poorly disguised resentment. "The Colonel didn't like it very much."

"The Colonel can go to hell."

"It's because of you we're in this prison!" snarled Victor. "If you hadn't woken up one day and decided to become a dissident, we would still be able to come and go as we pleased. You didn't even try to hide that it was you leaving those messages. You made it seem as if there was a conspiracy brewing against the PIDF."

The lady now spoke up. "Can you please, for once, give the fighting a rest? It's bad enough just being here without having to listen to you two always bickering."

"Finally found something worse than griping about how Marcus is mistreating the Pals, Lily?" retorted Axel.

"No, but if anything all this is a testament to how incorrigible human cruelty is. The colonel claimed the PIDF was protecting the wildlife here, but all he was doing was profiting off them in secret...and you don't give a damn. And you…" Lily now levied her scathing criticism against Victor, "had to go and make the Pal Essence Condenser, thinking that would appease Marcus. The first thing he does is feed our own Pals into the ether. Of course you didn't have any Pals of your own, so what did you care."

Zoe broke in, addressing Victor. "You invented it? Why would you invent something like that?"

"To see if it would work." Victor looked as bored and nonchalant as ever.

"I suppose you regret it now," Lily prompted.

He thought about it for a moment. "...no. It was a good experiment."

Archer had the distinct idea Lily would have liked to hurl something at Victor, just out of spite.

"The only reason the Unowns weren't immediately done away with is that they somehow jammed the device with their psychic energy. It's anyone's guess why the Colonel is keeping us alive," Victor continued, turning back to Archer and Zoe. "Colonel Dryden is very open about what he dislikes, not necessarily what he plans to do about it. …You know the Unowns weren't even the initial plan? He'd sent his men out before to catch a Frostallion, up in the Astral Mountains, and wanted me to attempt crossing its DNA with that of his Faleris to see if an even stronger Pal could be produced. I heard they successfully caught one, only to turn around and have it run off."

"That must be the Frostallion we stole," deduced Zoe, with a glance towards Archer.

"You stole it? From the PIDF?" Victor sounded truly impressed. "No wonder the Colonel is so angry at you."

"Look," Archer said, "ever since I landed here, Marcus Dryden seems as determined to prevent the islanders from knowing about the mainland regions, as he is to keep the mainland regions from knowing about this island. I know he's the ruling dictator or what-not here, but there's something more that he's up to and for all the shit I've been put through I feel I ought to know. This Pal Condenser thing, for starters. What's he trying to siphon energy from Pokémon for, anyway?"

"His ultimate weapon," Victor replied, as if that answered the question.

Footsteps preceded an arrival, and they all glanced up to see none other than Colonel Marcus Dryden enter with a contingent of four or five of his soldiers. Tanzee immediately scampered over to him.

"Good work Tanzee," Marcus said to it, "I'll make sure you get back home to your tamer."

He held a Poké Ball – a modern one, in its shiny red-and-white finish – and opened it to call Tanzee in. He then turned to Archer, entirely disregarding Zoe.

He was beaming at his own triumph. Archer wanted to beat the smugness off his face.

"I presume you've been making yourself comfortable here with my other guests," Marcus began, "Faleris is still recuperating its strength in its Pal Sphere in the other room because of you. As a result you've left me without a ride home, at least till my soldiers get another mount here."

He'd retrieved another Poké Ball from his coat pocket. This one was one of the antique Pal Spheres, which considering Faleris was recovering elsewhere, Archer figured must be empty.

"It's not a loss. I have plenty to entertain myself with here," said Marcus, the hint of a threat playing in his tone.

Archer tried to stop himself from watching the Pal Sphere that Marcus held too closely. He tried to force away growing feelings of fear; he couldn't shake off the worry that he'd soon have to relive a nightmare. You're letting your traumas run wild. You might be a prisoner, but Zoe said it was seen as inhumane here, just as it's supposed to be on the mainland. Not everyone even thinks about doing such a thing. ...They're not going to trap you in one of those.

Marcus noticed Archer's unease, and Archer glanced away. Without saying anything, he tucked the Pal Sphere in his coat pocket and regarded his prisoner steadily for a moment.

"Where are the Unowns?" Marcus demanded.

"Halfway across the globe," Archer replied, not missing a beat.

"They think they're safe now, I suppose."

"You expect to chase them?"

He'd spoken flippantly, as if it were a joke. It took a double-take for him to realize that Marcus was, in fact, genuinely serious.

"I'll grant you an explanation," said the colonel.

"You mean a monologue," Archer replied.

Marcus ignored his comment and spoke, "On this island we can mine gold and paldium – what you of the mainland call tumblestone – to excess. By blending gold and paldium and adding crude oil, we can produce a material we call plasteel."

Archer was unimpressed. "You just ripped that name off from a science fiction story. I'm pretty sure I heard it before."

Marcus continued. "I have an entire factory working to produce plasteel. It makes it possible to produce weaponry and armor beyond even what the modern world knows of, and to create Pal Spheres capable of capturing any creature without fail."

"...do you mean Master Balls?" Archer remarked, now realizing with interest they'd somehow attained the missing ingredient to a formula Giovanni had sought for some time.

"All that's left to acquire are weaponry blueprints my associate is sending us from outside," Marcus continued. "With that kind of technology, and with Faleris as the strongest Pal the island has ever seen, the PIDF will be an unstoppable force. We'll be able to conquer the world beyond the sea!"

Of all his captives, all remained speechless – all, that is, except for Archer, who began laughing loudly.

Marcus regarded him with disdain. "I fail to see what's so amusing, Mr. Verdi."

"The banana republic dictator thinks he can take over the planet," snickered Archer. "...and why? Because you've had success with your little Pal-world? The Pokémon world is far bigger than your tiny island, with more power than you can ever imagine. It's pointless how many laser cannons or overcharged gatling guns your third-world sweatshop can produce; your army is outnumbered a hundred-to-one."

"I have an ally on the mainland who says it can be done," replied Marcus undaunted.

"I don't give a damn if your ally is on the fucking planetary council," Archer told him seriously, "They're lying to you."

"Are you trying to bluff? Because you're not in a position to. This is my island," emphasized Marcus, "No one who lands on this island ever leaves. Palpagos Island doesn't even exist to the rest of the world without my say-so; it's only on the map when I say it is."

Archer became somber suddenly, and said, "This island is a stolen paradise, and everything the civilized world could want. That's just it – you're fighting a losing battle." He hesitated here. "You have no idea who's behind me. You obviously have no idea who you're dealing with."

"I'm sure the Rayne Syndicate once believed that. And look what they've turned into, thanks to several years of drugged food and living in the jungle outside of town like wild Pals. They're as blind as the islanders," Marcus laughed scornfully. "For all I care, they can all live their little sad lives without ever knowing the extent of what's really going on. Besides, if I let garbage like them get carried away learning too much, they'll just go off demanding rights."

"Like the truth behind this tower? Beyond its history; the secret it holds. The tower is the key, right?" Archer said. "You already control Palpagos Island. You don't need the mainland. What is it you really want?"

"Accomplishment. My grandfather established this regime. My father cemented it. I will be the one to expand it. And I won't let anyone undo the work of a hundred years in a day." Marcus seized Archer by the lapel. "You will never, in a thousand centuries, learn the secret of this tower."

"I already know," Archer retorted. "You told me when you said you're keeping the island off the map. The tower's the tallest thing for miles, so you put the antenna for a cloaking device on the roof."

They faced off steadily for a few moments and then Marcus addressed the soldiers.

"Take him...and her."

They opened the jail door, and two guards hauled Archer and Zoe out at gunpoint as Marcus led the way from the room.

Chapter 14 - Mirage Island ✅

Miles from any known region, a ship sailed on the sea towards coordinates as of yet unknown. It was manned by Pokémon trainers in distinctive black uniforms with a bright red R, and coiled whips and Poké Balls on their belts, the unmistakable attire of Team Rocket grunts; at the ship's helm were elite agents James and Jessie, dressed in their high-rank white uniforms with equal armament as their subordinates.

"Remember when we were on submarine duty?" James, ever the sentimentalist, reminisced, "the three of us crammed in that Magikarp-shaped vessel?"

"Don't tell me you're nostalgic for that tin can," Jessie laughed good-naturedly, "at least here we can see where we're going without a damn periscope."

Beside them on the deck, Meowth was lashing his tail. "So lemme get this straight," the cat said, redirecting their conversation, "they got this island we're sailing to on record as a wildlife sanctuary?"

"Because supposedly the Pokémon here branched out separately from the rest of the world," affirmed Jessie, "so you can find species here which just don't thrive elsewhere."

Meowth narrowed his eyes. "Except they didn't tell anyone there were humans living on the island too? ...and it mysteriously vanished off the map many years back?"

James gave a brisk nod. "It wouldn't have been very flattering to admit that in this modern day and age, the planetary council didn't defend one of their smaller regions from takeover."

"Meanwhile," added Jessie, "the people there are apparently still living like a third-world nation fighting over food and water, or at least they were those many years back."

"But I don't get it?" meowed the cat, "Doesn't the council do anything to oversee the place at all? What about the Pokémon League...didn't they have a division here?"

"Supposedly they've been letting them govern themselves all this time; no one's cared to check up on them. And the Pokémon League could easily be paid off in grants for its losses. Anyway, the island belongs to the boss now," Jessie said.

Wind buffeted the deck of the ship with its salty sea-spray, and the closer they got to the coordinates, the more seagull Pokémon they saw flying around and diving for prey in the water. Not a single sliver of land appeared on the horizon however.

James stood on the starboard side of the ship, gazing out at the sea. "Jess, I think we might've been sent on a wild Chansey chase. I don't see anything over there."

Meowth leapt onto James' head, the cat's ears and whiskers alert towards the ocean. "You sure about that? There's some kinda energy barrier rippling about the water."

"I don't see any force field."

"You humans don't see things right in front of you," meowed the cat.

Jessie came over to James' side and lifted binoculars towards where Meowth was now pawing the air.

"Meowth…" said Jessie, gazing intently through the lens.

"Yeah?"

She lowered her binoculars. "There's nothing there."

The cat hissed.

Lifting the binoculars again, Jessie continued to search the ocean with a scowl. "We've been sailing around this damn area for hours already. If we can't spot that island soon, we might have to head back and let the boss know he paid money for a mirage."

Archer and Zoe walked in silence with their escort of guards as Marcus strode ahead down the corridor. Deep inside, Archer's unease was growing; he could only surmise what their captors had in store for them.

They were led back to the brightly lit room with the Pal Condenser. Marcus halted here and turned to face them both.

Maybe another explanation. A...demonstration? This was just like that time back in the Orre region; the courtesy before some agony would be inflicted upon them. His mind was already painting elaborate nightmares from a palette of deductions, and he forced himself to stay calm.

No, but it's not the same, Archer assured himself, though his heart was beginning to hasten its pace, they're not going to do the same thing. There's no way they'd do that...

The slightest shudder ran through him.

He felt Zoe briefly press against his side, a comforting presence that brought him back to the moment.

"You impressed me with the battle against Faleris," Marcus was saying. "No one has ever been able to defeat us before. So I'll grant you a favor. I'll let one of you live."

Marcus turned around as a Katress padded into the room; it was a bicolor, light-blue and black feline, reminiscent of an Espeon though it stood on its hind legs, with a tuft of purple fur on its head that looked somewhat comically like a witches' pointed hat. In its paws it carried a cup filled with some kind of dark liquid, which Marcus took from the cat and placed before Archer and Zoe.

"This is made of nightshade," said Marcus, "...what we here on the island call 'Bellanoir's eclipse' after the legendary dark type. It'll kill whomever drinks it within twenty-four hours."

"You can't be serious?" Zoe echoed.

"Hell no," Archer countered. "If you expect to intimidate us into committing suicide, you can forget it."

"If you don't decide, then you will both die." As he spoke, he pointed a gun first at Archer, then turned slowly and aimed directly at Zoe. "In that case I can assure you, taking poison is more merciful."

Both Archer and Zoe gazed at him dumbfounded. Marcus lowered the gun.

"Make your choice," he said.

When they glanced uneasily at the poison and then at each other, yet neither made a move, Marcus advanced towards Zoe. She backed away from him but the soldiers seized her on both sides roughly, leading to her struggling in desperation. Marcus grabbed her by the chin and she tried unsuccessfully to kick him only to get slapped hard across the cheek, and she gasped in pain.

Archer didn't wait to see how it would play out, nor did he attempt to call their bluff. He reached over to take the nightshade drink from where it was and, willingly, he closed his eyes and swallowed it all.

It was sweet, but gave way to a subtle bitterness that lingered on the tongue. He placed the cup on the table, and looked up towards Marcus. "All right, satisfied? You have your sacrifice. Now let her go."

"You never cease to surprise me," Marcus remarked, lifting his eyebrows. "You struck me as mercenary, never as the gallant type."

"Archer..." Zoe started to say, but her voice trailed. Archer just jerked his head slightly for her to leave now, and without saying anything more Zoe turned to be led away.

The moment she did, Marcus reached into his pocket and whirled around – flinging a Pal Sphere at her.

She barely had time to give a startled outcry as the capsule struck her and opened, and she vanished in a flare of light.

Archer saw this, and his own tormented memories mingled all at once with aghast horror. He tried to leap for Marcus but the soldiers halted him with their weapons. "You bastard! You said you'd let her go."

Marcus turned towards Archer, evidently regaling in the torment he was inflicting on him. "Don't try to put words in my mouth. I merely said I'd let her live."

He only stared at him, unable to retort, as the sphere stopped shaking and Marcus picked it up from the floor. At that point, one of the soldiers walked in and saluted.

"Colonel," said the guard, "Your mainland associate has telephoned and is on hold to speak with you."

"Alas, I have business to tend to. It appears this will be the last we see of each other in this life, then... Good luck, Mr. Verdi," said Marcus, with a cordial dip of his head, and exited the room with the Katress following.

The world had seemed to slow for Archer. Everything had been a disaster, and nothing had gone to plan. Then again, why would he have thought it would? He wasn't in Kanto or Johto or Unova, where people took honesty and honor as cornerstones of civilization and one could buy antidotes at the corner mart; he was on a primitive island in the middle of nowhere. And he was going to die.

The worst was the thought he'd somehow been responsible for Zoe's capture. Throwing the sphere had been a deliberate choice by Marcus, because he'd seen Archer's concern over the empty capsule in the holding room. Somehow he'd deduced it was Archer's biggest fear, and of course used that to advantage.

The terrible thing was he should have seen it coming...he should have anticipated it. He was from Team Rocket, an admin of Team Rocket no less; he also knew these techniques from having been in both the position of inquisitor and victim at different times. A person's innermost terrors were always the first thing to be manipulated.

He wouldn't have wished imprisonment like that on anyone, let alone someone who'd become a friend.

In a sudden impulse and rush of vengefulness, he clenched his hand into a fist, spun about and hit the guard next to him.

The guard fell, knocked cold to the floor, as the second soldier reached for a handgun, but Archer acted faster punching him too. The impact knocked him backward into the Pal Condenser's glass container, and without thinking twice Archer slammed the door shut and struck the large button.

A single warning alarm blared out, and a scream drowned in a burst of burning light as the dial on the meter swung sharply right. Archer didn't wait to see the gruesome outcome; he snatched up the dropped handgun from the floor and raced out into the hallway.

The sound had drawn the attention of the guards outside, and even Marcus, who had walked away down the hall, turned back in confusion in time to see Archer burst into view.

Marcus's guards quickly cast forth Pal Spheres, whereupon multiple snarling Direhowl and even a couple of Lamball sprang out to attack. One of the sheep rolled at him in a spinning tackle; Archer jumped aside and fired above the animals, aiming for their trainers. He hit two soldiers one after the other and as they collapsed the rest ducked aside.

Then the worst thing happened at the worst moment. Archer's gun jammed.

As he scrambled to remove and reload the magazine, a Hyper Beam blasted towards him. Archer hit the floor as the screeching energy struck where he'd stood, crackling overhead as it fizzled out against the wall. One of the Direhowl launched itself at Archer, fangs bared, right as the magazine snapped into place and he jerked upward to shoot. The impact of the bullet pushed the wolf back in mid-air and it fell to the floor dead.

He fired again at the soldiers, but this time one of them seized a Lamball they'd sent out and held it in front of him. The little sheep bleated with fear as the gunshot narrowly missed. Archer grimaced.

"Fucking coward, using your low-level Pokémon as a shield," he muttered, shooting at the soldier's leg instead. When the man exclaimed and subsequently dropped the Lamball, Archer quickly shot again and dispatched him.

He'd momentarily gotten his opponents into disarray. Catching sight of Marcus fleeing down the path, his open coat billowing behind him and Zoe's Pal Sphere in hand, Archer pointed the gun at him.

Marcus gave a sharp yell as the bullet grazed the back of his hand and the Pal Sphere flew into the air, colliding against the wall. It burst open in a flare of white light and Zoe emerged, her violet eyes wide with shock.

Instantly Archer was at her side, crushing the sphere that now lay on the floor under his heel. It shattered into pieces, far more fragile than a mainland Poké Ball. "Zoe," he said, holding her, "are you all right?"

"I'm fine," replied Zoe, gazing into his eyes.

The emotion of their reunion was short-lived. They turned to see Marcus standing only steps away, clutching his bleeding hand as fury contorted his features into a scowl.

"Twenty-thousand pieces of gold..." Marcus ordered, seething with fury, "for the man who brings them back dead."

"Run for it!" Archer cried, pushing Zoe down the corridor, when suddenly they were confronted by the Katress.

Hissing, the catlike creature sent out several balls of violet energy, which twirled towards them. They pulled aside evasively; one of the orbs of energy flew past them into the holding room to crash against the prison door, melting the lock. Axel saw his opportunity and immediately pushed it open.

"Let's get out of here!" Axel cried out as he ran from the jail cell, with Lily and Victor running close behind.

As they all ran for the doorway Archer noticed a low hanging shelf on the way out of the room; on it were the Poké Balls that were taken from him and Zoe upon captivity. With a swift motion, he grabbed them and stuffed a couple into his pocket, handing Zoe the others.

He glanced back when he heard a scream, and saw Lily fall to the floor, killed by a Hyper Beam in the back. In the same instant, Victor was seized by Tanzee's vines. The grass type monkey, which had apparently been sent out during the fray, cackled fiendishly.

"Go...!" Victor shouted, motioning to Archer, Zoe, and Axel to flee, right as he ripped out of the entanglement. It was futile though; another gunshot pierced through the air, and he collapsed onto the floor dead.

The three of them ran all the way to the rooftop. Here, Archer whistled and Frostallion flew up to meet them. The moment they all saw the horse standing there, however, a new problem was discovered.

"Three people won't all be able to ride on its back," said Archer, voicing their unanimous thoughts, "We'll be too heavy for it."

"Too bad," muttered Axel, and then added forcefully, "It seems our alliance ends here!"

Before Archer could fully react, Axel swung about and struck him in the stomach, and in a single motion leapt astride the horse. The animal reared back with a whinny and jumped into the air.

"You traitor! We helped you escape!" shouted Zoe, as she took the gun out of Archer's hand and lifted it to fire at Axel. Archer quickly outstretched an arm and held her back. Zoe did not protest but looked at him in surprise, asking:

"Are we just going to let him get away with this?"

He didn't answer. They watched as Frostallion got into in full flight, and Axel couldn't resist a parting gloat:

"When you see Faleris at mealtime, tell him I said bon appétit...!"

Archer smiled coldly and pulled out a Poké Ball.

"Frostallion...return," he ordered.

Axel's boastful glee was replaced by a look of sheer horror, and he couldn't utter a single word before his mount was engulfed below him in glistening red light, Frostallion disappearing at the same time as he screamed and plummeted miles down to the doom of solid ground.

Zoe winced, a bit disconcerted as she peered over the edge of the drop. Archer, to the contrary, was jovially callous. "Gravity's a bitch."

"Apparently so," agreed Zoe.

Archer sent out the perplexed Frostallion again; he and Zoe mounted the horse and flew off right as the PIDF soldiers burst onto the rooftop and began shooting at them.

He gazed down at them as the flying horse looped around the building. The effects of the poison concoction were slowly creeping on him; his vision was starting to blur, and his breath was beginning to get labored, but if he was going to die then he'd take a few of his enemies with him – and fuck up Marcus' plans besides. Archer mustered a grin and gripped the reins tight.

"All right Frostallion, show me what a war-horse can do."

Frostallion whinnied and outstretched its wings, coating them in a flash of pointed ice like glacial swords. It swooped down at high speed, past the soldiers, and aimed directly for the antenna.

A giant explosion engulfed the tower rooftop in a shock wave of ice and flame; Marcus, who'd opened the rooftop door, immediately pulled back as his soldiers were flung backwards, some screaming as they fell to their deaths from the height. He could only shout curses as Frostallion whipped past overhead, its wings shimmering with ice and its riders cheering their victory.

Out in the ocean, the Team Rocket ship had given up on locating the island and turned to retreat back to the mainland when they heard an explosion in the distance.

A charge of energy accumulated on the sea and, like a tidal wave, cascaded against an unseen barrier that rippled all at once into visibility. Beyond it, as if hidden by a curtain all this time, lay the most pristine tropical island Jessie, James, and Meowth had ever seen in their many travels. The coastline ringed with shimmering tumblestone boulders shaped into pyramids, palm trees along fine gold sand with a forested mountain peak as backdrop, and most impressive of all a single skyscraper with the Unown letter I on it glowing like a company logo.

Atop the skyscraper was a ball of fire, and circling in mid-air was what looked like an icy Rapidash racing across the wind. The creature, and what looked like two riders astride it, swooped down and vanished beneath the canopy of trees into the secluded safety of the woods.

Looking through her binoculars, Jessie noticed the riders of the flying horse, and recognized Archer. "Turn about!" she cried, as the boat spun backward towards the island.

She joined James and Meowth as they gazed out in astonishment at the beautiful sight before them.

"I can't believe it," James marvelled. "Our mirage island actually exists?"

Meowth chimed in with a yowl, "Told ya so! That also means all those different species that're supposed to live there must exist too!"

"Different or not, they're still Pokémon," declared Jessie, with a smile, "and all Pokémon exist for the glory of Team Rocket."

Chapter 15 - Poison ✅

Jett had been on hold for what seemed like an unnecessarily long time, and was about to hang up the telephone when her business associate at last took the call.

She was incredibly peeved. "Marcus."

"Jett," he reciprocated, "apologies I couldn't come to the phone sooner. I was held up over here by an unforeseen situation."

He sounded out of breath. She didn't much care.

"Yes, well, I'm simply calling to let you know that the second supply shipment is on the way, so you'd better make sure you send extra security or whatever you need to get it. The plane will be passing over the island in a few days time."

"That's fine," said Marcus, "we'll be sure to get the drop."

"... and after that," Jett continued a bit emphatically, "I expect the payment to be sent."

'Payment', of course, was a mild allegory for what essentially amounted to 'flatten a section of Lumiose City for me.'

Marcus, to her chagrin, did not acknowledge the statement in any way. "By the way I have your Pal here, which you sent over to help keep lookout on those Syndicate people," he said instead. "Do you want it back?"

"Well, I think Pansage has had enough of an adventure over there," Jett concurred. "Probably enough to raise his level several times over. I'll come by around the same time as the supply drop does to pick up my Pokémon myself."

The easiest way of training a Pokémon, she'd found, was to drop it on Palpagos Island to help Marcus in whatever chore he had and to get it back after a couple of months. It was far faster than deigning to go out battling herself and much more cost effective than paying one of the local Pokémon daycares or breeding centers to do it for her. Jett imagined her Pansage, or Tanzee as Marcus and the rest of the islanders apparently called its species, would probably be just about the right level by now for her to consider evolving it into a Simisage.

"Your yacht can dock at Fisherman's Point, like you've done in the past. We will speak again soon," Marcus said, and hung up before she could respond.

"You're in an awful hurry, Marcus," Jett muttered as she returned the receiver to its cradle. That said it hardly mattered, so long as he came through with what he promised.

She distrusted him. But as long as he did not distrust her, the gamble would pay off.

At least things had been relatively quiet in the past few days. There had not been any other rogue wild Pokémon attacking anywhere, and she was glad for it. The urban redevelopment project was making good progress and Lumiose City was already seeing more tourism as a result, with trainers flocking to catch some of the rare Pokémon that had begun nesting in the newly built wild zones, and Quasartico Inc. was profiting as well. So far, so good, she thought.

As she let her mind wander, her gaze briefly landed on the flowering plant near the window. Its three pointed petals were open towards the sun and vines reached out of its pot in a beautiful cascade, with fine dew shimmering on the leaves.

...actually, that can't be dew, Jett realized. How can it have dew indoors? I guess it's just like that... What a remarkable plant.

Jett stayed there all day. By late afternoon the phone rang. It was Corbeau.

"Jett, I've been meaning to ask you...what are these flowers called, again?"

"Eternal Flowers."

"How big do they grow?"

"I really don't know." She glanced reflexively at the flower pot beside the window; she could've sworn the blossom was even larger today than yesterday, and not by a small amount. "I think they're supposed to grow fairly big...?"

She'd already asked the gardener, Seymore, the same question a couple of days ago. He'd been apologetic and admitted that he had no idea. "I've never seen this kind of flower before," Seymore had told her. "The ones outside have shown varying degrees of growth. The vines spread fairly rapidly."

"Well, the plants you gave me have grown enormously," Corbeau replied, snapping her attention back to the present conversation, "so much so that I've had to place them outside of the building, near the entrance... I could swear they moved a few inches from the spot my landscaping team initially planted them."

"I must confess, the same thing happened to the plants I've been dealing with," Jett confided. "My gardener has no explanation."

"You know Jett..." he paused for a moment, then continued, "I'm a practical man, but I'm also a careful man; I think I'll bring in a scientist to take a look at these plants and give me their opinion. I still think they might be poisonous."

"Corbeau, with all due respect, you say that because you are, among other things, a gym leader that deals with poison types."

There was a minute of silence at the other end of the phone line and Jett worried she might have offended him, however, he continued speaking without any change in the inflection of his voice. "Jett, I am going to find a scientist who will do a bit of research on these strange plants. I figure you might want to hear about this, considering I know something similar happened near one of Quasartico's construction sites," he told her, "There was another incident with a wild Pokémon, near my gym. This time it was an Audino."

"Oh no," Jett muttered.

"The good thing is that this Pokémon didn't want to annihilate everyone; it just seemed in distress. It seemed it'd gotten itself tangled in vines."

"In vines?"

"It was a rather peculiar Audino; it had white fur instead of pink, and its ears were standing up straight. One of the gym employees managed to untangle it from the vines, and they tell me it reverted to being a regular Audino right in front of them," Corbeau recounted. "Unfortunately the Pokémon ran off before they could get a better look at it."

"I remember the myths they tell here in the Kalos region about a type of temporary evolution some Pokémon can undergo, called mega evolution," Jett reminisced, "I know no one has ever seen it in real life, but some scientists say it's theoretically possible...perhaps in another dimension. This would be the first I've ever heard of something akin to that actually happening."

She frowned pensively.

"But if that's true, why? Why would all these Pokémon suddenly be mega evolving seemingly by themselves, out of nowhere?"

It couldn't be the Eternal Flowers affecting the Pokémon, could it? Jett reflected with annoyance, as she thought back to the previous account of a mega evolved Pokémon. Hadn't that occurred after the flowers were brought in...? Not like that will make a difference of course. These plants are too beautiful to uproot merely because the wildlife doesn't have sense enough to walk around them.

"Well, no one saw the strange Audino outside of myself and my gym's employees," Corbeau said. "I am busy, so we'll chat later."

He hung up the phone, as did Jett, and she was left thinking about the possibility of the beautiful blooms being poisonous. If the wild Pokémon are getting tangled in the plants, certainly they wouldn't try to eat them...would they?

Jett stared at the flower and shook her head.

"Doesn't matter...If it were really harmful something would've happened by now," she told herself.

Jett sighed, and began sorting through all the paperwork she had on her desk, not paying attention to the plant near the window, which was now using its vines to slide itself slowly away from the sun to a shadier spot on the window.

By the time Archer and Zoe reached the cabin, the sun had already set and evening shadows were darkening the forest. Archer was ill. He could barely focus on what was ahead of him, and with it came a feeling that he might faint or vomit or both. Zoe took Frostallion's reins from him when she saw him lean forward, resting his head on the horse's frosty mane.

She tethered the horse and helped him off the animal. He was partially leaning on her for support as they went into the cabin, and she directed him to the main bed.

Archer lay down shivering. Zoe took a blanket and covered him with it.

"It's probably a long shot..." Archer said, his voice growing faint, "have you ever seen large pink berries, with pointed leaves? We call them Pecha Berries on the mainland... Maybe they're a different color here, or something..."

She gave a small shake of her head. "I've never seen any plant like that here," Zoe replied. "We don't know of any cure for poisoning."

"So if your Pal gets attacked by a poison type, they die?"

"Some of them get immunity."

"I wish I were back home," he answered. He closed his eyes briefly and reopened them to notice Zoe's worried look as she searched his face for any progression of the poison.

He suddenly felt a pang of sympathy for her, after all she was caring for him, and now he had begun worrying about her. What would happen to her if he died? How would she make it back to her people now that Marcus had her on a hunt list? His thoughts were interrupted when she spoke.

"I never got to thank you for what you did back at the tower," said Zoe, "I don't understand how Tanzee could have betrayed us."

"There's nothing to understand," replied Archer, "It sounded like that monkey had a previous trainer... Tanzee was planted there like a spy."

"No wonder Tanzee showed up around the time Grizzbolt disappeared," Zoe considered ruefully.
