"Marcus thought up a lot, but he overlooked something..." Archer said weakly, "For all that about wanting to expand his rule with special weapons or plasteel or whatever he's doing....I don't think he even realized the weaponry blueprints he needs were part of what we stole from that supply drop."

They were both quiet for a long moment. He glanced over to the nightstand drawer where they'd hidden the schematics.

"If you ever see people who say they're part of Team Rocket...with a uniform that has a red letter R...give them the blueprints and tell them what happened...please." Archer swallowed with difficulty; his throat was beginning to feel dry. "Maybe it's wishful thinking but I can't help but hope that the Unowns maybe went off to get help, or someone...and then they'd be back... Stupid, isn't it?"

"It's not stupid," replied Zoe, "They seem to be intelligent creatures."

Archer felt his eyelids getting heavy and could barely keep his eyes open. Zoe put a hand on his forehead and noted, "Your face is warm, hopefully not a fever brewing. I'm getting something to bring down your temperature." She walked away and came back a few minutes later with a cool wet cloth, which she put on his forehead.

"That feels good," he said.

Archer was unaware precisely when he fell asleep, only that it came alongside a whirlpool of confusion. His nightmares were bizarre and fraught with violence, and he tossed and turned in restless sleep. He was far from the island, hauled by memories back into a dark and forbidding room, with a master who inflicted cruelty and compassion on a whim. It was constant interrogation with intermittent agony, till his heart raced and his breath caught short and he was begging once more for reprieve. All he wanted was peace.

"Please...I'll do whatever you ask of me..." he was whispering, "I can't take any more... Stop..."

Delirious from the effects of the poison, Archer tried to reach towards items on the floor next to the bed. Zoe, who had remained by his side, followed his gesture and realized he wanted to get the Poké Balls.

She took Houndoom's Poké Ball and handed it to him, then watched with wonder as he tapped the button on it. The sphere's red lid opened and, with a flash that momentarily illuminated the dark room in glistening white light, sent out Houndoom. The dog pawed at him and whined.

He gazed perplexed at the open capsule, as if his mind was blank with confusion. "Archer, try not to move around so much. You need rest," she advised him.

Archer lifted his eyes groggily towards her; his pupils were dilated so wide they seemed like ink wells. "Where are we?" he murmured. "I barely remember getting here."

"In the cabin. We're safe here."

"You've been taking care of me all this time?"

"You sound surprised. We're friends, that's what friends do."

Suddenly, there was clattering outside, followed by frantic clucking of the Chikipi. This drew Zoe's attention to the window. Houndoom, meanwhile, lay his head beside Archer on the bed as she walked away.

She pulled back the curtains slightly. Everything outside was still. Moonlight shed a feeble glow across the pond, which did not even betray ripples of a nighttime breeze.

With a slight frown, Zoe turned away from the window and returned to Archer's bedside.

"It's strange. I could've sworn there was something out there bothering the Chikipis." She had barely said these words when the door burst open and in came several soldiers clad in black with a red letter R on their uniforms, followed by their captains James and Jessie.

Houndoom barked and wagged his tail.

"Good to see you haven't forgotten us, Houndoom," Jessie said.

"Archer, you look like shit," James observed. "I thought vacationing on a tropical island would do you some good."

God, he was happy to see his colleagues again. Weak as he still was, he managed a smirk.

"What took you guys so long…?"

"The Unowns found us on the beach and pointed us in the right direction," said James.

Meowth came in at that moment, took one look at Archer and said, "Damn. Who messed you up so bad?"

Zoe glanced at Meowth in surprise; she'd never seen a talking Pal, at least not one that could communicate in human language, but she wasn't going to start questioning it. "It's poison," she piped up, "We barely escaped with our lives."

"...and who might you be?" Jessie inquired.

"Guys, she saved my life..." Archer hurried to tell them, "She's stayed by my side all this time."

"Well in all fairness," added Zoe, "He saved my life too."

Jessie and James looked at each other. "It looks like an interesting story," observed Jessie, "but first things first, we need to get him an antidote before he gets any sicker."

"It kinda looks as if his body is fighting it," Meowth chimed in, "I can go get the medicine he needs from our team medic." Meowth didn't wait for an answer, he spun around as fast as his feline paws could go and ran out to the rest of the minions that were stationed outside the cabin.

Archer pressed further into the pillows, still shivering and feverish and half-wondering if he was still dreaming and his friends being here was hence yet another cruel trick of his imagination. His throat was so incredibly parched by now; his mind flitted aimlessly from one thing to another, directed by the fever's whims. He could hear James and Jessie talking with Zoe beside him but he didn't strain to focus on their words.

It wasn't long before the cat returned with the antidote.

"It's Heal Powder. Ya need to mix it with water and drink it down," Meowth explained.

Zoe immediately brought a cup with water and while Meowth mixed the powdered medicine into the liquid, she helped Archer sit up on bed.

She helped him hold the cup up to his mouth and he swallowed the contents slowly. "This stuff is damn bitter!" he complained.

"Just drink it," Jessie ordered, "The boss is going to want to hear everything you've gone through and probably have a lot of questions."

Chapter 16 - Conquest of Territory ✅

Archer had fully recovered by the next day, and went with Zoe to meet Giovanni who was set to fly in that morning.

Archer straightened his posture as the helicopter landed lightly on the grass and the boss of Team Rocket emerged, preceded as usual by his pet Persian.

As Archer stood at attention and saluted, he could sense Zoe beside him fidget with nervousness. He had already told her so much about his organization by now, and he knew she wanted to make a good impression.

He knew as well that what little she'd seen of Team Rocket, ever since they'd landed on Palpagos Island and reunited with him, awed her. The encampment James and Jessie set up here on the beach was a miniature fortress, having a number of large tents with turrets positioned defensively around the perimeter and several Meowth digging in the ground for gold, and some electric type Pokémon powering a small generator so that they even had electricity. They'd quickly established a pocket of modern life, and Archer knew it could only get better as they expanded further into the island.

Giovanni halted before him and said, "At ease. Archer...it's good to see you are alive. For a while we thought of the possibility that something had happened to you."

"The enemy did try," replied Archer, "but I had some help. Sir," he added, turning from Giovanni towards Zoe, "this is Zoe Rayne; she's the one I spoke to you about over the telephone. I owe her my life."

Giovanni extended a hand which Zoe shook briefly. "A pleasure to meet you Zoe. I believe a thank you is in order since you helped Archer in his time of need."

"It's an honor for me, sir...to meet the leader of Team Rocket in person," she replied.

Giovanni's Persian had walked up to Zoe and, evidently having come to a decision about her, gave a long meow and entwined itself around her legs. She smiled and petted the large cat, which reciprocated by purring.

"You have a charming..." Zoe hesitated briefly, and Archer could see she was now having the same dilemma, only in reverse, to the one he'd once had with naming the island creatures, "...Mau?"

"Persian," Giovanni corrected, adding, "It seems my consigliere approves of you. Not many people can claim such high honor. ...Let's go to my office on the yacht, it seems to have docked already."

They walked in the direction of the newly built ship dock. The Team Rocket minions had spent all night working on it so they now had a brand new boardwalk stretching out to where Giovanni's yacht had been anchored off the coast of the island. They boarded and went directly to Giovanni's office aboard the ship.

Much as in his casino office at Celadon City, there was a tapestry bearing Team Rocket's bright red R insignia. This hung on the wall behind a fine mahogany desk, with bookshelves and a globe to the side, but here there was also a wide window overlooking the ship deck as well as a wicker basket lined with blankets for Persian to curl up in when the sun streamed in at just the right angle.

At least the sun is as it should be on Palpagos Island, thought Archer, who still found himself at a loss for answers when it came to many of the island's peculiarities.

"Everything is strange here; even the damn moon is upside down," Archer was remarking to his godfather as they all sat down.

Giovanni was blunt. "We're in the southern hemisphere. The sky looks different on this side of the equator."

That explains a lot, thought Archer.

Dismissing the topic hence, Giovanni moved on to more pressing matters. "You said in our earlier conversation that you and Zoe acquired some schematics being delivered in an airplane supply drop?"

Archer nodded, and he handed Giovanni several documents.

"These are the blueprints," Archer explained, and as Giovanni began perusing the documents, he went on, "This island is full of natural resources. They've got gold and tumblestone everywhere in the sand; you barely have to mine for it. That's not all...iron ore, coal deposits...about the only think I think they lack is crude oil, judging from how Marcus was flying it in."

Giovanni looked up at him from the blueprints with interest. "Well, Archer, it seems like you've stumbled on a very literal gold mine."

Receiving the praise of his godfather was always something Archer viewed as an honor.

"...and you say that he receives these supply drops at least once a week?" asked Giovanni.

"Yes sir."

"Interesting. I'll call our chief scientist here to take a look at these schematics. These could prove useful to us."

"Apparently Marcus Dryden needs a material he calls plasteel to make those weapons."

"You mentioned it could be the same material we need for the Master Ball."

"He claimed it was."

"All the hassle it took to finally take over the Silph Company..." Giovanni reminisced, "only to find that we lacked the secret formula to manufacture their most valuable product. Now to have it practically fall in our laps...but you aren't sure how they make this plasteel?"

Archer gave a shake of his head. "All we know so far is it's some sort of blend using tumblestone, gold, and crude oil."

"Then the priority is figuring out what the exact amount is," Giovanni replied.

"For that, we may have to find out where Marcus has his factory," said Archer.

"It's only a matter of time that we do... We own the island and everything on it," Giovanni said. "There's a legal caveat, of course, because the territory was on record as a wildlife sanctuary we have to entertain some sort of an ecological delegation here as a condition of sale. That said, they know fully well they're expected to approve."

His brown eyes glinted with unspoken menace, and Archer returned a small smile at the thought.

"In any case," Giovanni continued speaking, "we're going to start construction on several developments, including drilling for oil."

"Sir, if they're having crude oil shipped from the mainland, wouldn't that mean Palpagos Island lacks it?" Archer asked, perplexed.

"I highly doubt there's no oil on this island. The fact Mr. Dryden is flying it in simply says he doesn't know enough about oil production to be aware of its existence here."

Both Archer and Zoe seemed more confused than ever. Giovanni glanced at Zoe.

"Do the townspeople use gas lamps?" he asked.

"Yes," Zoe replied.

"Crude oil is always found underneath natural gas reservoirs."

Jessie, James, and Meowth showed up then at the open door, and briefly knocked before their boss waved them in. Giovanni turned his attention back to Archer and Zoe. "We can resume this conversation later," he dismissed them.

Archer and Zoe bid farewell and accordingly left the office.

Not long afterwards Archer saw an opportunity to show Zoe around the Team Rocket camp and introduce her to people. He started giving her a tour and crossed paths with his sister, Kris.

Even considering she was a fairly young recruit, it made sense Kris had been assigned to their present island operations, Archer reflected; she owned a Suicune, something that made her the pride and joy of Team Rocket since few trainers were privileged enough to have caught such a vaunted legendary. Luckily for them she had gleefully joined their ranks early on, because he couldn't imagine how the state of their organization might have been otherwise.

"Kris! There's someone I want you to meet; this is Zoe Rayne." He then turned to Zoe and said, "Zoe...this is my sister, Kris."

As the girls greeted each other amiably, Archer looked with surprise at what he saw his sister had.

"Kris, what the fuck is this?" he asked.

Kris was beaming. "I got myself a pride of miniature gold Suicune."

Her Suicune had settled itself importantly in the midst of several smaller animals. They were half the height of it and looked almost identical to the horned leopard, save that their fur and horns were brilliant gold, and instead of two long tails they had a single fluffy one tipped at the end like a Ninetales'. They all looked up at Archer, bored.

"You mean a pack," corrected Archer. "They have one bushy tail. They're canines, not cats. Where did you even get them?"

"Suicune went out for a run and came back with friends. So did Eevee," added Kris, glancing over at her other pet. Eevee was scampering around, playing tag with one of the white Eevee that were typical on the island.

Archer turned towards Zoe and motioned to the animals. "What do we call the shiny Eevee and the little Suicunes?"

"Cremis and Gildane," Zoe replied, gesturing to each one in turn, and then added, "…I never thought I'd hear a Gildane being referred to as little. They're typically hard to catch, but fairly common here on the shoreline near Feybreak Cove."

Kris' eyes opened wide. "Shiny Eevee and Suicune are common here?"

Around this time one of the minions walked in carrying a Pokémon under their arm. It was a little fox with a fiery tail and paws.

"Look what I caught," grinned the minion.

"What is that?" asked another.

"A fox."

"I know it's a fox. What kind of a fox?"

"I don't know but I think it's a fire type."

"...really? With the fire on its paws I never woulda guessed."

A third minion walked by. "Hey, what's up?"

"I caught me a fox."

"Ooo, I want a fox. Where'd you find it?"

"Out on the meadow. It actually lets me carry it around and shoot fire at things."

"You serious? How'd you train it to do that?"

There was a small cluster of minions by the time Archer, Zoe, and Kris walked over.

One of the grunts pointed at the animal. "We don't know what kind of a Pokémon that is."

"It looks like a Vulpix."

"It only has one tail."

"That's a Nickit if I ever saw one," another chimed in.

"Come on. Nickit aren't fire type," yet one more commented, "That's got to be a form of Fennekin."

Kris pointed her Pokédex at the fox. On the device's screen was displayed:

Pokémon unknown. No available data.

"It's a miracle, considering everything else here is pretty much a known Pokémon with a different type," Archer remarked.

Everyone turned accordingly towards Zoe.

"Around here we call them Foxparks," she said. "They're everywhere on this island. They prey on the Chikipi."

The Foxparks licked its lips at the thought of chicken.

"Zoe," Archer said tentatively, "where did we put the Chikipi we've been using for eggs?"

"They're in their Pal Spheres, safe and sound," she replied.

"Okay. Whenever it is we let them out to feed them we're going to have to make them a coop somewhere around here like what they had back at the cabin in Bamboo Groves. Something Foxparks-proof."

While the group was pondering the fate of the Chikipi in the paws of the Foxparks, Jessie and James showed up with their tagalong Meowth.

"Everyone," Jessie said, "go along your way and do whatever was assigned to you earlier. Archer, Kris, and Zoe...stay."

When the minions had dispersed, James addressed them. "Giovanni wants you three to come now to join the group going to speak to Zoe's Syndicate. He's on his way there now."

The Syndicate encampment was not very far from where Team Rocket had set up their operations.

When they arrived, the Syndicate villagers greeted them warmly; much more warmly than they had first greeted Archer. How Zoe explained it to him later was such: if he was her husband, and the Team Rocket group were related in some fashion to him, then they were like in-laws and all one big happy family.

Introductions were made and the group sat down with the head of Team Rocket to discuss the situation. The tribe elders explained their situation and their concerns, while Zoe gave her opinion of it. Since they'd stopped eating the drugged food Marcus' army had been providing, they were starting to recover their memories slowly, including that of the 'ancient language' spoken by Archer and those from the mainland. Giovanni sat and listened intently to everyone and then spoke up himself.

"What has bowing your head to Colonel Marcus Dryden gotten you? You're reviled by the townsfolk. Marcus' group of minions, that which he refers to as 'the PIDF' has spread lies claiming your tribe, or 'the Syndicate' as you refer to yourselves, are poachers and thieves. Because of that, the townspeople hate you." Giovanni stopped talking briefly to let his words sink in.

"If that's the case, well then, I'm not sure what we can do," said one of the elders, looking around to the others there from the Syndicate, "It's hopeless for us I guess."

"No. It's not hopeless," Giovanni answered, "I have great interest in your island and all the bounty it can produce. I propose that your people join mine and together we shall rid the island of the scourge brought upon it by Colonel Dryden and his evil followers... It comes with a price, of course."

"Name your price, sir," proclaimed the elder.

"Complete loyalty to me," the Team Rocket boss explained, "Your youngsters will be trained to do battle, in the way not of mainland sportsmen or island mercenaries but of military warriors. Others will help with mining the precious rocks and mineral that are so plentiful here. Of course I will provide the most up to date equipment...it won't be picks and shovels...you shall be trained and your people will be advanced into modern day society."

"I believe we can all agree to what you ask of us," the elder said as all the others nodded in agreement. "We have seen how the one you call Archer fights, and it is impressive." Then seemingly having an afterthought, he asked, "...but other than modernizing our society and learning precision fighting, how will that help us to push away the threat of those who hate us?'

"Because," Giovanni said leaning back and looking at him straight in the eye, "When you become what they hate, they fear you."

Chapter 17 - Meeting with the Enemy ✅

"What the fuck do you mean, 'they're building a resort'?" Marcus was irate.

It was the first word he'd received about the Syndicate's recent activities, and the idea of their being so bold as to even attempt such a thing sounded ludicrous to his ears, if not outright impossible. The soldier standing before him fidgeted with unease.

"Well, Colonel...they've set up an oil rig on the eastern coast, gold and paldium mining operations in several locations around the island, and yes...they're building some kind of a tourist resort on the beach. Construction is proceeding exceptionally fast as well."

"They're a bunch of fuckwit primitives. They don't have the resources for that."

"They have help from the outside."

"Who the hell would that be?"

"The name of their commander is Giovanni Delavita."

"Delavita?" Marcus questioned, suddenly recalling something his mainland associate had once mentioned, "...The leader of Team Rocket?"

"Yes sir."

This bit of information took Marcus completely aback. He had vindictively been planning to fly over to the Syndicate encampment and get Faleris to strike some fear in them; it was only then that he began to realize the possible extent of the situation.

He should have anticipated intruders from the moment the island's cloaking device had been decimated, but they couldn't have come at a more inopportune time. He still did not have the weaponry he wanted for his mainland takeover. Granted, he had the materials being made, but without the schematics there was little more he could do but stockpile plasteel and await the next airplane shipment by Jett. He'd just gotten rid of one mainland troublemaker, or so he thought; could these newcomers be somehow linked to that man? Moreover, if they were in fact linked, were they as dangerous as Archer had been...?

I could call Jett and ask how much trouble these people could be... Marcus considered, but the last thing I need is her knowing about this. Jett's involvement in providing items was necessary to him, up to a point, but he didn't exactly want her interference in what he viewed as an island affair.

"Go to the encampment under a flag of truce," he ordered. "I want to meet with Delavita."

During all this time, Team Rocket had unequivocally established their presence on Palpagos Island.

They had indeed begun a lavish construction on the beachfront, with a multi-story structure of glass and fine marble, intended to eventually have an open seating area looking out to the ocean and a beautiful promenade with palm trees. Both the Pokémon they'd brought with them from the mainland and the newfound Pals they'd been wantonly capturing here on the island helped with the building, each creature assisting where its unique skills and moveset would do best.

Meanwhile, Team Rocket was already making professional warriors out of Zoe Rayne's Syndicate. They were given the same training as Team Rocket minions, and they found training sessions went far easier than those back home with their average new recruits. The Syndicate members picked up on everything fast, and the hunting and survival experience they already had provided them another advantage. In between sparring matches and weapons training, all mastered skillfully within a few attempts, Archer could already see Zoe's group becoming a formidable force and the perfect Team Rocket alliance.

For as strong as they were in physical combat, they still needed Pokémon. A few had pets of their own that merely needed to be trained up to higher levels, but most of them did not have any, so one of the first things they all decided to do was go out and catch some.

A small cluster of Team Rocket and Syndicate members set out at moon-rise and in the course of one night caught many lizard Pals called Leezpunk, which wore their shed scales like a kind of hoodie, and several flightless vultures called Cawgnito – all of which Archer took one look at when they got back to camp in the morning and immediately labelled "regional variants of Scrafty" and "Murkrow-Mandibuzz knock-offs" with no further consideration given to the matter.

"The ones who will really be able to say what they are will be the ecological delegation that's supposed to show up sometime in the next few days," said James.

"The way I see it the delegation is just going to be an annoyance," Archer commented.

"Yeah, but if we're going to make a profit off these critters back in Kanto we may as well know what to properly call them."

"What's there to know? Look at them. You can't tell me that's not a Mandibuzz." He pointed at one of the Cawgnito, which was strutting about with its species' quick, bobbing steps. "And its not like the average trainer really cares, so long as it's something rare they can show off in a battle."

"That looks nothing like a Mandibuzz."

"It eats carrion, and it has the same feather crest of a Murkrow."

"It's just a damn bird," James cast aside the notion. "The face covering is more like that of a Cubone."

"I knew it was a knock-off of something," declared Archer, vindicated.

A sharp squawk from Cawgnito made them all turn to see when Foxparks bit it from behind. The bird vaulted about, lunging to peck as the fox ran off with a mouth full of pilfered tail feathers and cackling with laughter.

"Keep an eye on your fox," Archer chided at the Foxparks' trainer across the way.

Nearby, he noticed Kris with her pet Eevee and the wild Cremis. She was trying to pull the two little animals away from a slice of cake that they were both devouring.

"Don't eat so much!" Kris was chiding them, "You'll both get indigestion! ...Look at this Archer, I turned my back on my plate for one minute and the Eevees raid it."

This brought forth a small chuckle from Archer. "You ought to get them the honeymoon suite once the top floor of the resort's finished. Around here sharing cake is considered a marriage," he quipped.

At this point Jessie came over with Meowth padding beside her.

"As per the boss' orders," Jessie said, standing decisively with her hands on her hips, "we need to get a group of minions and head off with him to a meeting requested by that guy, Marcus."

Archer smirked. "Well now," he said, "Won't it be interesting for him to see I'm still alive."

Once the group was gathered, they all marched to where their boss' transport vehicles were waiting. They stood in formation for Giovanni a few minutes and when he showed up, he snapped his fingers as he got into his limousine, giving them the signal to get into their cars.

The journey was fairly swift, but it probably would have been a longer travel time if they had not been using modern transportation. The island's lush vistas sped past as they headed direct to the meeting-spot. They had agreed to meet in a clearing that was a midpoint between the town where Marcus had his offices, and the Syndicate and Team Rocket encampments.

When they arrived, they found Marcus Dryden and several of his soldiers already there. As the Team Rocket entourage pulled up and stepped into view, Archer could see a few of the soldiers looked awed at their mode of transport – certainly astonishing compared to the islanders' typical mounts and horse-carts. He wondered if this was the first time many of them had ever seen modern vehicles.

Their leader was also astonished for a far different reason. Marcus took one look at Archer and went pale. He stood there, stunned into silence for a couple of minutes until Giovanni broke the ice.

"It is not easy to eliminate a Team Rocket agent," he said simply.

"Well, ahhhh," stammered Marcus.

"Let's get down to business," Giovanni said, waving off Marcus' concern. "I believe you asked me here because you are curious about my real estate development?"

Forcing himself to stop staring at the presumably resurrected Archer, Marcus Dryden recovered his voice and said:

"Mr. Delavita, I wondered just exactly what are your plans for Palpagos Island."

"We're going to transform the island into the premier tourism destination of this century," Giovanni replied, "Resort hotel and casino, proper Pokémon Centers and marts at walking distance from human settlements, not to mention we're taking the old colosseum you have and bringing it up to date."

"The arena?" asked Marcus quizzically.

"We're building a new one... for sport battling, not these bloody duels you locals seem to favor," Giovanni said. "We'll have an annual tournament where we invite the strongest trainers to compete, with the exotic landscape and wildlife as a backdrop. We're going to bring civilization back to Palpagos Island."

"The fact you're civilized is exactly why you should be afraid to go against my army. We don't have such a weakness," Marcus threatened.

"Colonel Dryden I'm surprised you see it that way, considering you've previously met me," Archer spoke up confidently. "Civilization doesn't mean you don't know how to wield a spear. It just means you know how to smile at your enemy before stabbing them through the back."

Giovanni turned to Marcus. "Explain," he said, "Why are you against developing the island? Development brings profit."

"You're the only one getting the profit!" exclaimed Marcus. "What do you see us as, your own personal money-making Mozzarina?"

Giovanni glanced over to Archer nonchalantly, who translated, "Cash cow."

Giovanni leant towards Marcus, and looking him straight into the eyes said, "I am making an effort to be nice, which you are undeserving of. Get off my island or face the consequences."

"How dare you speak to me in that manner!" shouted Marcus, "What makes you think you can do that?"

"I own the island."

"You can't legally own an entire island," he countered.

"I purchased it legally and officially from the planetary council. They have little interest in trying to manage developing a third-world holdout with the myriad violations of human rights you purport as typical here; so little interest, in fact, they were more than happy to relinquish this whole tiny region to me."

"Well, one thing is paperwork. Another thing is reality…and that's one of the things we value on Palpagos Island – crude reality. I don't give a damn what documents were signed on the mainland. I'm going to put it bluntly, Mr. Delavita," said Marcus, hardly able to hide his seething, "You're on my island."

Giovanni snapped his fingers and instantaneously, the Team Rocket minions standing behind him pulled out guns and pointed them decisively at the PIDF soldiers. Marcus' eyes showed sudden fear but it was not until Giovanni pulled out his own gun from inside his suit that the emotion became outright shock.

Giovanni aimed it directly at Marcus and then with a swiftness that displayed years of experience, moved his wrist and shot at the soldier standing to Marcus' left. The man stumbled backwards and fell lifeless to the ground.

There was momentary silence and Giovanni spoke:

"You're on my island. I rule. Team Rocket now requires payment for the list of provisions and generosities we've allotted you."

Giovanni kept his eyes on the silent Marcus and extended his hand to one of his guards who produced a piece of paper upon which was written a lengthy list of items. The Team Rocket boss gave it to Marcus who read it over once and then looked back up at Giovanni.

"You've only just arrived here and you're demanding we pay you money for the privilege of hunting game on private land," he said adding, "for having built towns here, and for protection?"

"You know how to read, I see."

"And this," added Marcus with indignation, "Retroactive compensation for manufacturing Pal Spheres without your approval?"

"Considering I own all major manufacturers of Poké Balls, I'm doing you a favor by overlooking the fact you're essentially an unlicensed competitor in the market."

"You really think you can just show up and flaunt power and have me submit?"

"I'm doing you another favor," added Giovanni icily, "by not killing you right now."

"Fuck you. I'll have it all," responded Marcus, and without waiting for an answer turned sharply and left, as his men gathered up the body of their dead compatriot and followed him.

Giovanni put away his gun, turned to his associates and announced, "Interesting how there are still unreasonable people in this world." He then turned specifically to Jessie and James and ordered, "Keep everyone on training schedules… War approaches."

They didn't have to wait very long for the war to start.

Archer was minding his own business along the beach when there was a flash of light, and what should appear before him but a cluster of Unowns. They squeaked a cheery greeting.

"You guys again! It's been a while," Archer returned their greeting, and then took a wary step backwards. "You'd better not be planning another surprise trip for me."

The Unowns squeaked and turned about in mid-air, reorganizing their positions to spell:

TOMORROW ATTACK DAWN

"...what?" Archer inquired, confused.

The Unowns, apparently deciding they couldn't be bothered to elaborate, surrounded Archer in a wide circle. He barely had time to react before there was a flash of light and he was once more teleported away.

Thankfully this time he didn't go far; they warped him to Giovanni's office on the yacht, and came along with him.

Giovanni was on the telephone. At a meow from Persian he acknowledged Archer and the Unowns with a cursory glance, but otherwise he was unfazed and seamlessly continued the conversation he was in the middle of as if nothing out of the ordinary had happened.

Archer fidgeted, wondering if he ought to step out, but an adamant squeak from one of the Unowns made him conclude he ought to stay put – otherwise they'd just zap him back in here, as easily as one might recall a rambunctious young Pokémon to their Poké Ball.

It returned uneasy recollections of past experiences, but at least he knew these little creatures bore him no ill intent, even if they were mischievous beyond his liking. He tried to push his bothersome memories away.

From what he deduced, whomever Giovanni was talking with was on Kanto's Pokémon League commission.

"...naturally there will be some overlap with the main League challenge when it comes to viewership, so I intend for the Palpagos Island competitions to take place in the summer," Giovanni was saying.

On the other line, outside of Archer's range of hearing, the League commissioner sounded confused.

"Palpagos Island...?" he echoed blankly.

"The former wildlife sanctuary I own in the southern hemisphere," Giovanni elaborated.

It took a moment before he succeeded in refreshing the man's memory.

"...oh, right, that island. Everyone here has totally forgotten about that Pal-island place. Whatever happened with it; did you raze the town there already?"

"That's coming soon," said Giovanni with nonchalance, "but I want to get the League's official endorsement of our planned battle tournaments for when we open up to tourists."

"Oh, that'll be no problem. You know I'm always able to do a favor for my esteemed friend, Mr. Delavita," he hurried to say, trying to hide the fearful quiver in his voice.

"Then it's settled," Giovanni smirked knowingly, "I'll expect the Pokémon League's public endorsement of the event shortly."

A victorious Giovanni hung up the telephone and turned his attention over to Archer.

"Sir," began Archer, "the Unowns apparently have brought a message."

"I see they deem it urgent," observed Giovanni, with a glance at the Pokémon. The Unowns rotated about to spell the same enigmatic statement they'd written earlier:

TOMORROW ATTACK DAWN

Persian gave two or three meows and a chirp. One of the Unowns answered with a long conversation of chattering squeaks, and then Persian flattened its ears and turned to Giovanni.

One of Giovanni's many great qualities, Archer thought with admiration, was how he could understand the cat. Giovanni listened as Persian translated the Unown's message into meows, ending with a pointed hiss, and then the don gave a wily half-smile.

"Well, this will make the game interesting," he replied. Persian squinted and coiled its tail about its paws.

"What's going on?" asked Archer, who couldn't understand any of these animals.

"It appears Mr. Dryden thinks he can attack our encampment at dawn and wipe us off the face of our island," Giovanni said, turning to address Archer. "The Unown overheard it and, since they're both grateful for you helping them and – according to their own words – want to make Dryden's life miserable, they've come to warn us."

The Unown all squeaked in happy unison, glad that their message had been accurately conveyed.

"Time to show Mr. Dryden how Team Rocket functions," said Giovanni.

"Sir," said Archer, "don't we have the delegation arriving fairly soon?"

"Yes, we do. But I'm sure we can steer them away from any unfortunate occurrence while we deal with things," Giovanni dismissed. "They're supposed to arrive within a couple of days and should only be here as long as it takes for the necessary documents to be signed. Then no one can dispute our rule over this island."

"Yes sir," Archer replied.

"Also, I invite the Unowns to stay with us. Their alliance is welcome. I would say we should offer them something to eat but quite honestly I'm not sure what they eat. I'll ask Dr. Colress when he gets here; he'll be flying in around the same time as the delegation does to assist us with deciphering the weaponry schematics."

One of the Unowns twirled about and a few of the others squeaked cheerily. Archer gave them a skeptical look but said nothing. Better they be on our side, especially since they're troublesome little letters.

The Team Rocket camp was in a flurry of activity all night long, and when dawn arrived everyone was in their designated spot awaiting the presumed ambush by the PIDF. Colonel Dryden's group did not disappoint.

From where he was hidden, Archer could see their shadows coming up the trail and filtering in between the tree trunks. As they got nearer, he could see the soldier leading them wore the uniform of a PIDF lieutenant. A pity, thought Archer. I was kind of hoping Marcus would show up himself so we could thrash him. I guess he's not that dumb.

Before they were able to breach the encampment Archer gave a signal, and within moments the PIDF squadron found themselves not conducting an offensive but unequivocally on the defensive, having been quickly surrounded by enemy forces.

The Syndicate group were all aiming weapons far more advanced than even the machine guns their enemies carried, with their Pals right beside them growling with eagerness for the fight. Even if they could have possibly gotten through that line, standing behind the Syndicate as an ominous promise were countless Team Rocket agents with their own highly trained Pokémon and top-class weaponry.

"Didn't come prepared for trouble, did ya?" a feline voice taunted. The astounded lieutenant leading the invading forces turned around and found himself face to face with James, Jessie, and Meowth. They stood imperiously on a platform right outside the encampment, a gleam of murder in their eyes and a bazooka pointed straight at him.

Archer made his way through the squadron of Team Rocket minions to stand in front of the lieutenant; the Team Rocket admin could see at that moment the whole PIDF squadron had realized how outmatched the fight was and that they were going to get obliterated.

He suppressed laughter under the subtlety of a smile. "You can turn back, and tell Marcus Dryden to start making arrangements for his funeral...or you can come in, and we'll hold yours now."

The crude simplicity of this threat made the lieutenant rethink the invasion. With an unspoken directive, the PIDF army meekly retreated.

Marcus was in his office. He'd sent his soldiers out to strike at Team Rocket's camp and was waiting to get word that his orders had been carried out. The day had dawned cloudy and promised rain. "Perfect to wash away the outsiders' bloodstains once my forces reclaim the beach from them," Marcus had said maliciously.

There was a knock on the door, and he looked up to see the lieutenant who had been sent out earlier to lead the invasion. The lieutenant saluted, and Marcus immediately beckoned him in.

"I trust the intruders are all dead or dying by now?" Marcus said.

The lieutenant drew in a breath, but proceeded to relate what had transpired. Marcus listened to it all without comment or outward reaction, and when the lieutenant had finished the account, the first thing Marcus said was:

"You ungrateful army of cowards."

The accusation was delivered with no scarcity of vitriol. His lieutenant fidgeted under his superior's scathing glare.

"Colonel, we would have been annihilated..."

"You should have called their bluff. Of all the inept decisions you could have made, this one makes us look like damned fools!" Marcus snapped.

In the midst of this conversation, another of the PIDF soldiers raced into the office. His face was pale with fear, and he saluted his commander briskly before blurting out:

"Sir, we have a problem. They've got the town surrounded."

Marcus whirled about to face him. "What?"

"Team Rocket and their Syndicate allies," the infantryman explained, nearly stammering the words with frightened urgency. "They've engaged us in battle and they're moving into the town perimeter. Our forces can't repel them."

Marcus turned back to his lieutenant, who was in a state of utter shock. "It's bad enough you failed in your orders, you inadvertently led them here!"

Before the lieutenant could even react, Marcus pulled out his revolver and shot him. He reeled back and collapsed to the floor, dead.

Marcus hurried outside with Faleris' Pal Sphere clutched in his hand. A thin drizzle was cascading down on the town square, which was beginning to form puddles, and all the townspeople had retreated inside their dwellings as if anticipating the worst. Distantly, from the far outskirts of the settlement, came the raging noise of a large-scale Pokémon battle alongside the shooting of rifles; the sounds melded together in a nondescript manner, till it was easy to be unsure which were gunfire and which were energy attacks.

He sent out Faleris, which glanced over its shoulder at him as he got on its back, as if asking where he'd like to go.

"The plasteel factory would be the safest place to hide right now," conceded Marcus, and the bird accordingly stretched its wings and took flight.

A short time after Marcus Dryden fled, the town was invaded by a horde of both Team Rocket and Syndicate members working in tandem. They killed the guards and took the whole town in a matter of minutes.

The townspeople were mostly quiet folks and submissive. The tales told them by Marcus' group, of the Rayne Syndicate being ruthless poachers and outlaws, had impressed heavily on them. However, they were also not particularly loyal to the old PIDF administration either; they were perfectly willing to bow their heads to whomever ruled so long as they could live in peace, and if the Syndicate and their evident Team Rocket superiors had no intention of slaughtering them – well then, they were all willing to hail Giovanni.

Giovanni settled in immediately to the PIDF's former headquarters, replacing their shield emblem with the Team Rocket tapestry and Faleris' gold perch with a gilded cat tree for Persian.

On this particular day, Giovanni asked for Zoe to be brought to his office. Archer arrived quickly with her and stood at attention as Giovanni asked her some questions.

Giovanni addressed Zoe first. "How many towns are there on this island?"

"Three," she replied, "but this is the biggest. Besides this one, there's Fisherman's Point and Feybreak Cove."

"...and how many soldiers does the PIDF routinely assign to defend these two towns?"

"Not many," Zoe considered, "though I don't know if they maintain hidden strongholds near them. Usually there's only a handful of guards at the town entrance."

"Very well," Giovanni said, "Thank you for the information. You may go on your way until I ask for you again."

As Zoe stepped out of the Team Rocket boss' office, Archer immediately leapt.

"Shall I organize a scouting party to investigate the towns ahead of attack?" He was always quick to grab any chance to impress his godfather and assist Team Rocket in the process.

Giovanni, contrarily, shook his head. "Archer, at ease. You know you don't have to be proving yourself all the time."

"Sir, it's not a holdover from—" and he cut off, a bit embarrassed.

Maybe it was an echo, deep in his mind, of that time he was held captive and being used as a pawn. Of being expected to accomplish everything or suffer torture. Of being told his life was useless otherwise.

"It's not," Giovanni acknowledged, snapping Archer's attention back to the moment, "Even before you were taken prisoner, you've routinely striven to do as much as possible for Team Rocket's glory...often to a fault. You're overworking yourself. I'll be sending detachments of lower-rank agents to scout out the other towns. ...Besides, I have a more important assignment for you."

The despondency Archer had been starting to feel immediately vanished as Giovanni went on:

"Marcus has something we want and need; he's not a reasonable man by any stretch of the imagination."

"So then, we would need to simply help ourselves to whatever," said Archer nonchalantly.

"Our goal is to sneak into his factory and steal the formula they're using for plasteel," Giovanni ordered. "Once we have that, Team Rocket can produce anything we want – from Master Balls to weapons currently in the realm of fiction."

"Are the weapons really that novel?" Archer remarked.

"Extremely," Giovanni emphasized. "In that, Colonel Dryden is right; it's something the mainland would be astounded by. According to our top scientist Dr. Colress, the schematics are for a new kind of laser weapon far more powerful than even a Pokémon's Hyper Beam. That said, with how small Dryden's militia is, I still think his invasion of the mainland regions, if it came to fruition, could be knocked down by sheer numbers...if not downright outwitted by the military strategizing they sorely lack."

"Either way it behooves Team Rocket to make those laser weapons first," concluded Archer.

"The plasteel factory is located somewhere in the moorland of Hypocrite Hill." Giovanni gestured to the map before him. "Scouts with bird Pokémon have been able to sight it from above, but it's in such a protected area that it would be impossible to attack by air. Because of this, we'll have to take precautions and approach the area stealthily."

A small smile passed over Archer's lips. "When do I set out?"

"Tomorrow," Giovanni affirmed. "You'll take some of our younger cadets, as well as Zoe and a few of her people with you. This will be the first major mission any of the Syndicate recruits go on...they could use the extra practice."

Chapter 18 - The Long and the Short of it ✅

Early at dawn, Archer and Zoe set out for the journey to find the plasteel factory, commanding a joint group of five Team Rocket and five Syndicate minions.

One of the Team Rocket minions who had come along was Archer's sister, Kris. However, she'd left both her Pokémon – Suicune and Eevee – back at the encampment. Once she'd heard the horror story about the enemy's 'Pal Essence Condenser' and how they would incinerate stolen Pokémon to power up their own, she quickly decided that her prized Suicune would be better off protecting the construction site from a possible enemy raid, and Eevee ought to stay behind as well to accompany its new friend Cremis; the white-furred Eevee was moody lately and kept hiding in cubbyholes around the base, or so Kris claimed.

Whereupon Archer drearily pointed out that she needed to bring at least one Pokémon along for protection, even if it was something as mediocre as a Ratatta or a Zubat. She dutifully grabbed a Chikipi from the coop.

"It seems we have two ways we can go," Archer said as he studied the map. "The first is the shortest, down this path, then we veer off when we get to the river and follow it till we reach our destination."

"And the second?" asked Zoe.

"The second way means cutting through the woods, past a gully that's located somewhere around here... That'll send us through the deepest parts of Verdant Brook, past Gobfin Turf, and finally to Hypocrite Hill." He hesitated and stared dubiously at the name, as if he still wasn't quite sure whether it was a typographical error.

"Seriously? We're better off taking the straightforward path," said Zoe. "The road has already been cleared, and there aren't many dangerous Pals in that area unless you deliberately pick a fight. The long way there, however, is full of hazards, and Hypocrite Hill is especially treacherous."

"Is that why they call it Hypocrite Hill?"

"No one remembers why they call it Hypocrite Hill."

"Of course they don't."

"It's supposed to date back to the island war; that's all anyone really remembers."

Archer was still scrutinizing the map, in particular the place called Gobfin Turf. "...What the hell is a Gobfin?"

"Land-sharks."

"What the hell is a land-shark?"

She seemed a little gratified to have discovered a species neither he nor any of the mainland people were apparently aware of in the slightest. "Once you see them, you don't forget."

"I know!" Kris chimed in, flipping out her Pokédex. "Is it this?"

On the Pokédex screen, there was a picture of a rotund little dragon with sharp teeth and a sharklike fin on its head. It read:

Gible
Type: Dragon-Ground
It once lived in the tropics. Gible attacks anything that moves, and it drags whatever it catches into the crevice that is its lair.

"God I hope not," frowned Archer.

"Gobfin are sort of like that..." considered Zoe, studying the image, "but they're not as cute."

Archer glanced at her, questioning. "You think Gible are cute?"

"They're cuter than Gobfin," Zoe replied.

"Okay...even more reason to take the short way to our destination. Short way it is," decided Archer.

As anticipated, the journey was relatively peaceful.

It was a straightforward trek across a wide forest path. The sun was shining and the trees were full of birdsong, though try as Archer might he could not determine what species was singing – it was a beautiful trill somewhere between the song of a Starly and a Taillow, and whatever bird it was had ensconced itself deeply in the foliage.

They actually saw very few wild animals, except for a few Lamball and a distant Mozzarina, all of which as Zoe had said kept to themselves and posed no danger to the travelling party. It actually reminded Archer somewhat of the peace of traversing routes back home, and it might have even been easy to forget an enemy army was out there somewhere, waiting for the right moment to launch an attack and turn the tranquil forest into a raging war zone.

None of their Pokémon seemed at all concerned by this, however. Frostallion in particular pranced ahead, evidently relishing that it was the mount of one of the squadron commanders, and every so often Archer had to gently pull back on the reins to keep it from trotting too far from the others.

When night fell, they set up camp in a secluded area of the forest, sheltered beneath a canopy of trees below one of the tall cliffs.

Several campfires were set up and some tents as well. Most minions were still awake since Team Rocket always had guards posted when they camped.

"Well, in any case, this seems like a good spot to stop for awhile and feed the critters."

They settled down in the grass to rest and let all the Pokémon out of their Poké Balls to feed them.

Frostallion, Rapidash, and the other large Pokémon they had as transportation grazed peaceably off to the side. The Leezpunk and Cawgnito belonging to the Syndicate tamers began running around and playing with the Raticate, Golbat, Grimer, and Liepard that were of Team Rocket, while some of the smaller animals sat beside their trainers.

Meanwhile, Houndoom trotted over to Archer with a stick it had found in the grass, tail wagging as it placed it at his feet and barked. He dutifully tossed the stick, and the dog spun about and raced after to snatch it in mid-air and promptly return for him to throw it again.

As the dog bolted after the stick for the third time, Archer glanced over at Zoe. She was reclining against a rock staring at the bonfire flames, deep in thought.

The flame-light flickered across Zoe's gentle features; especially those amethyst eyes, which caught the glow akin to the jewels they so effortlessly resembled. He'd never really stopped to admire her, at least not in this way. She is pretty, he thought.

She spoke, snapping him out of his brooding thoughts. "Is this sort of what it's like, journeying on the mainland?"

Archer blinked pensively. He'd almost forgotten when it was he'd mentioned how trainers elsewhere would go out collecting gym badges. His recollections now hearkened back to that night they'd travelled from the Syndicate camp to the town, and camped out beneath the openness of Palpagos Island's strange sky. Zoe smiled and added:

"I remember the tales you told me about how Pal tamers off the island travel from place to place, testing their skills against one another in friendly battles, and exploring the wilderness for fun... Come to think of it I don't ever remember voyaging through the island woods with the kind of camaraderie we have here, ever."

"Yeah it is," said Archer. "It's exactly like this...minus having to look over your shoulder for something that wants to eat you."

He looked awkwardly away from Zoe, glancing over to see his sister sharing pieces of her sandwich with the Chikipi sitting on her lap in a ball of feathers.

"Kris, is there any Pokémon you get that you don't coddle?"

"All Pokémon grow through friendship," she said with a smile. "I should think even more if you're calling them a Pal."

The Chikipi clucked and tilted its head to look up at her.

Archer looked dubious. "That Chikipi already knows Hyper Beam. I doubt it will learn anything stronger."

"Maybe it will evolve," said Kris.

Zoe had overheard the conversation and joined in. "No one has seen a Pal evolve on this island in a long time."

Even Archer now glanced at her with surprise. This bit of information was unexpected, and she elaborated.

"We kind of know they do..." Zoe told him, "it's just no one's really witnessed it. For instance there are large birds we call Penking that some say are the evolution of Pengullet, though an equal number of people say they're not related to Pengullet at all."

"They sound like they could be Empoleon," considered Archer, "the evolution of Piplup."

Zoe shrugged. "If you say Pengullet evolve on the mainland, I have to take your word for it."

"Well," interjected Kris, "even if this chicken doesn't evolve, I still like it." She gave it a hug.

This led Archer to point out the obvious. "You brought the Chikipi along so you wouldn't suffer if something happens to your pets. Now you're getting attached to it and are going to be upset if it gets grabbed by our enemies."

"I can't help it," admitted Kris, "I've always had an affinity for animals."

"Yeah, it's okay," Archer smiled; he was thankful that his sister had that sort of gift where most Pokémon naturally bonded with her, and decided not to pursue the issue.

Kris noticed the chicken was now trying to hide its head under a wing. "Are you sleepy, Chicki?" she asked it.

Then she looked up and noticed one of the Team Rocket minions, sitting a sort distance away. He was the one who had caught the Foxparks; his Pokémon had fixed its eyes intently on Chikipi.

"Your fox keeps staring at my chicken," Kris informed the minion.

"I think Foxparks is hungry," he replied, looking at the fire type.

Not waiting for a fight to begin, the fox flattened its ears and trotted off.

"It's interesting that Foxparks won't stick around. I know it's hungry but we can find some food for it to eat," commented Archer.

The topic of conversation turned to something else, and it was several minutes later they heard a commotion coming from inside the forested area.

Suddenly Foxparks raced back into the camp, ears flat and eyes wild. There was a crash as a tree toppled and they looked up to see one of the huge grass elephants.

Archer took one look at it coming towards them and grimaced. "Zoe, why does that elephant look pissed?"

The Mammorest slammed its hooves down and a shock wave exploded outwards from it, nearly knocking them down in an Earthquake attack. Kris gave a frightened outcry and a few of the Syndicate minions reached for their weapons.

"I told you not to bite the locals!" exclaimed the Foxparks' trainer.

"Let's get out of here!" shouted Archer. They wasted no time; they all mounted their Pokémon and ran away as fast as they could. The ground shook as the massive beast galloped after them.

The chase sent the small group weaving through the forest, underbrush snapping and trees crashing down behind them as the furious Mammorest kept in pursuit. Just as suddenly they found themselves at a narrow rope bridge suspended across a steep ravine.

"Across the bridge!" cried Zoe, and they all hurtled over the bridge.

For a rope bridge, it was surprisingly sturdy. They had gone halfway across when the Mammorest reached the bridge as well.

Too large to get across the narrow way, the elephant swung its head and unleashed spinning leaves that sliced through the air above them. It barely missed hitting the bridge, which swayed.

"We're going to fall!" someone shouted.

"Foxparks, use Flamethrower!" its trainer ordered, holding out the fox.

"Wait...!" Archer tried to halt him, too late.

Foxparks opened its mouth; fire blazed from its jaws towards the Mammorest. The elephant trumpeted in pain as some of the flames seared against its hide, and backed away.

The flames also hit the rope holding up the bridge.

"Go!" Zoe said, pushing at everyone to race the rest of the way across the bridge. They made a run for it and reached the other side, right as the burning rope snapped and the bridge crumbled into the ravine.

They all clustered breathlessly on the other side of the ravine. The angry Mammorest raised its trunk and trumpeted noisily but couldn't reach them.

It was Foxparks who broke the silence, giving a little yap and tugging at its trainer's sleeve. "Guys...Foxparks is still hungry."

"Okay, so long way it is," decided Archer.

With no further fanfare he motioned to the others and walked away from the cliff.

The small group of Team Rocket and Syndicate members spent so much time running away from the elephant that by the time they were able to shake it off, the sun rose. Archer was angry.

"This is ridiculous," he said with an exasperated voice, "There's no way to find a good location at this point to make another camp, plus it's not wise to keep walking because we'll fall victim to exhaustion, and a warrior is not as effective or efficient if he's exhausted...so here we will stay for a few hours until we recover."

Everyone nodded. They were tired, and what Archer said made perfect sense.

After a few hours of napping, Archer gave the signal to regroup and they set out again.

Soon they came to a rise overlooking a marshland, with thin waterways peeling through mangroves and muddy sand. The land seemed barren of animals.

Archer was about to give the order to head forth and cut through the marshes, when Zoe held him back.

"That's Gobfin Turf," she said, motioning down to the marshland.

Archer gave the landscape a second look; perhaps because he'd been so used to Gible living in rocky terrain, he had presumed Gobfin Turf would be full of caverns. Seeing it now, this was worse. Marshlands were notoriously difficult to fight in.

"I don't see any Pokémon down there," he observed tentatively.

They descended the cliffs with ginger steps. Zoe and the rest of the Syndicate group were especially on high alert, while Archer, Kris, and the rest of the Team Rocket agents uncertainly watched the landscape around them as they walked. They weren't quite sure what they were supposed to be looking for.

It was Archer who first caught sight of it – a faint disturbance on the water, like a gust of wind when there was none. As he stared at the rippling spot, he was met with two shining eyes beneath the murkiness of the water that were fixedly staring back up at him.

He jumped back at the same time as the creature vaulted out of the water, snapping to bite him. Just as suddenly, he heard a cry from some of the squadron ahead also faced with belligerent wild Gobfin, and bursts of light flashed across the marsh as mainland Poké Balls and island Pal Spheres all opened at once to send out their pets for the fight.

Gobfin were everywhere. There were dozens of them; snarling, savage beasts with the fins and teeth of Sharpedo and the bulky forearms of Machop. Their Pokémon were knocking them out, but for each one that fainted more kept coming in waves.

Archer clenched his teeth as another one lunged for him and his Houndoom tackled it back. "Most wild Pokémon would've backed down by now. These things don't quit!" he exclaimed.

"We're not going to make it to the other side of the marsh," Zoe shouted at him from across the way, where she was commanding her Pengullet to strike enemies with its ice attacks. "There are too many of them."

"I've had enough of this," Archer declared. He raised his rifle and shot three of the Gobfin dead.

This now diverted the creatures' attention, and attracted by the scent of blood they all sprang on their fallen cohorts. They're like damn piranhas, he thought with disdain.

"Retreat!" cried Archer.

They all raced back the way they had come and ended up back on the precipice, watching the Gobfin tear into their meal.

"Is there any other way to Hypocrite Hill?" Archer asked, glancing at Zoe.

"Go around Gobfin Turf? We'll lose another two hours," she said.

"It'll have to do," Archer said, and as he turned to go he noticed a minion of Team Rocket walking around with a very tame Gobfin.

Archer eyed him with obvious incredulity. "You caught a Gobfin? Why the fuck do we need a Gobfin?"

"Why not?"

"Oh for crying out....put it in its Poké Ball, at least until we're sure of the typical reactions it has!" Archer ordered, then turned back to Zoe and said, "Okay, so we'll go around Gobfin Turf, and as soon as we get back to camp, I'm going to advise Giovanni to consider paving over this damned marsh and make a plaza or something."

Kris, who was nearby, chimed in cheerily. "I don't think the Gobfins will like that."

"Fuck the Gobfin. I don't like Gobfin. Fucking land-sharks." Archer waved his hand for the squadron to follow him down the path and without saying anything more he walked ahead.

They skirted the marshland, travelling along the cliff edge while keeping in distant sight of Gobfin Turf. At some point the trees began to grow thicker, and they moved away from the marshes and further into the deep cloak of leafy forest.

It was noon when they came to a wide clearing in the woodland with a statue of a Frostallion.

Frostallion had merely gotten one look of its likeness commemorated in stone and had straightened itself regally.

Archer lingered here. "So this must be the Frostallion statue you once told me about, commemorating their role in protecting the island."

"Yes, that's the one," Zoe replied.

"I guess no one remembers what the threat was that they were supposed to have repelled," he presumed.

"Only that they brought winter to fight it off," she said.

Before the conversation could go any further, they heard propellers overhead and Archer gave the signal for everyone to get out of sight. Everyone ducked into the bracken, including the animals, as an airplane passed by over the tree branches; it dropped a package, and went on its way.

"Looks like we might not get our hands on another mysterious delivery this time," said Zoe, from where she knelt beside Archer. She pointed down the trail. "Some people are coming."

As they watched, a cart drawn by two Univolt – or, as Archer saw them, green-and-yellow striped Zebstrika – came down the forest path. Archer could see the driver was one of the PIDF soldiers, and other soldiers accompanied the cart too.

The cart slowed to a halt in the forest clearing, and the soldiers quickly loaded the large supply chest onto the back of the cart; then one of the men in the group took a seat at the helm of the wagon and turning the horses around, set them off at a trot.

Seeing this, Archer motioned to his small squadron.

"We're following them," he announced, "I have a hunch they'll take us straight to the factory – and the plasteel formula."

Chapter 19 - Plasteel Factory ✅

The cart with its two Univolt kept to a quick trot along the main path, with the drivers scanning the road ahead and the trees close by, all too preoccupied to glance up at the hills where the small group of Team Rocket and Syndicate members were silently trailing them. Stealth had always been one of Team Rocket's strong suits, and apparently one that Zoe's Syndicate also effortlessly embodied.

It's a good thing they haven't noticed us yet, Archer thought, nevertheless, as their combined party followed the PIDF cart at a distance.

Before long they reached a clearing of flat land encircled by trees and low hills, and in the center they could see the factory building – a stone fortress enclosed by tall metal walls topped with barbed wire. Directly outside were two PIDF soldiers, and one of their trained Lamball behind a semi-circle of sandbags with a mounted machine gun.

Archer directed the group to linger in the cover of the trees, and they were able to spy on the goings-on below. The cart drew up to the factory building, whereupon the drivers pulled back on the Univolts' reins to halt them and then dismounted, with some words spoken to the posted guards that were completely out of hearing range of the Team Rocket observers. The PIDF soldiers took the supply drop chest down from the cart and went inside the building.

"Okay," said Archer, glancing at the minions, "Zoe and I will be infiltrating the factory. You fight any soldiers that run outside and make as big a show as you can. Wait for the signal; you'll realize when."

He motioned to Zoe to follow him, and they crept along the edge of the cliff away from the others till they had an angular view of the site with a direct line through the tree branches at the guards. Archer knelt down behind a rock, and Zoe crouched beside him.

"What's the plan?" she asked him.

"Pick them off one by one like Venonat," replied Archer, scrutinizing the soldiers below through the scope of his gun. He directed Zoe's attention to them. "Watch this."

He aimed directly at the guard standing to the left and fired, killing him instantly. The second guard only had time to turn in confusion before Archer aimed at him too, striking his mark perfectly.

Noticing what had happened, the Lamball started bleating and waving its hooves as it hopped up and down frantically. A small group of other PIDF soldiers rushed out at the creature's alarm, and with a motion from Archer his waiting squadron of Team Rocket and Syndicate minions gave a war-cry as they sent out all their Pokémon to the attack.

Archer smirked to see the ensuing fray and hopped down from the cliff, keeping close to the trees. "While they're amassing their forces at the front, we sneak in the back, get the formula for the boss, and we all get out of here."

They hurried soundlessly to the edge of the fence and Archer motioned to the barbed wire. "Houndoom, melt that for us."

Houndoom sent forth a furry of embers towards the twisted metal strands. They melted down easily into smoldering liquid, and he glanced at Zoe.

Zoe had already sent out Pengullet, which at a motion from her shot its ice attack at the mass; the metal cooled instantly in a burst of steam. From there it was an easy matter to get over the fence and sneak in through the main entrance while the guards were trying to fend off the intruders in battle.

The lighting here was uniform and modern. As Archer proceeded swiftly down the path, Zoe and the Pokémon right beside him, he glanced up to see long, fluorescent lights had been placed on the ceiling.

"Looks like this is one of the few buildings on the island with electric power," he observed.

Zoe was worried about the minions they'd left outside. "Do you think our people will be able to hold up against Marcus' men?"

"They've all been well-trained. Besides, they're a distraction; they can bolt if they start losing the battle because they're not really trying to get in. Infiltrating is our job," Archer added, his blue eyes glittering.

They emerged to a vast room that was the factory. A number of large red oil tanks had been placed on either side of the room; Archer and Zoe quickly hid behind one of them to watch.

There were many people and animals alike here, gaunt figures that unquestionably kept their eyes down as they shuttled tumblestone, gold and crude oil from one end of the room to the other, forced to toil ceaselessly to blend them together.

They were gathering the first two items in a furnace, kindled by the fire type creatures, and producing solid bars that shimmered like platinum. A conveyor belt of some kind lay to the far side, feeding these ingots into a grinder. The fine shards were then blended with the crude oil, and the resultant mixture was being refined further, to at last produce sheets of a nondescript material that Archer surmised was the elusive plasteel.

Supervising the entire operation were many stern PIDF soldiers and a few Direhowl, which kept a firm watch on their captive laborers. Oppressive heat from the machinery and furnaces hung over the room, creating a worse sauna than that of the tropical sun outside, with a couple of large fans blowing the hot air around aimlessly in a pointless endeavor. A long table to the side held various Pal Spheres scattered across it, and was guarded by one of the soldiers. On the wall beside the table hung a long blade somewhere between a machete and a butcher's cleaver.

As far as the animals went, there were plenty of Lamball here, as well as several Lucario with coarse brown fur, Petilil adorned in lava instead of leaves, navy Espurr with a particularly jaded expression, Gogoat with berries trimming their grassy pelts, three-tailed Ninetales that looked partly crossed with Glaceon, and a few light-blue dragons Archer couldn't place but had the slim necks and delicate faces of Ampharos. I'll probably figure out something better to compare them to if I think about it, Archer thought.

"Anubis, Flambelle, Depresso, Caprity, Foxcicle, and Elphidran," Zoe rattled off the names with ease. "Some of these Pals are the ones the Syndicate gave to Marcus."

"Obviously the ones he deemed strong enough to spare from zapping in that Condenser thing," Archer replied. "Where do you think they've got the plasteel formula written down?"

He caught sight of a large window overlooking the factory from a height; it was one-way though, and he couldn't see what lay beyond it. Maybe there's a monitoring station or private office behind that, thought Archer, That's probably going to be the likeliest place to look...

Archer heard a small gasp from Zoe, and he turned to see she had clasped a hand over her mouth and was gazing across the room. "All this time," she whispered, "I thought she was dead...!"

She pointed at a large cage they had to one side of the factory, which held a massive creature inside.

It was a giant Pikachu. Or at least, that was Archer's first notion of what it was; it was a bear as large as a Snorlax, with claws as long as a Zangoose, but it had the same short yellow fur and pointed, black-tipped ears of a Pikachu. Then again, maybe it was a closer relative of an Electabuzz. From this distance Archer couldn't be sure of that, though he could tell it looked disgruntled at being held in such tight quarters, to say nothing of hungry. The cage was wired to a electrical panel, evidently siphoning electricity from the Pokémon to use as a power source for the factory's electrical lighting and conveyor belt.

"It's my Grizzbolt," she said.

Archer considered the creature with skepticism. "Are you sure? I think that bear would just as soon eat us as it would be grateful if we let it out of there."

"Grizzbolt's a huge sweetheart," Zoe answered. "She wouldn't harm anyone unless I told her to. Those assholes, they've had her all this time and they've been mistreating her. I guess Marcus was lying about having thrown Grizzbolt in the condenser; instead he's using her here like a battery. We've got to get her out of there."

Suddenly there was shouting in the island language, and they glanced over. One of the animals carrying tumblestone had tripped from exhaustion and scattered its cargo across the floor.

At a directive from a guard, a Direhowl pounced to seize the unfortunate Lamball in its jaws and roughly hurled it against the wall, where it struck with a pained squeak. The Direhowl's trainer pulled the blade from the wall and slammed it down, embedding it on the table as a plain threat. The working creatures all cowered and even the people seemed to shrink back.

From their hiding place, Archer and Zoe observed.

"We should find a way to rescue these people, too," Zoe whispered.

Archer squinted. "Maybe your stolen Grizzbolt is one thing, but there's nothing we can do for the rest. We're here for one reason only – to find Giovanni's plasteel formula, not to liberate Marcus' prisoners. One of the first rules we have in Team Rocket is not letting your feelings get the better of you."

Even as he said this, he was silently evaluating the crowd. He observed one of the people at the conveyor belt who had been pulled aside by one of the guards, begging for their life.

The guard shouted some kind of abuse in response before pulling out one of the antique blue Poké Balls. As Archer watched, the prisoner was recalled to the capsule; the guard then walked over to the table, throwing one of the Pal Spheres there to the floor and sending out some other person to work instead. The new person didn't dare protest, immediately taking up the vacant spot.

Archer saw all this, and it was all he'd needed to see. Aversion and dark memories made his body tense, and in the same instant he forgot what he'd been saying but a moment ago and let his feelings get the better of him.

"Change of plans," he decided. "We're finding a way to rescue these people."

From a private office that rose above the factory floor, Marcus could see everything that played out below if he so desired. A sprawling window overlooked the workplace, and an intercom system allowed orders to be given from here. For Marcus it was routine, though he usually left the onerous job of monitoring the plasteel manufacture to his subordinates.

For Mrs. Jett Silph, however, it was the first time she'd been here. Gazing down at the factory from where she stood at the window, she watched the human and animal captives at work with dismay. On her shoulder, Tanzee was munching on a berry, completely indifferent to any of it but happy to be back with its tamer.

"I can't possibly agree with this," said Jett, turning to Marcus. He was pouring out drinks for them both from a liquor decanter on his desk. "It's unneeded cruelty. Pokémon and humans were meant to have close bonds with each other and live in harmony."

"Exactly the same sentiment that makes me certain the average trainer living on your mainland regions would be easy pickings on Palpagos Island." Though Marcus shook his head with disapproval as he said this, it was spoken as an observation and not in a bad way. "You can't stomach the concept of survival."

"Survival? This is not about survival!" Jett exclaimed. "You told me you were recruiting help to work the factory, not that you were enslaving them!"

"So in your view, basic human rights should be upheld above all things?" Marcus lifted his eyebrows offering her a drink.

"Oh I don't care about the humans you have here," Jett scoffed, as she took the glass from him. "You can starve and shoot them at dawn for all I care. But those poor Pokémon...! What you're doing here makes Team Rocket look like good people. From what I understand, at least they're feeding the Pokémon working on their construction site back at their encampment."

"How do you think your late husband managed to produce at low cost?" Marcus countered. "You can have either cheap or humane. The Silph Company did not grow into a household brand by being humane, even if they were less than honest about where they sourced their materials from." His features contorted into a wry sort of smile. "Even in your world...it's survival of the fittest, darling."

Jett started to say something, but faltered. Her shoulders slumped, and she gazed at Marcus with resignation. "At least the Gogoat. I recognize those from the shuttle service in Lumiose; they're innocuous creatures."

"Gogoat...? Oh, the Caprity." His demeanor softened. "You'd like to remove them from the factory, I presume."

"If you could release them, I'd be so grateful."

"Very well," conceded Marcus, "I'll see to it they're released. You have my word they won't suffer here anymore."

Jett smiled with appreciation; she took a sip of her drink and laid it aside. "Then we come to the matter at hand. You still haven't paid me for the supply drops."

"Yes," conceded Marcus tentatively.

"...and you certainly never told me anything about the fact that Team Rocket was here."

Marcus pursed back a scowl. He hadn't wanted to tell her at all, but when her yacht arrived at Fisherman's Point and she was informed that his current office at the main settlement was no longer accessible, and therefore if she wanted to speak with him in person she'd have to visit the factory...it was enough to make her ask questions, and he wanted to avoid her learning the answers herself.

As soon as she'd arrived at the factory, he divulged the whole problem about the meddlesome castaway, who apparently was a Team Rocket agent all along, and who had brought his allies to overtake the island. Her features had blanched the moment he'd admitted that, and even now there remained a semblance of deep worry in Jett's eyes.

"They're brazen, coming here to try to take over our small, independent island when they have it all already," Marcus said to her, incensed. "We'll have to divert our attention from more important matters to fend them off."

"Fend them off? Don't tell me you've starting waging all out war against them."

"You don't expect me to relinquish my territory?"

Jett was more concerned about a different matter. "Stirring up a war against Team Rocket is having a death wish. I'm from the mainland, Marcus; I know firsthand. That's how my husband died."

"If the planetary council is so inept as I hear they are, then there shouldn't be that much of a concern."

"Taking on the planetary council is not the same as taking on Team Rocket," she said emphatically. "When I speak of the council I'm referring to people more entertained by the status quo. Team Rocket in contrast wants a monopoly, in anything and everything they do."

Marcus crossed his arms pensively as Jett went on:

"The council have established a precedent for mediocrity in the past few years. The leadership have their own views on how our world should be run. They're loathe to take outside opinion, and when they do they half-ass it to fit their own standards."

"Then I should think for that alone the mainland regions should be easy to take over."

She gave a complacent shrug. "The problem with the mainland, to be fair, is the population can't be appeased anyway.
