Everyone wants something different, everyone gets excited when the leadership announces something new, and when it fails to meet up to each person's imagination everyone comes together to complain about it. There's a strange sort of unity in that, anyway."

"Your mainland leaders want to pretend their world is a utopia," replied Marcus. "There is no utopia, not in the real world anyway."

Jett sighed. "As I've said, there should be no problem with attacking the mainland. So long as you start your invasion at the south-eastern side of Lumiose City."

"You're quite emphatic about that," he observed.

"It's the weakest point." She didn't elaborate. "But Team Rocket – that's another beast altogether."

Marcus shook his head slightly. "Don't worry about Team Rocket. I'll wrap things up here and as soon as my people can get the weaponry developed, I'll make sure our plans are placed back on target."

Recalling Tanzee to its Poké Ball, Jett opened another sphere to send out her Clefable. "That's acceptable. I really must be returning to the Kalos region. There's still a lot of work to be done on the land developments, and my absence would be noticed," she replied, and turned towards her Pokémon. "...Clefable, teleport us back to the dock at Fisherman's Point."

Clefable gave a cheery cry, and swung its paws to and fro; Marcus said nothing as both Jett and the fluffy pink Pokémon were whisked out of the office in a flash.

The moment they'd teleported away, however, he addressed one of the soldiers. "Tell the workers they'll have to double their labor. And inform the guards we'll be having a special dinner back at the town square tomorrow of herb-roasted Caprity."

Meanwhile, Zoe was determined to get her Pokémon back; now that she saw it was alive there was no way she would just turn around and leave it.

She crept up to the cage. The electric type animal gave a small growl of recognition.

"It's me Grizzbolt," Zoe whispered. "Don't worry; I'll get you out."

Zoe picked at the lock as Archer and his Houndoom stood beside her as lookout. When she succeeded in opening it, Grizzbolt exited the cage putting its arms around her in a bear hug.

"Oh Grizzy, I've missed you too!" she said.

There was a shout, followed by Houndoom growling an alert, and they looked up to see a number of Marcus' soldiers running towards them. They had been discovered.

"Faint Attack," called Archer, and Houndoom leapt forward and tackled one of the enemy Direhowl. The two canines ended up in a snarling fight of fangs and fur.

"Get 'em, Grizzbolt!" Zoe shouted.

Grizzbolt roared, and slammed down its massive forepaws onto the ground. Electric arcs like lightning resonated outwards in a shock wave, bursting up from the ground to collide with their enemies.

A bolt of electricity fired sideways, striking the window of the monitoring platform headlong. Inside the office Marcus had to leap aside as the glass shattered completely.

The factory was cast into a tumult. Some of the prisoners seized the unexpected opportunity and struck out at the guards in a fight to snatch away weapons, and even the Pokémon working here now turned on their captors, snarling and unleashing their strongest attacks in a bid for freedom. Though weary and ill-fed, the thought of escape had an invigorating effect and bolstered the strength of sheer numbers.

Archer was contending with a number of enemies himself. He managed to shoot a couple of them but then his rifle ran out of bullets.

Unable to reload in time he turned about to club them with it; he hit one of the guards in the stomach but another punched Archer from the side and he stumbled, and in the ensuing fight the gun fell to the floor. Before he could retrieve it, one of the guards had grabbed the cleaver off the table and jumped at him. Archer found himself leaping back, trying both to evade the swordplay and find an opening to knock the weapon out of the soldier's grasp.

As the man lunged for him yet again, Archer succeeded in catching hold of his wrist. They fell backwards onto the conveyor belt, which proceeded uneventfully down the line as the two men fought.

They grappled viciously for the weapon, and Archer was about to steal it away when his enemy succeeded in wrenching his arm free and swung forcefully downward. Archer jerked aside; the cleaver slammed down on the conveyor belt inches away from his cheek.

His eyes then caught sight of what was coming down the line. They were moving towards a large entryway marked with faded yellow and black hazard stripes. Sharp blades rotated in the center like a blender on its side, whipping at high speed in a cyclone of steel and wind.

Archer's breath caught in his throat. "Oh shit—!"

He kicked his opponent hard, and was able to signal to Houndoom. The dog pounced with a snarl and sank its fangs into the enemy's arm, embers flickering at the edges of its mouth; the man cursed at the Pokémon loudly yet inadvertently loosened his grip on both Archer and the weapon.

Archer managed to snatch the cleaver away and tumble off the conveyor belt with Houndoom bolting after him, right as the soldier looked up. Realization flashed in his eyes but his shout was quickly torn apart, in both a figurative and literal sense; a warning indicator on the side of the contraption lit up in bright green.

As Archer sprang back to avoid getting soiled, the sound of beating wings and an overhanging shadow made him look up. Above, he saw Marcus riding on Faleris' back.

Marcus clicked his tongue in amusement. "First the essence condenser, now my disassembly conveyor? You have the most inventive ways of disposing of your enemies, even if they leave a frightful mess."

Archer didn't bat an eye. "Then I guess I'll see you in hell."

He hurled the cleaver in the air, straight towards Marcus. The blade hit against an energy barrier protecting him and fell anticlimactically to the ground.

Archer grimaced; he'd forgotten about the energy shield.

Marcus grinned smugly as he stared down at him. "I've got a better idea. Why don't I bring hell here?"

Faleris craned its neck back as Archer pulled Houndoom down beside him and they hit the ground as a blast of fire roared overhead, colliding with one of the red oil tanks across the room. A tremendous explosion rocked the factory floor, and an alarm began to blare as the massive iron doors began closing. Yells broke out from guards and prisoners alike caught in the blast.

Archer whipped around just as Marcus urged Faleris onward, hanging on tight as the giant hawk screeched and flew past in a streak of fire. The bird angled sideways to escape outside as the main doors slammed shut.

Archer snatched up the Poké Balls from the table and with Houndoom by his side, he raced to join Zoe with her Grizzbolt, and all of the other people and animals who were clustered at the blocked exit. They were desperately attempting to break out before the fire reached the rest of the crude oil tanks.

Try as they might, they were unable to force the doors open. Even many of Marcus' soldiers, forsaken by their leader to die with the prisoners, were trying to help to no avail.

"The damn doors are locked tight!" said Archer through gritted teeth. "If we don't get out soon, this whole place will blow up like fireworks."

"Maybe there's another exit?" Zoe proposed. Yet looking around the now decimated factory it was clear that there was only one way in or out, and it was the currently locked passageway.

The flames were carrying closer to the other oil tanks.

Meanwhile, Archer was thinking fast. "Remember what we did to cross the barbed wire?" he said. "We're going to do something like that...it's an old trick we've got in the Kanto region."

He motioned to Houndoom. "Hit that door with the strongest Inferno attack you can make," Archer told it, and the Pokémon howled affirmation before sending forth a wave of fire. As Houndoom let loose fire attack after fire attack, Archer turned to the lava-coated Flambelle standing in a cluster to the side.

"We need your help. We have to get this as hot as we can," Archer told them.

The Flambelle squeaked and hopped over to stand beside Houndoom, and soon all of the fire types present were attacking the door. Flame surged against the metal, till it was glowing red hot. Upon seeing this, Archer opened Frostallion's Poké Ball, and the ice type Pegasus emerged flapping its wings and neighing.

"Frostallion...and any ice or water types we've got here," he raised his voice, directing his attention to the crowd. "Use your ice attacks and aim right where the fire hit."

Frostallion reared back and unleashed a powerful ice beam. Zoe's Pengullet joined in, and the group of Foxcicle as well, blasting the door with ice and producing a cloud of steam.

When he heard the metal cracking, Archer felt a surge of elation, but a second explosion of an oil tank behind them made many of the animals leap up with startled cries and brought the urgency of the situation back to the forefront. "Now, Zoe, use your Grizzbolt to break this open," he urged.

"Grizzbolt, go!" yelled Zoe, as Grizzbolt gave a mighty roar, and slammed its whole body against the door. The metal creaked.

"Come on," muttered Archer, desperate. "It's got to have weakened enough by now..."

Grizzbolt hit against it again, and again. Finally there was a crash as the metal gave in and burst apart, allowing everyone to escape outside in a flood.

They ran for the forest's grassy slopes and when they were all at a distance, they saw the entire factory building explode in a ball of fire.

Archer led the squadron in cheers, and when the celebratory moment passed, Kris walked up to her brother, hugged him, and with a big smile on her face asked him:

"So Archer, let's see this formula we all practically risked our lives to get."

"Oh no," Archer said, growing pale, "Fuck!"

"What's going on?" Zoe asked as she joined them, "Is something wrong?"

"The formula!" Archer exclaimed, "Zoe, do you have it?"

"No. I thought you had gotten it," Zoe admitted.

They all looked at the burning building that was practically reduced to nothing.

"All up in flames...gone," Kris said, "and the formula with it."

"How am I going to explain this to Giovanni?" Archer lamented.

No one knew the answer to that, so no one said anything. They stood there in silence watching what was left of the structure become a pile of ashes. At that moment one of the liberated prisoners came over.

"Excuse me," the man said speaking to Archer, "I was told you are in charge of this group?"

Archer nodded. "Yes," he confirmed, "My boss is Giovanni Delavita."

"Well, we just wanted to thank you...and your boss...for rescuing us," the man said, adding, "We'll never forget that you got us out of that hell hole."

"Good," Archer said, "Then if you're so appreciative, I want you to say it to my boss, so he'll understand how extremely difficult the whole process was. Maybe he won't be too angry we didn't get the secret formula."

"Secret formula?" the man asked.

"The secret formula for plasteel, which is used in the manufacture of the Master Ball and advanced weaponry," explained Zoe.

"We're so screwed," Archer mumbled.

The man heard him and answered, "Oh! Sir you have nothing to worry about, everyone held captive at the factory know the formula."

Archer, Zoe, and Kris all turned to look at the man directly, with surprised expressions plain on their faces.

"Are you kidding me?" Archer said, frowning, "Because if you are, let me tell you I'm in no mood for jokes right now."

"No joke," the man answered, "Dryden thought we would all die in captivity so he didn't keep the formula a secret, plus he had us all cross trained to do any chore needed...every week or so someone died so..."

"So he needed to be sure that everyone knew what they had to do," said a woman who had also been a prisoner.

Another prisoner joined in the conversation, adding, "We all knew a part of the process that was assigned to us, but we also were all aware of the entirety of the formula."

Archer smiled. "Well then," he said, "You will tell Giovanni, all of it."

Chapter 20 - Rise of the Syndicate ✅

When Archer, Zoe, and the rest of the squadron walked into the encampment with all the liberated prisoners, they found fainted Tocotoco strewn everywhere though the construction site was undamaged.

"Let me guess. Tocotoco raid?" Archer asked as soon as he saw Jessie and James.

"Exploding Xatu should fetch a fortune back home," Jessie said, tossing a Poké Ball at one of the birds. With the Tocotoco knocked out, the Poké Ball did not even shake, the indicator light merely flashing a few times before immediately registering the capture.

"No doubt. Any idea when the boss is going to ship out all the Pokémon we've caught?"

"He said he was shipping them out in batches of five," James answered, "starting tomorrow."

Jessie chimed in, "Opening the resort to tourists is on standby though, at least until the issue with Marcus is resolved..."

"One way or another," added Archer.

Meowth, meanwhile, had padded over to the large group of people and animals Archer had with him. "Looks like your squadron tripled in size," the cat yowled. "What is this, the whole factory workforce?"

"Oh, yeah. They all decided to walk out. Something about unsafe working conditions," Archer quipped.

"So long as they're not here to unionize the penguins we got finishing up our resort. The boss'll have a fit."

Archer waved the comment off. He turned to head on his way when he heard a moo and looked around to see a Mozzarina – the island's version of a Miltank – standing atop the newly finished annex to the hotel.

"Why is there a cow on the roof?" Archer ventured.

James shrugged. "It can't get down."

"It says it's hungry," added Meowth.

"How did it even get up there to begin with?"

"Chasing a squirrel."

"...never mind; screw this shit. Leave the cow there," Archer said, and steered the conversation elsewhere. "Where's Giovanni?"

"The boss is on the yacht." Jessie pointed towards the dock.

"Thanks," said Archer, and motioning to his group to follow left the trio and their wayward bovine behind.

Archer directed the crowd to an area of the encampment where they could get food and water, and while they rested he headed towards the dock.

He found the Team Rocket don in his office aboard the ship; Archer knocked at the open door to announce himself, and was immediately waved in.

"Good news, I hope," said the leader of Team Rocket.

Archer looked down at his feet. He was ashamed that the mission hadn't gone completely as planned. Persian prowled around the perimeter of the office incessantly, its keen eyes locked on Archer. He could practically sense it judging him with the same disapproval he was sure would be reflected in its master's eyes; nevertheless he glanced back up and told Giovanni everything that had transpired.

"Well we don't really need the factory, most of the laborers probably wouldn't want to continue working in a place that was basically enslaving them," Giovanni said, after Archer finished the account, "We can build our own, bigger and better."

"Yes sir," Archer replied.

Giovanni got up from his seat, put his hands in his pockets and continued speaking:

"Since the people you rescued all know the formula and procedures for this endeavor, it stands to reason that we are keeping them to do most of the manual labor; of course we will treat them better than Marcus did...and also," Giovanni glanced at Archer adding, "they are aware of the expectation regarding complete loyalty to Team Rocket?"

"Yes sir, I did have a chat with them earlier," Archer informed him.

"And, are they willing to be reasonable and cooperative, or will we need to employ more persuasive methods to get them to talk?"

"They're volunteering the information," said Archer. "No need to beat them up."

"Good. All the better," Giovanni replied. "We won't have to waste time."

"Sir, they are getting something to eat," Archer informed him, "Would you wish to speak with them now?"

"A little later," Giovanni said and glanced at Archer. "At the moment, I have urgent business for you to tend to in the Kalos region."

"Kalos?"

"Yes, Kalos. We were able to track down the originator of the supply drops from the starburst logo on the weaponry blueprints. Apparently, Marcus is getting his shipments from Quasartico Inc., the land development company based out of Lumiose City," Giovanni said. He had started pacing, as he did on occasion when he was analyzing something deeply. "Your mission is to find out who in the company is behind the supply drops and tell them on my behalf, that I now own Palpagos Island and those shipments to Marcus need to stop. If they decide to do business with Team Rocket at some point, that is another issue and we can discuss it at a later time."

"Sir...might I ask...what if they decline?" Archer saw Giovanni stop pacing and look at him directly, so he went on speaking, "Suppose whomever it is says they want to speak with Marcus first?"

"Nevermind about that," the boss replied, "just do as you're told. You will take Zoe with you...she is the link to the island and I'd like to know if she's ever seen the Quasartico person. When you finally speak with the person authorizing the drops, depending on what they say to you, will determine the next step Team Rocket will take."

"Yes sir."

"That group you've brought in must be finished eating and resting. Go get them and bring them here. Time they met their new boss." Giovanni said this and with a wave of his hand dismissed Archer, who quickly left the office.

Archer walked back across the beach, past the rooftop with the Mozzarina. He stopped briefly when he saw Jessie, James, and Meowth had pooled together a small cluster of minions to try to get a ladder up to the roof.

"Why don't you just recall it to its Poké Ball?" Archer asked them.

"It's not our cow," said Jessie.

"Yet," added James.

Archer stared at them incredulously. "You mean it's wild? Then why not throw a Poké Ball and make it our cow already instead of fucking around with the ladder?"

"That's not as fun," James complained.

"Oh, whatever. Where's Zoe?"

"I think she's off speaking with some of the folks from her group," Jessie said, gesturing to point him in the right direction.

Meowth gave a pointed yowl as Archer was starting to walk away. "Why don't you just admit that you like Zoe? It's no damn secret, everybody notices the way you look after her...and for that matter she looks out for you too!"

Archer turned back alertly. "What?"

"Why don't ya just tell her you like her already and see what happens?" the cat purred. "It's not like it'd be a big deal; you're already married."

"Very funny. You know that marriage was a matter of convenience for both of us, and in my case I didn't even know I was getting hitched," Archer retorted. "At any rate it's a one-sided thing. She's the leader of her group here on Palpagos Island, and I'm returning to the Kanto region when we're done with our job."

"Purrr-lease. That won't be the last of it. Every time I see you twos, you remind me of Jessie and James."

"Is that supposed to be a compliment?" asked Archer dubiously. Yet Meowth had already turned his attention back to the Mozzarina, leaping up to the rooftop to apparently reason with the stubborn Pal; meanwhile, both Jessie and James had snickered in response but said nothing.

Archer did find Zoe near the tents, speaking with a group of people from the Syndicate. I wonder what's going on? he thought, lingering at a distance.

"That's stupid!" Zoe was exclaiming to the leader of the small group, a man of about forty years of age, "If you don't ask for Giovanni's permission he's going to say you're committing insubordination!"

The group leader rolled his eyes. "We are fully trained now and it is our island... Look, I get it... your alliance is now with your husband, and you're using that to try to step away from your role as Syndicate boss, but we don't have that link. Giovanni's not our boss."

"You're wrong. Very wrong," Zoe insisted, "Listen to me. I've been around them much more than you...they demand no less than complete loyalty, and when you've proven yourself they'll protect you forever, but if you go against them..."

"You're wasting our time," the leader interrupted her, "Let's go everyone."

He turned leaving quickly with the rest of his group following him. Zoe watched as they all marched out of the campsite and felt a sudden surge of stress flood over her.

"He's always been stubborn," Zoe heard a voice behind her and turned to see an elderly woman who was from her tribe. "Hawk is my grandson, and he's always had a different viewpoint about our culture and how we do things."

Zoe sighed, "But this isn't about culture, this is about survival. Team Rocket has very strict rules of engagement when it comes to internal affairs."

The old lady shrugged her shoulders and walked away. Zoe decided to tell someone what was happening; she walked quickly in the direction of Archer's tent but as she was less than halfway there she found him looking on at the conversations she had been having.

"Anything new?" Archer asked diplomatically.

"Archer! I was coming to see you. A group of the Syndicate, being led by Hawk, is heading off to the tower," she confessed, "their plan is to ambush and take it over from Marcus' people."

"I haven't been informed by Giovanni that he gave the go ahead for that," Archer said. "He usually tells me those type of things."

"That's the thing," Zoe replied, "They didn't ask him. Hawk took it upon himself to plan it and talked a few others into it. All the Syndicate is not involved but I worry they'll be giving the rest a bad name."

"Come with me," he said, taking her by the hand, "We'll go see Giovanni right now. Only those involved will have to answer to the consequences."

When Giovanni was informed of what was happening he was not pleased; in fact he was very angry. On the boss' orders, Archer organized Team Rocket soldiers into two squadrons to bring back Hawk's group. Archer mounted Frostallion, while Zoe rode alongside him on Grizzbolt's back, and they led the way out of the camp.

They could see the Syndicate's tower with its glowing I insignia before they even neared it, the tall skyscraper relic standing sentinel over the island. Archer, Zoe, and their group reached a rise overlooking the clearing at the base of the tower, where they could see the rogue squadron that, having gotten there first, had immediately engaged with the enemy. A battle was already raging, with trainers and Pokémon alike embroiled in combat and little heed paid as to whether one's opponent was man or beast.

"Looks like they're losing big-time," commented one of the Team Rocket minions.

"Yeah well Giovanni didn't send us here to be their backup." Archer searched the violence-ravaged scene. "Do any of you see Hawk?" he asked.

"There he is!" yelled Zoe as she pointed him out with a couple of his men running away from the tower entrance.

Archer urged Frostallion forward, to fly down and land beside Hawk barring his way. Zoe joined him, her Grizzbolt's massive figure blocking off his other side.

Archer snapped at Hawk, "No one gave you authorization for this."

"We don't need authorization to reclaim what's ours," Hawk countered.

"Your orders are to abandon this fight at once," Zoe said. "You're being given the chance to do so willingly as a courtesy."

Hawk didn't respond, except to dart unexpectedly past Frostallion and race back to his ranks. Before Archer could order his Pokémon to attack them or order his squadrons on the hill likewise, the Unowns suddenly appeared.

They swirled around near Archer and Zoe and spelled out a word:

RUN

Archer's eyes quickly darted from the Unown to the tower, and to the flicker of motion and green feathers lingering near the bushes at the entrance.

He focused on the lone Tocotoco there, which was observing the fighting blankly, and his stomach plummeted with realization.

Where's the rest of the...oh shit.

"Run for it!" Archer exclaimed, right as several Selfdestruct explosions sounded, one after the other; a splinter of light shuddered up the length of the building, like the vertical leap of a Raikou, and just as suddenly the whole pillar came straight down.

Stones fell like a deadly hailstorm, and with it an oppressive cloud of dust. Everyone immediately turned to flee for their lives. Those Pokémon too small to carry their trainers brought forth glittering Protect barriers to shield them, while the rest tried to outrun or outfly the blast.

The tower had exploded. A bunch of Tocotoco birds had flown into it, or...had someone sent them in?

The Unown were flitting around and chirping, upset their tower had been decimated. They organized themselves to spell out the word DISASTER.

"They used that flock of Tocotoco like an implode unit," Archer grumbled. "Those bastards didn't give a fuck the building would come crashing down on their Pokémon."

From Archer, spite over this was perhaps an unexpected emotion. He had little affection for those exploding dodo birds, yet it still seemed unnecessary to capture a whole flock for this when the PIDF could just as easily have put conventional explosives, if destroying the tower was what they'd intended to accomplish. Or maybe it was the careless simplicity of how they threw away the lives of their servants.

Zoe meanwhile was staring at the vestiges of her family's heritage, the once imposing skyscraper now a forlornly crumbled pile of rocks and debris with a mist of ash still lingering in the air like a shroud.

"This tower had always been important to us," Zoe lamented, "so treasured by us that we protected it with our lives. It was a landmark here on our island for over a century. In little more than a minute, it's gone."

The folly of becoming attached to real estate, Archer thought, but he wouldn't have ever said so. He felt bad for Zoe; he could see how much it had meant to her, and he came over to stand by her as she gazed sadly at the rubble.

"I'm sure Giovanni will want it rebuilt," said Archer. "It'll be even grander, you'll see."

"Maybe, but it won't be the same," Zoe said, a bit hoarsely. She looked up at the rogue squadron standing by mutely, as well as their commander Hawk, and her hands tightened into fists.

"If you had followed orders," she told them bitterly, "if you had played by the rules... we would have planned for the enemy's every possible maneuver and avoided this! That tower was everything to our people; it was the symbol of what Dryden's regime took from this island, and if you'd only worked alongside Team Rocket instead of becoming as egotistic as a Penking this wouldn't have happened. It's your fault the tower was destroyed!"

"Better demolished than gifted away," Hawk responded, "Why else would we have sent those Tocotoco in?"

The world hushed, for none more than Zoe. She stared at him, only stared.

Hawk went on, as arrogant as ever. "It's time for a new rise of our Syndicate, which you're not going to bring. We've lived on this island for generations. Everyone knows the tower belonged to us – and only us! And you, a direct lineage of the Rayne family...you would have given it to the outsiders—"

"What outsiders?" Zoe retorted, cutting him off short. "The Syndicate and Team Rocket are the same! We always were the same!"

The ferocity in her voice stunned Hawk into immobility. Zoe's amethyst eyes now burned with violet fire no one had ever seen till that day, a transformation that shocked them all, especially when she whipped out a pistol and shot Hawk point-blank in his forehead.

He fell to the ground, dead. Zoe turned her fiery glare and the pistol on the rest of the squadron, and they all flinched back in anticipation. Archer, standing aside, hid a small smile.

"Is anyone else confused about their loyalties?" demanded Zoe.

"No, ma'am," one replied, having recovered his words, "you are the heiress of the Rayne Syndicate. You are our boss."

"No," she specified, dryly, "your boss is Giovanni Delavita."

Team Rocket marched their five prisoners back to the encampment and straight to the boss' office aboard the yacht.

In the office, alongside Giovanni, were his trusted guards James and Jessie together with Meowth. Archer and Zoe both saluted and as soon as the prisoners were placed before Giovanni, the other guards and their Pokémon who'd come with them exited.

"Report," Giovanni commanded.

"Sir," Archer began, "these are the traitors who went on the mission without your consent. Their leader, one called Hawk, is dead. Hawk destroyed the tower by way of Tocotoco explosion. It is in total ruins."

"Who eliminated the traitorous leader?" Giovanni asked.

"Zoe did so sir, and emphasized to these prisoners that you are their leader."

"Zoe, step forward," ordered the boss of Team Rocket.

Zoe took a step closer to Giovanni's desk. Her countenance was resolute and her demeanor courageous. "Tell me Zoe," Giovanni asked, "What prompted you to take action on behalf of Team Rocket's honor?"

"Sir, it's thanks to Team Rocket and your leadership that this island and its people are being liberated," she replied. "I want to be part of the new Palpagos Island."

Giovanni nodded his head approvingly. "You are a part of Team Rocket and have proven yourself to me."

The boss of Team Rocket then turned his attention on the five rogue Syndicate members before him. One of them opted to speak.

"If you want to know why we did what we did, it was only because..." began one of the prisoners.

Giovanni cut him off short.

"James," he said sharply, and the Team Rocket admin stepped to Giovanni's side at attention, "Explain to this dimwit what is wrong with his manner of address."

"He has not spoken with respect," James replied promptly. "He failed to refer to you as Mr. Delavita or Sir."

"Correct," said Giovanni, icily turning towards the now fidgeting prisoner. "Would you care to try again?"

The prisoner turned pale, then spoke again. "Sir... We were all following Hawk...who claimed he could lead our Syndicate best...he assured us that we had a right to do what we did, and we are all proud of our island, but..." He stopped here and swallowed hard then went on. "It seems we have offended you and for that I speak for all of us... we apologize sincerely."

"I accept your apology," replied Giovanni, "nonetheless, the fact remains that you all disobeyed orders. There will have to be punishment for this."

He turned towards his trio of guards. "James, Jessie, Meowth." As he called their names, they quickly stood before him and saluted.

"Take these prisoners to the camp center and execute them. Announce that by my order, this be an example of what happens when some decides to get out of line without my express permission."

The prisoners' eyes widened with incredulous fear, and the one who'd been speaking before now blurted out, "You can't do this...!"

Giovanni smirked. "This is my island. I can do whatever I want."

James and Jessie surrounded the five prisoners and ushered them out of the office at gunpoint, with Meowth growling a warning in case one of them should try to flee.

The procession towards the center of the campsite was a new sight to the Syndicate people. When they saw a group of their own being handled as prisoners, many became afraid. That however, was part of Giovanni's plan. The boss of Team Rocket wanted to make this execution as public as possible to scare the new recruits of Team Rocket to the point that they would not even consider turning against them.

The whole thing was very fast. The prisoners were lined up against a wall that belonged to the hotel building they were constructing. Shots rang out and were heard for at least two miles in the surrounding area.

Every time Jett had visited Palpagos Island in the past had been calm and uneventful, and if the island had not been so primitive and underdeveloped she might have even considered it a good spot for a holiday.

This time was a little different. Jett remained inside her yacht and only gingerly peered out of the windows, concerned about Team Rocket seeing her. She told herself she had nothing to be afraid of; Team Rocket's conflict was with Marcus, not her.

She glanced over at the three Pokémon she had aboard ship with her: Pansage, Clefable, and Furfrou. Her Pokémon, at least, gave a distraction from her numerous worries.

"So Pansage, or is it Tanzee? ...You seem to prefer the name Tanzee now, I see," she observed, as the monkey cackled and swung about with its tail.

"All right, you can be Tanzee for now. It's only for a little while longer anyway," Jett added, "I'm buying the finest Leaf Stone from the boutique back home so you can evolve into a Simisage."

The monkey hopped up and down shrieking gleefully; if it liked the name Tanzee, it evidently liked the idea of evolving even better.

In the midst of this there was the sound of beating wings, and she saw a shadow descend beyond the window. She pulled back the drapes to see Marcus stepping down from Faleris and recalling the bird to its capsule.

He looked somewhat dishevelled, and obviously exhausted. He no sooner stepped into where she and her Pokémon were waiting than Jett exclaimed, "Marcus! What happened to you?"

"Team Rocket made another unannounced appearance," he divulged. "They burnt my factory to the ground."

Jett went pale. "Had I stayed there but a little longer, they would have seen me. ...I need to get back to Lumiose as quick as I can."

"You do that," said Marcus, "I'll be hard to reach for a few days, at least till I can gather my forces and assemble the weapons we need to invade Lumiose."

"You already said the factory was burnt to the ground."

"I never said I would be the one to assemble them," Marcus replied. "If my hunch is right, Giovanni won't resist being able to make those weapons for himself. He already has the first set of schematics his people stole from us."

"What good will that do?" Jett said vehemently. "Then he'll have both the island and the weapons."

"Not if I play my cards right," said Marcus grimly. "I've got a secret weapon in play that'll put them all to shame."

Jett studied him blankly and he thought he may have spoken too much, however he soon realized that she hadn't interpreted the remark correctly when she said, "I know your Faleris is a high level, but I think you might be overestimating your Pokémon's attack strength just a little bit. Team Rocket owns at least a couple of legendaries, from what I am told."

"Faleris' attack power rivals Legendary Pals," Marcus replied, deciding to uphold the ruse, "and it's a naturally fast flier as well. Anyway, I'll find a method to contact you as soon as I can."

With that, he bid farewell and left the yacht, and Jett departed for the Kalos region soon afterwards. She was starting to regret her little plan for Lumiose; if Marcus was having these constant setbacks, and now Team Rocket was getting involved, then maybe trying to get those buildings on the south-eastern side of Lumiose forcibly demolished was becoming more trouble than it was worth. She already had the urban redevelopment contracts. Maybe she was asking for too much.

No one from Team Rocket saw the ship sailing away.

Chapter 21 - Lumiose City ✅

Archer watched the forest landscapes run swiftly by as the train made its way towards Lumiose City, with Zoe sitting in front of him and her pet Pengullet perched cheerfully on her lap.

Giovanni had sent them both on this mission, and Archer would never even entertain the travesty of disobeying his godfather. However, out of all the mainland regions he'd visited, the one Archer had always liked least was Kalos.

Kalos was beautiful in its landscapes, but it was a tailored beauty of meticulous gardens and baroque mansions, and the people, while charming and cultured, mostly upheld a kind of politics that basked in what was – at least in Archer's view – blatant hypocrisy. Then again Kalos had its own vibes; different vibes, compared to the rest of the world.

Over in Kanto there was an air of exploration, of going into the ferns and woods right outside the cities and seeing what you could find, and coming back either with three or four Rattata or tales of some scary beast lurking in the shallows off the Cinnabar coastline. In Johto it was similar, with the exception of cities being more traditional in their style, and the people bearing legends vague enough to carry the allure of untold mysteries hidden in some forgotten cavern – and you'd certainly find something if you pried around those pitch-black caves, though it probably wouldn't answer your questions.

Hoenn had secrets behind every rock and bush, it seemed, though no one really spoke about them, being too enamoured with the sea and the sun; and Sinnoh, well, Archer honestly hadn't been much to Sinnoh, but everyone he'd met who had spent some time there spoke of the region like it was just as marvelous as Johto. Unova was modern but still held mysteries and places to explore, although you probably wouldn't find anything worthwhile there unless it wanted to be found; however, bustling Castelia City and their famous ice cream parlor more than made up for it.

Orre meanwhile was his kind of place, sinister and practical, with money upheld as a strict priority among the inhabitants, all of whom were sly enough to keep up appearances unless you deliberately went looking for trouble. Hidden as oases in its forbidding deserts lay some of the most beautiful landscapes and impressive stadiums Archer had seen in his life; it was a shame few tourists went there, yet the few who did all spoke longingly of a return.

He was also aware of other regions too, countless others he hadn't yet visited for one reason or another, but which surely each held their own charm. He knew from Jessie and James about Galar, though from what they recounted it was a straightforward place with little wonder, and beautiful wild areas occasionally marred by scrawny trees. Business in Wyndon was always thriving and drew you in magnetically, but an average trainer without investments or holdings there might've felt like they were missing out on something.

Then there was Palpagos Island, which he wanted to view with disdain but couldn't anymore. It was as practical as Orre and as openly explored as Kanto, with the untold mysteries of Johto and the tropical sea and sun of Hoenn one could be enamoured by at a glance. How could he despise a place that reflected everything he loved about home? All it was missing was a big city, and Team Rocket would build a city themselves.

But Kalos was going to be Zoe's introduction to the mainland. And as they stepped off the train and into the city, Archer was silently puzzling over the task ahead. He wanted to show her all that was wonderful about the mainland, a feat he imagined would be challenging here.

To his surprise, it turned out to be exceptionally easy.

"You can buy bread?!"

Archer looked at her blankly for a moment. "...yes?"

"But you don't understand, on the island you have to bake bread yourself! ...and that could take hours of your day! You mean here there's actually a merchant who devotes his entire business to baking bread and selling it to people?"

"That is a bakery."

"You have a name for it, too?!"

Maybe Kalos was going to be interesting this time around. One could hope.

The myriad trappings of modern life, which Archer saw as commonplace, were a source of fascination for Zoe. He'd seen her awe when Team Rocket first arrived on Palpagos Island, yet somehow he'd underestimated just how behind in contemporary knowledge the island people were. They knew of electric power and the like, but they commonly accepted that electrical appliances and technology were reserved only for the government in power or anyone clever enough to get their hands on it. With the way Archer had extolled the Team Rocket organization, Zoe could have been forgiven for believing Giovanni to be a king of some sort on the mainland and hence had his island encampment equipped accordingly.

To see such marvels now as streets filled with cars and well-stocked stores with central air conditioning and even automatic sliding doors – the latter amazed her enormously, for some reason – and that it was all available for the masses, was more than enough for Zoe to declare that the mainland was a jewel and screw Marcus for having kept all this from the islanders for so long.

Yet perhaps it was hard to hide his lacklustre regard for Kalos, because at some point as they were strolling down the sidewalk Zoe remarked:

"This isn't your favorite place, is it." She second-guessed herself almost instantly, and backpedalled, "I'm sorry, I shouldn't pry."

"No, it's not bad memories or anything like that," Archer replied. "Honestly it's politics. Kalos is a mess."

"How so?"

He tried to distract the conversation elsewhere yet she was relentless.

"Come on, now I'm curious. How is Kalos a mess?"

"The people here have strange ideas, that's all." Archer said. "To start with bureaucracy is rampant... Taxes for everything are such highway robbery it puts many of our Team Rocket extortion schemes to shame...They have the wild idea that there's an additional elemental type called fairy, and that they need to reclassify Jigglypuff because of it. Colress says it causes a fuss whenever the debate is brought up at scientific conventions..."

"That's ridiculous. Everyone knows there are only nine types," Zoe interjected.

"...seventeen types," Archer corrected.

Zoe dismissed it with a wave. "It's all good."

"They also believe an ancient myth about something called mega evolution. As if Pokémon can evolve temporarily and then revert to their old forms afterward."

"Wait – that sounds kind of neat. So a Sparkit...sorry, a Pikachu, can switch to a Raichu and then go back to being a Pikachu?"

"No. More like a Venusaur will grow more leaves in battle and then shed them afterwards. It's stupid."

"I don't think it's stupid. I still think it sounds kind of neat."

Archer would prefer the simplicity of Kanto and Johto, where they didn't trifle so much with what he viewed as frivolous gimmicks, and where any strange and fascinating ability was a mythological tale left to the Legendary Pokémon.

But he still hadn't told her the worst of it, or what he saw as the worst...

"They had an uprising here a few years back, though it never got as far as the Plasma War in the Unova region."

This piqued her interest. "Oh? What was it about?"

"...are you sure you want to hear it? Kalos is a mess."

"It can't be that bad."

Archer decided to indulge her with the tale. "This guy here in Kalos took one look at the war happening over in Unova and decided to destroy the world."

"...why?"

"He said it wasn't beautiful enough."

Zoe stared at him quizzically.

"The world, not the war," Archer specified. "There's probably no way to have a beautiful war."

"Okay..."

"So he kidnapped a condor and a deer and tried to use them to power a mythical weapon to nearly annihilate half the region. That shit didn't work out so he figured, the next best thing would be using this weapon to somehow give himself immortality."

"So he could live in the ugly world?"

"A bunch of teenagers show up to tell him it was a bad idea because apparently they'd read a history book and discovered his long-lost ancestor tried something similar once upon a time and it didn't go well, but the other guy basically said 'fuck you, I'll do it anyway' ...at which point he fired off the weapon only for his whole underground bunker to come crashing down on his head," Archer recounted, entirely deadpan. "Somehow he survived because the deer did increase his life span but the condor got pissed and fucked up his looks. The last I heard he and his buddies now run a food truck somewhere on the south side of Lumiose. Damned expensive food, too."

"Is this for real?" Zoe asked in disbelief.

"Unfortunately so."

"Kalos is a mess."

A third voice chimed in. "Kalos has its own kind of beauty. A nostalgic sort, maybe, but it is there."

"Taunie! Good to see you!" Archer greeted, as the newcomer joined them.

Taunie was the youngest of Giovanni's godchildren, and knew Archer from family gatherings. Blonde hair tipped with red highlights accentuated a face with soft features and large blue eyes. She had a Pokémon with her, a Totodile.

"What brings you to these parts, Archer?" Taunie asked as she and Archer hugged hello.

"We're here on business," Archer replied, "but I figured we could spend the first day sightseeing. It's Zoe's first time in Kalos." He turned to Zoe and explained, "Taunie and I have the same godfather, Giovanni. We've known each other all our lives, because Giovanni has gatherings often where he reunites all his godchildren. As far as we're concerned, we're all kinfolk."

Taunie stuck her hand out for Zoe to shake, which she did. "Nice to meet you Zoe." She then said to Archer, "you know you probably have time to show her around a bit."

While true, there was more to their tourist holiday than merely showing Zoe around. He wasn't very sure where to begin as far as figuring out who in Quasartico Inc. was Marcus' business associate. Having a day to get settled in would give him a chance to properly plan their strategy.

"Taunie we wouldn't mind if you were to tag along," Archer said.

"I'm fascinated by everything I've seen so far," Zoe added.

"Okay!" exclaimed Taunie, "Guess you've got yourself an extra tour guide. First though, I think we should find a place to eat...get energized for the walk about."

Taunie's Totodile growled happily at the thought of food and hopped up and down with enthusiasm.

They stopped at a local café to have some of the city's famous croissants and galettes, then afterwards went about to some of the most well-known tourist locations.

Unfortunately, Prism Tower was closed, with a wall encircling the property while construction crews finished up renovations on the façade, which left them to admire the iconic building from afar.

Then Taunie showed Zoe the mall, whereupon they spent close to three hours looking though clothes and perfumes and pretty things, a shopping spree which no doubt made up in Zoe's mind for Kalos otherwise being an egregious mess, and which Archer eventually got bored with and went off to see if he could pick a fight with some other Pokémon trainer in the plaza.

Taunie stopped him, awkwardly apologetic. "Pokémon battles are outlawed in Lumiose City by day."

"Come again?" Archer asked.

"You can only hold them on designated battlefields or at night in the special tournament they're going to be holding called the Z-A Royale," she explained.

"That's the stupidest thing I've ever heard. What is our world coming to?" Archer complained.

"The city council said something about keeping Lumiose safe for passersby and avoiding people loitering around as bystanders."

"There must've been some hell of collateral damage that happened for Lumiose's municipal government to enact such a dumb law. What, did a kid get hit by a rogue Hyper Beam or something?"

"There was a rash of Pokémon thefts a couple of years back where trainers would get jumped in alleyways after battle for their Poké Balls."

Archer remained unimpressed. "That's just doubly dumb. What kind of trainers hang out in alleys without a Pokémon by their side, out of its Poké Ball for protection?"

"It wouldn't be of any help anyway," Taunie replied, "It's illegal to have your Pokémon target a person in Lumiose City even if it's supposedly in self defense."

Archer spent the rest of the outing muttering obscenities about Lumiose having too much government and misusing taxes, longing to be in Johto or Unova or even – heaven forbid – Palpagos Island. Despite how much he'd clamored to get off that damned island with its knock-off species, up to a point its ways reminded him more of old-fashioned common sense than Kalos ever could.

He cheered up considerably when, after passing the fifth poster advertising the coming Z-A Royale tournament, he inquired after the rules.

"You mean to say we can sneak up and ambush opponent Pokémon to gain the advantage?" Archer could hardly believe his ears. "This isn't a one-off thing; this is actually expected and part of the rules?"

"Yep," Taunie affirmed, "you have to lurk around the shadows in the streets cordoned off for the event to spring attacks on other competitors before they hit your Pokémon first."

"I like that. I'm entering the tournament."

Suddenly a bunch of the Unowns surrounded them. They squeaked at Archer, and one of them poked his arm in a hello.

"Good afternoon," Archer greeted them nonchalantly, "I didn't expect you to show up here in the Kalos region. You get around."

"Are those Unowns?" Taunie took a wary step backward, "I've heard they can be unpredictable in groups."

"Don't worry. The only one they want to pester is me." Archer turned back to the Unowns. "What've you got for us?"

Rotating their positions, the Unown spelled:

PLANTS

"Huh?"

COME SEE

The Unown led Archer, and consequently Zoe and Taunie, to one of the stretches of parkland in the city – a miniature route of sorts that was marked by a translucent green energy barrier. A sign in front invited trainers in, and labelled the area: Lumiose Wild Zones, Quadrant 9.

"Wild zones?" Archer glanced quizzically at Taunie.

"They're part of the urban redevelopment project Quasartico is doing," Taunie explained. "They're parks throughout the city for wild Pokémon."

Archer immediately took interest when she mentioned it was a Quasartico backed development. "We're going to follow the Unown in and see what's up. We'll catch up to you later, Taunie."

With the Unown in the lead, Archer and Zoe entered the park. A meandering walkway cut a trail through grassy fields and overlooked pristine manmade ponds. Despite this, it felt small. The buildings formed a canyon around the wild zone, yet it was remarkable how many species of Pokémon Archer observed in the same site.

They must have trucked them in, he reasoned, unable to imagine such a large diversity of species deciding to move into the city of their own accord. He spied everything from wild Pikachu scampering into the tall grass to Slowpoke fishing for Shellder at the pond.

They brought them to a flowerbed where dozens of exotic red flowers were planted. Here, the Unowns halted, and once again spelled out the word:

PLANTS

"Yes, I think you're right," said Archer, bored, "those are plants."

"Wait," exclaimed Zoe, "those are the same plants from our island."

Archer gave them a second look. She was right; he recognized the flowers with their dewy vines as the same strange variety that had grown wild in the abandoned city on Astral Mountains.

The only place those flowers could have come from was Palpagos Island.

One of the Unown trilled as if calling to someone, whereupon a new Pokémon tentatively emerged from the bracken to stand before Archer and Zoe.

It was a little green Pokémon with a big hexagonal red spot and a single eye, almost formless in shape, but about the same size as the Unown. It chirped, and was joined by several others which crawled out from underneath the bushes. All of them seemed to respond to the first, which was the only one to have a spot. Archer guessed it was the leader.

"What the hell are these?" he asked.

The Unowns reorganized their positions and answered:

COUSINS

Archer eyed the cluster of new creatures dubiously; Zoe opened a Pokédex she'd been gifted by Team Rocket, back on the island, and pointed it at them.

Zygarde
Type: Dragon-Ground
It's hypothesized that this Pokémon monitors the ecosystem from deep in the cave where it lives. If its habitat falls into disarray, it reveals its secret power.

"So it's a regional form of Unown," Archer decided.

"No, it's a Zygarde," Zoe corrected.

Archer was unimpressed. "It's got one eye and they hang out in groups. It's a regional form of Unown. We'd best be wary of them."

Zoe was studying the information displayed on the Pokédex. "If this says Zygarde live in caves, how come these are here in the middle of the park?"

"Unown live in old ruins, and they routinely come out to raise havoc," said Archer with a glance at the Unown, one of which gave a squeak attesting to it.

"Somehow I don't think that these other Pals are out here because they want to be," Zoe said.

Several of the Zygarde looked annoyed, and the leader chirped a couple of times. The Unown replied to it with squeaks, and then turned around to address the humans again.

PLANTS BAD EAT

"These plants weren't put there to eat," Archer said, "they were put there as ornamentation. Did one of you get indigested?"

The lead Zygarde gave a series of chirps that was obviously a long-winded account of the happenings, though of course neither Archer nor Zoe could comprehend it. Suddenly, it stood up straight as if it had sensed something, and gave a shrill sound to the others. All the Zygarde scattered.

The Unown also seemed to have detected something, and squeaking over each other in unison circled around and teleported away without explanation.

Before either Archer or Zoe could react, there was the howl of an animal and a loud crashing sound of an attack being fired. A large white-furred Pokémon bounded into view, trying to shake sap and vines away from its muzzle.

Archer recognized the creature as an Absol. The fur on its ruff had bristled and fluffed out to nearly triple its size, like flared wings, and its fangs were longer than usual and bared furiously.

A winged Absol. Archer had never seen a winged Absol. For a moment he thought he was back on the island with its familiar-yet-distinct wildlife.

"What kind of Absol has..."

He didn't have time to say another word before the Absol swung its head, and a scythe of violet energy spun outwards towards them. Archer and Zoe hit the ground as it narrowly missed and collided with a lamppost behind where they stood. The light crashed to the ground.

"Houndoom, come out!" Archer called, as he grabbed the Poké Ball from his pocket and swiftly pressed the button to open it.

Houndoom sprang forth in glistening light, and immediately turned its attention on their aggressor. It leapt to sink its fangs into Absol's shoulder; Absol countered by raking its claws across Houndoom's flank, and both Pokémon tumbled backwards into the flowers.

Sap from the flowers was now streaked across Houndoom's pelt as well. Houndoom snarled, yet its growl had become fiercer and more guttural, and suddenly its fur began to glow almost as if it were evolving.

The light held an almost magenta sheen; if this was an evolution, it was unlike any other. Houndoom's stature grew till it was almost the same height as its opponent, the horns on its head straightened upwards, the ridge around its shoulders lengthened till its swept outwards like a shield of bone, and its claws and the tip of its tail began to shine a bright red-orange as if dipped in lava...

Archer couldn't believe it. He stared in shock at the dog, not sure whether he should call it back into its Poké Ball or try to stop the metamorphosis.

"Did Houndoom evolve?" Zoe questioned, glancing at Archer with wonderment.

"Houndoom aren't able to evolve," he emphasized.

With a howl, Houndoom sprang viciously at Absol again, which shrieked and raced out of the park towards the city streets.

Houndoom ran after Absol with a vengeance, and Archer grabbed Zoe's hand as they chased after the two Pokémon.

A block away, there was a crowd gathered where the city mayor was making a speech proclaiming the opening of the last of the city's planned wild zones. Mrs. Jett Silph was also present, along with her security guard Mr. Muscat, and as the mayor finished his speech he turned towards Jett. "...the CEO of Quasartico Inc. Would you like to say a few words?"

Jett smiled, and obliged. She spoke a bit about the beautiful new parks, and how they would bring in plenty of tourism, which was mostly a restatement of what the mayor had already said; however the eloquence of how their renewed city would cultivate the bonds between mankind and nature – that was all hers.

"Our development is not just for aesthetics. It's a step towards the future, a step towards making Lumiose a city for everyone," Jett declared, spreading her arms wide for emphasis. "A city for people and Pokémon, together..."

Her voice was drowned out by an explosion, somewhere from behind her. Jett hardly had a chance to turn round to see what it was before the crowd was flung into a panic and everybody scattered.

Jett caught sight of the flash of white fur and the spark of a rising energy attack before the full image came into focus: the winged Absol still desperately trying to shake the vines and sap away from its face, and the huge Houndoom trying to subdue it. Absol spun about to unleash another attack, successfully shaking away the vines in the process; the flare of energy flew towards the podium but fell short, striking and fizzling out on the asphalt.

"Everybody! Run!" the mayor yelled.

Jett was not asking questions. She tried to run too, on the urging of Muscat, but as she sprinted off the platform her heel caught on the treacherous sidewalk and she tripped.

The Absol at that moment noticed Jett, and seemingly without a second thought leapt at her with claws outstretched. Jett screamed, and tried to shield herself from the attack, only to see the wild Absol get tackled away by Houndoom.

In the same instant Archer darted in front of her, his entire focus on ordering his Pokémon. "Keep it up, Houndoom. Faint Attack!"

Jett stared at the battle between the two strangely evolved Pokémon incredulously. Muscat was suddenly at her side, pulling her up from the sidewalk. "Mrs. Silph, are you unharmed?"

She pushed him away and headed in the direction where Archer's Houndoom was now repelling the Absol.

Looking upward, she saw a balcony that would give her a good vantage point where she could see the fight, and didn't hesitate in sprinting up to the overlook. Muscat, her bodyguard, followed her up.

"Inferno!" shouted Archer.

Houndoom leapt into the air, and the moment its paws hit the asphalt a tidal wave of flame burst outwards, far stronger than any Inferno attack it had been able to use before. Archer started second-guessing the move when he saw just how fearsome it was in his Pokémon's present state. Maybe I'd better not order that again; it might hit the parked cars.

Absol narrowly jumped back, avoiding the fire by a whisker's length, however the plant sap on the creature's fur evaporated as a result of the proximity. Absol's unnaturally frizzed fur began to lie flat and its ferocity seemed to die down as well. It had seemingly returned to being a normal Absol, albeit a confused one.

Archer took advantage of the creature being stunned. He seized an empty Poké Ball in his hand and threw it directly at Absol.

It struck Absol's forehead, and there was a flash of light as the Pokémon was swept into the capsule. The Poké Ball landed on the ground, shaking back and forth.

Archer found himself holding his breath with tense expectation, ready to issue another order to Houndoom if need be, till the Poké Ball's flashing indicator light shut off. He'd caught the Absol.

As he walked over and collected the capsule from the ground he suddenly heard cheering. He glanced over to see a small throng of people applauding his victory. Subtly, he winced. He hadn't realized how public the whole battle had been. He looked over at Houndoom to find his Pokémon standing unsteadily, steam wafting off its fur from its body temperature.

Zoe spoke up. "Archer, that was fantastic! ...but why is Houndoom's fur giving off steam?"

Archer knew fire types had higher temperatures than most other Pokémon, but the only time they'd cause actual clouds of steam was when they had a fever. Like had occurred with Absol, the transformation faded, and Houndoom – back to normal – collapsed with exhaustion.

He was immediately at his Pokémon's side. "Houndoom! Are you okay? ...I'd better get you to the Pokémon Center," he murmured, recalling his pet to its Poké Ball.

From her position up on the balcony, Jett watched the events unfold with skepticism.

"Mr. Muscat, who is that trainer?" she asked.

"I don't know, ma'am."

"Find out."

Chapter 22 - The Meeting at Quasartico's Headquarters ✅

Following the Pokémon battle, Archer rushed to the Pokémon Center to heal Houndoom and the newly captured Absol.

He was worried about his Pokémon. He knew plenty about the Houndour line, of which Houndoom was, as far as he knew, the final evolution. He was fairly certain he had never heard anything about the kind of temporary transformation he'd seen it undergo.

Or, for that matter, what he'd seen Absol undergo.

He spoke with Giovanni via a videophone in the Pokémon Center lobby, and related everything that had transpired – from the Unowns and the exotic flowers, to the rogue Absol he had fought and captured.

Giovanni sounded exasperated. "Archer, what did I ever tell you about making a name for Team Rocket?"

"Sir, I believe you said, 'People must feel fear at the name Team Rocket, never laugh at it'."

"I expect that is becoming the case in Lumiose," Giovanni stated.

Archer certainly hoped so. Right now he didn't think that he was becoming feared or mocked by the city folk, but he was probably gaining celebrity.

The conversation with his boss wrapped up and Archer went back to the waiting area of the Pokémon Center.

He didn't have very long to wait before the nurse returned with the Poké Balls, as well as some documents outlining laboratory results of a thorough examination done to both Houndoom and Absol.

Archer gathered all his Poké Balls and went outside to meet up with Zoe. Once outside he took a look at the health report issued by the Pokémon Center when they healed the animals.

"It looks like when they got themselves covered in sap," Archer observed, as he perused the documents, "that caused some sort of an imbalance in their elemental energy."

"So that's what happened to your Houndoom," Zoe said.

Archer thought about this briefly, and the more he did the stranger it seemed. "Sap from a plant couldn't exact such a change in a Pokémon, could it?"

"Is that mega evolution?" Zoe asked.

...was it? He shook his head.

"Whatever it was, it's no good. It seemed like the transformation was causing both Absol and Houndoom pain," he said. A thought occurred to him. "Zoe...the sap and vines the Pokémon were covered in...were they from those flowering plants?"

"They could've been. It certainly looked like the same vines," Zoe considered, "But I've seen large Pals on the island routinely eat them with no problem."

"Maybe so," said Archer, "but just because they find it tasty doesn't mean its good for them. Anyone can develop allergies."

"The plants release a scent that reminds Pokémon of berries," noted Zoe.

"Why would it send out a scent that would mimic food and lure Pokémon to it? It's almost like the flower wants them to eat it. Or wants them to get near, anyway." Archer reasoned.

"It's a plant," replied Zoe simply.

"But it's got to serve an evolutionary purpose!" insisted Archer.

"It doesn't matter." sighed Zoe. "The point is that it's harming the wildlife in Lumiose."

"Not to mention how this could be dangerous if a higher-level Pokémon decides those flowers make a tasty snack," added Archer, "Can you imagine a rampaging, mega-evolved Charizard on the loose?"

"What's a Charizard?" asked Zoe.

"Never mind," said Archer, "I'll explain it later... right now these Pokemon need to be fed."

Archer sent out all three of his Pokémon in the fenced-in area behind the Pokémon Center.

"Time to eat!" he said.

He set down dishes of kibble for all the Pokémon. Houndoom wagged its tail, while Frostallion neighed and flapped its wings. The newcomer, Absol, shrank back a bit embarrassed and gazed at its paws.

"What's the matter?" Archer sighed. "I don't blame you. You were frantic to get those vines off your face."

"Aren't these supposed to be shy Pokémon?" asked Zoe, reading through information on her Pokédex, "They say Absol only appear in front of humans to warn of coming disaster."

"That's an old wives' tale."

"It looks a little like a Felbat," Zoe said. Archer gave her a quizzical look, realizing she was referencing an island Pal, and she elaborated, "Except Felbat are bat like, not leonine. But it has the same color points and the single horn."

Zoe had been scrolling through her Pokédex and then exclaimed, "Here it is! I found Charizard... You know, I've never seen any Pal quite like this. Would you believe we have no real equivalent on Palpagos Island?"

"Now that's an interesting bit of news," chuckled Archer, "so far that seems to be the only Pokémon we've got that you guys don't!"

"Excuse the interruption," a voice spoke behind them and they turned to see a man who added, "My name is Muscat. I am Mrs. Jett Silph's bodyguard...she is the head of Quasartico Inc. She saw you battling today and would like to thank you in person for rescuing her from that vicious Pokémon."

She wants to thank us? thought Archer. Unexpected though it was, he could see a potential way to take advantage of the meeting. This could be our chance to find out who in Quasartico is behind the supply drops.

"Tell Mrs. Silph," said Archer, "we accept her gracious invitation and will be there within one hour."

They found the headquarters of Quasartico Inc. on the far side of the city. It had modernistic architecture, with glass walls and balconies in an avant garde style that looked almost out of place next to Lumiose's historical boulevards, and an adjoining, fenced-in Pokémon battlefield.

The interior lobby was wide, with stone flooring and a wall topiary arranged in a triangular formation on the right wall, and to the left were glittering holographic displays showcasing the urban redevelopment plans underway for the city. Archer and Zoe went directly up to the reception desk opposite the main entrance.

"The receptionist, who had been looking at some documents on her desk, didn't even raise her head and as she continued sorting the papers asked them, "May I help you?"

"Yes, you may," Archer informed her. "We are looking for Mrs. Jett Silph. She extended an invitation to us to drop by to speak with her."

At this statement, the receptionist looked up from all the paperwork. "Just a moment please," she said as she pushed a button on the intercom and called Jett.

"Let them pass!" Jett was overheard exclaiming.

The pair were let in quickly to meet with her; she began apologizing fast.

"I am sorry I failed to show my appreciation sooner." Jett smiled briefly. "Come in. Do sit down," she said, motioning to two chairs situated in front of her desk. "I wish there was some way to repay the favor...Archer...I remember you from Giovanni's soiree." She looked at Zoe with a perplexed look and said, "Not you, however."

Archer cleared his throat and said, "This is Zoe... she's an associate of ours." He left it at that, and Jett knew better than to question further.

"Well," said Jett, "I am glad you and your fellow associate were around at the right time to help out, but I find it intriguing that Rocket Enterprises is in our fair city."

"The reason we came to Lumiose is that Mr. Delavita sent us to find out who is dropping supplies from an aircraft onto Palpagos Island."

Jett grew quiet all of a sudden and Archer noticed it. She must know something, he thought.

"Why would Mr. Delavita be interested in such a thing?" she asked.

"Because he is now the new, legal, owner of Palpagos Island."

"What? How?"

"He bought it."

The silence in the room was so intense that the wind blowing outside the open window in Jett's office sounded noisy. Jett got up and walked towards it. "It's become windy suddenly," she commented as she closed the window.

"Mrs. Silph." Archer paused briefly, "You did say you wished there was a way to repay the favor, did you not?"

"Yes," replied Jett, swallowing nervously.

"Perhaps it would be easy for you to find out who exactly is dropping supplies on Palpagos Island." Archer looked at her eyes directly.

Jett stared at him silently for awhile and then looked over at Zoe, who has been sitting observing it all without saying a single word.

Finally Jett spoke. "I am the one ordering the drops."

Archer and Zoe looked at each other wordlessly, and then Archer turned his attention back to Jett.

"Mr. Giovanni Delavita sent us to find out who was coordinating the supply drops and to inform them that because Palpagos Island is now under the direction and control of Rocket Enterprises, Mr. Marcus Dryden will not be negotiating any business deals from this point forward, so adjust yourself accordingly."

"Well," said Jett. She paused, as if thinking things through in her mind. "Perhaps your boss and I could do business...it doesn't matter to me who my business partner is as long as my company doesn't suffer financially."

"I will relay that information to Giovanni," Archer replied. "If he decides to do that, he will most likely set the terms and conditions."

Jett smiled. "Oh, I'm sure your boss and I could come to an agreement," she said, "after all, money does talk. Perhaps if I could meet with him directly..."

Archer put a hand into the air to stop Jett speaking, then said, "Giovanni has made it perfectly clear that his message to you is to let you know your business transactions with Marcus will stop, and the drops onto the island should stop. He considers imparting this message to you, a courtesy."

Jett's face reflected a slight frown, but she replied nothing as Archer and Zoe got up from their seats to leave. "You will hear from us again," he added.

Jett didn't know what to think. She felt sick to her stomach at the thought of being placed in a similar situation her late husband had once been in.

Team Rocket doesn't hold power in Kalos, some part of her mind reasoned, they can't do anything here without falling afoul of Corbeau. But Corbeau doesn't know anything about this business with Marcus, does he? And Marcus himself; how will he take it if I cut off the supply drops? ...Oh, why couldn't the city council have just approved those demolition permits?

Corbeau had many contacts in the city of Lumiose, be they people loyal to him, or people who owed him, or people who wanted to garner favor with him. He had no shortage of these fountains of information in his syndicate's territory, so it was rare that he would be unaware of events within the Kalos region.

This was, ironically, why Corbeau was uneasy after having heard from the city mayor that evening. As soon as he'd run through all the scheduled gym battles with the day's challengers, he returned to his office in a great haste.

One thing was rogue wild Pokémon; he'd heard about that too, and while he could imagine it looking bad for Quasartico and their urban redevelopment, Jett already had most of the project completed, and anyone with the means to make it an issue could be convinced to overlook the whole thing with a bit of bribery or old-fashioned coercion. Corbeau didn't think it was that important. However, the fact that the latest rogue Pokémon had been quelled by a skilled trainer from outside Kalos? Who, upon further inquiry, turned out to be the godson of Giovanni Delavita – the don of Team Rocket?

That was concerning to Corbeau. He didn't like the idea that a Team Rocket admin had shown up unannounced to Rust Syndicate territory, and even worse he hadn't heard a single thing about it till said Team Rocket admin made a blatant spectacle by catching a rampaging wild Pokémon in the middle of the city. Corbeau half-wondered if the whole thing had been staged just to send a message.

Corbeau called some of his agents to meet with him in his office and asked them what they'd been able to learn so far about Archer Verdi and his intentions. They didn't have much new to say about the Team Rocket admin, except for one tidbit.

"He was overheard outside the Pokémon Center discussing plans to participate in the Z-A Royale tonight."

"The battle tournament?" Corbeau considered this briefly. "Well, maybe that would be a fitting place to coincide with our unexpected visitor."

He glanced up at his subordinates, who all stood expectantly at attention.

"I want to know whether Team Rocket is here on a mission of peace or war," ordered Corbeau. "If they are here for peace, then we will welcome them to Lumiose City in kind."

"...and if they're here for war?"

"I hope that's not the case." Corbeau's eyes glinted. "But if it is, even rockets can rust."

Chapter 23 - Corbeau ✅

Archer began watching the clock as soon as it hit nightfall, and at the designated hour he set out walking from the hotel, down the bustling sidewalk, to take part in the Z-A Royale battle competition that was being held nearby.

The designated streets were marked by a red energy barrier. It was easy to see the shimmer of light coming up the sidewalk, along with the ticket booth with a line of trainers and Pokémon in front, and the tall banners advertising its sponsors – one of which was, unsurprisingly, the land development company Quasartico Inc.

Archer entered Houndoom, and was given a ticket into the area. He was also reminded of the competition rules:

Anyone walking in the cordoned-off streets with a Pokémon is fair game. You lose if your Pokémon is knocked out. Anyone who still has their Pokémon in fighting condition by sunrise will advance to the next day's round.

And, of course, you're supposed to ambush other trainers' Pokémon in battle before they see you.

It was like a watered-down version of Team Rocket training, and Archer excelled at it. Within the first hour he and Houndoom had won against three other trainers, without incurring much damage themselves, and without anybody having been able to ambush them back. What to the rest of the trainers there was probably a challenge was child's play to him, especially considering the events on Palpagos Island still being fresh in his mind.

Archer kept to the shadows, as lithe as ever, with Houndoom close at his heels. He picked out their next target – a novice trainer, who was lingering around a tree with their sheep Pokémon, Mareep.

"Them," he whispered to Houndoom, "That Mareep looks to be a low enough level that you can probably one-shot it. Start with..."

He could barely finish the command. Seemingly out of nowhere, a barrage of sludge struck Houndoom, which yelped and spun about growling to face the attacker. Archer turned immediately to come face-to-face with Corbeau.

Beside him stood a tall, bipedal black lizard, with pink markings across its torso and a narrow, crocodilian snout, that Archer recognized as a Salazzle.

Corbeau was quick to order a second attack. "We've got the advantage now! Follow up with Poison Fang."

"Houndoom, Faint Attack," Archer called, reorienting himself to their new foe.

The battle was frenetic. Salazzle whipped about, while Houndoom bounded backwards to evade its snapping attacks and lunged to deliver its own.

While he kept his attention primarily on the two Pokémon fighting in front of him, Archer was nonetheless aware of people stationed on the rooftops and surrounding areas outside of the Royale streets, watching the battle between him and Corbeau play out with keen eyes. They were stoic figures with dark suits that bore a rhombus-shaped logo similar to that of the Lumiose gym's current badge design, and their Pokémon standing at their side awaiting an order.

Rust Syndicate members, Archer deduced, no doubt here to guard their boss, but they could just as easily be made to launch an attack from their positions.

Corbeau, however, displayed no inclination of being preoccupied with anything other than the battle competition before him.

"Sludge Wave," Corbeau ordered his Pokémon, "try to knock it down!"

Salazzle sent forth another surge of mire towards Houndoom. Archer held back till he saw the crest of sludge rise and then seized the opportunity.

"Now, Houndoom, straight through the sludge!" shouted Archer.

Houndoom leapt through the wave, its jaws alight with flame, to tackle into its opponent. Salazzle hissed, tripping back but catching itself at the last instant on all fours.

Archer saw Corbeau clench his teeth briefly in frustration, and his features contort into a frown; evidently the maneuver had been unexpected. Witnessing the reaction made Archer smirk. If he thinks I'm going to make this an easy win, he's got another thing coming!

Salazzle writhed about with surprising swiftness, leaping back onto its hind legs and rushing in for the counterattack. Houndoom dodged, but nonetheless swayed on its paws. It must've been affected by those poison attacks, thought Archer, I'd better try to end the fight fast.

"Inferno!"

"Flamethrower!"

The two Pokémon unleashed their fire attacks at the same time, with the moves striking them both head-on. Salazzle reeled backwards and collapsed, while Houndoom stumbled to the ground as well; with both knocked out, the battle had ended in a draw.

"Not bad," said Corbeau, recalling Salazzle to its Poké Ball. "It appears everything I was told was true about Team Rocket agents and the excellence of their battling skill."

"We pride ourselves with good training," Archer replied simply, as he also called Houndoom into its sphere.

Corbeau put out his hand and Archer shook it, so Corbeau asked him a question point blank. "Why is Team Rocket in my territory? Surely you didn't travel all this way for a simple contest?"

"Team Rocket business that needed to be addressed," Archer answered, then tucked Houndoom's Poké Ball into his pocket and walked away.

Corbeau watched him leave and summoned two of his agents. "Don't let him out of your sight...keep me informed of his every move...who he sees, speaks with, where he's staying."

"Yes sir." The agents saluted and ran off after Archer, keeping a distance so as to not be noticed.

Corbeau was pensive. "I'll get to the bottom of this," he said to himself.

Corbeau arrived at his office bright and early the next morning. He dialed a number on the telephone on his desk and after a couple of rings a receptionist answered it. "Rocket Enterprises; kindly state your business."

"This is Mr. Corbeau of Rust Industries. Please tell Mr. Giovanni Delavita I request to speak with him."

After a couple of minutes, Giovanni came on the line. "Corbeau, what a surprise! What's on your mind?"

"Giovanni, I know you're a busy man, but there is a question I have that has been causing me some concern... Why did your people pay a visit to Jett of Quasartico? I know it wasn't just a vacation or passing through. Our families have been neutral since before you and I were born...I am guessing there's a logical explanation for the minor intrusion."

Giovanni let him finish speaking his piece, and when he got silent he replied:

"It seems Jett has a business arrangement with Marcus Dryden who was the former controller of Palpagos Island..."

"Former?" Corbeau interrupted with surprise.

Giovanni ignored him and continued speaking. "I am now the new legal owner of the island and I have a feud going with Dryden. He is unreasonable and disrespectful so he will be evicted, one way or another. Jett needs to stop all business with him. If she wants to do business with me that's another issue altogether. This is not a turf war between you and me."
