"Well, firstly congratulations on your new land acquisition and business endeavor... Secondly, I am glad to hear our families can proceed in peace. I will speak with Jett and tell her to stay out of your way."

"Good," Giovanni answered, "It's also good that we can discuss these things man to man in a civilized way."

"Have a good day, Giovanni."

"Ciao," Giovanni replied, and the two men hung up their phones.

Following the conversation with Giovanni, Corbeau asked Jett to come speak with him. She arrived at the gym promptly and they met at his office there.

"Hello Corbeau," greeted Jett, "what's wrong? You seemed rather terse when you spoke over the phone. Is something the matter?"

"I wanted to discuss your business partner, Marcus Dryden," he said.

He noticed her waver, only a bit, but it was perceptible.

Corbeau waved a hand dismissively as he elaborated, "I know you have a business deal with him. What is it, exactly?"

"Well, he gets shipments of items...simple things...whatever he requests, really."

"...and what do you get in return?"

"The flowers, for one."

"Yes, they are a novelty," Corbeau considered, "and grow extraordinarily fast. If this keeps up they're going to reach as tall as the bamboo we've got in the gym's foyer."

He straightened his glasses and looked at her directly. Jett met his golden gaze, but said nothing. It was Corbeau who spoke again:

"You can't be flying out weekly shipments of crude oil, potions, and ammunition in return for only a measly fifty pots of flowers."

Corbeau knew more than he let on, Jett realized; perhaps he had made inquiries, or was particularly astute to whatever was going on in his territory, yet the fact of the matter was that he somehow knew these things. All at once, Jett decided it would be best if she admitted everything. She did not want to be accused of misleading him; yes, maybe she had been misleading him, only a little, but she didn't see how her business with the Palpagos Island leader concerned him or his organization.

"It was more than the flowers," Jett admitted. "They were intended to be a sort of interest accrued till Marcus could make arrangements for the real reimbursement. He was planning to invade Kalos, and I was going to take advantage of it by having him destroy the south-east side of Lumiose City, which I can't get the demolition permits for."

The reaction she got from Corbeau was a stunned stare.

"I know what you must be thinking..." Jett said, suddenly feeling self-conscious about the admission, "There's no way he can really take over. He doesn't have nearly the amount of manpower to contend with the mainland armies, even with the lasers... and with your people of course."

"Jett," he said, "What made you ever think that this was a good idea?"

She blinked, her expression almost innocuous. "It seemed like it would turn a profit."

Corbeau thought about her words for a moment, and then began laughing. It was a bitter sort of laugh, and Jett shifted her posture uncomfortably.

"All right," Corbeau stopped laughing and smiled at her, "I can appreciate a financial gamble, even something as outlandish as destroying half of Lumiose. I'll even overlook that it's technically part of my territory, too."

She winced noticeably.

"You owe me for two favors," said Corbeau, holding out his fingers to number them. "The first was getting your company the green light to renovate Prism Tower. The second was getting the buildings around the tower to be sold to you. The time has come for you to repay those favors."

Jett was starting to look nervous, but she swallowed the dryness in her throat. "What do you request?"

"First...cut off your business deal with Mr. Dryden."

"What?"

"Cut off your business deal with Mr. Dryden," Corbeau reiterated. "Palpagos Island is now Team Rocket territory and Marcus Dryden is waging war against them; I won't have anyone getting involved in it from within my territory. My family has always been neutral with the Delavitas and I intend to keep peace with Team Rocket even now."

"I don't think Marcus will take it very well..." Jett began to say, "the supply drops have been going on for years..."

Corbeau studied her quietly. "Jett, we've always been good business associates. I really would find it lamentable if our acquaintanceship...soured."

His voice was pleasant as ever, but the insinuations were there. Jett had no desire to contend with the cruel realities of crossing his organization. She knew Corbeau well enough to know that beyond any cordiality they showed one another, what they had between them was a business arrangement, and dissolving that arrangement on less than agreeable terms could turn out to be lethal.

"No, no I would feel the same," she concurred hastily. "I'll end the deal with Marcus Dryden."

Corbeau returned a nod, as if her answer suited him. "I'll see if anything can be done about your demolition permits, but for now forget about south-east Lumiose. I will withhold the second request...for the moment. Tell me as soon as you've completed the first."

"There's just one problem..." said Jett, looking dispirited, "I don't have any way to contact him. Not yet, anyway. He had to leave his base in a hurry because of Team Rocket and so he claimed he would contact me."

"Then as soon as you hear from him, you tell him the deal is off," Corbeau replied. "No more shipments, not even a single potion."

Jett had never felt quite so worried as she did that day, leaving Corbeau's office and returning to her own. The first thing she did was sit at her desk and hold her head in her hands, completely desolate in her predicament.

She glanced absently at the flowering plant. It had grown considerably, and was already almost the size of a potted palm and had been placed to the side of her desk.

Jett observed it with a sort of mild curiosity. The blossom itself was nearly as big as that of a sunflower. It's going to grow as massive as a tree if this keeps up, she thought.

Chapter 24 - Poké Balls and Pal Spheres ✅

The next day started out fairly rainy, and the downpour lasted throughout the day till subsiding around late afternoon. Because of this Archer forwent any outings, instead remaining in the hotel where he and Zoe had gotten rooms during their stay in Lumiose City.

Zoe had stepped out momentarily to get food at the cafeteria located in the ground floor. "I'll get take out," she had told Archer, and he went along with it, primarily because he wanted some time alone to think things through.

It was then that he received a video phone call from a familiar trio – James, Jessie, and Meowth.

James spoke first. "The boss wants you back on the island," he said.

Meowth leapt in with a yowl. "We've got that eco-delegation flying in that're supposed to sign off on the rare Pokémon here not being threatened or whatnot. It's to make the boss' purchase of Palpagos Island official."

"Not like getting that approval should be any trouble for Team Rocket," added Jessie mischievously.

"Well, it looks like the three of you have been busy," Archer said tongue in cheek, "Any mishaps? Not that I haven't had my own to contend with."

"Archer, out of all the members of Team Rocket, you're the one that's got the worst luck," Jessie pointed out.

Archer fixed a skeptical look on the unanimously bright eyes of Jessie, James, and Meowth. "Come again?"

James grinned. "That's even considering Pete's incident with the mangoes. We all took a vote yesterday with the minions. You won."

"Or lost?" asked Archer.

"Depending on how you look at it."

"I take it that's also considering how your own combined party of Pokémon got thrashed by a Pikachu you tried to steal, only to find out it belonged to the boss' son?" said Archer, glancing at them sideways.

"Oh, yeah, way worse than that," Meowth purred, squinting his eyes.

"You're always getting into trouble," Jessie went on with a smile. "Since we're Team Rocket's double-trouble experts, it's our pleasure to announce that you're the current poster child for 'shit happens'."

"Believe me, it's not by intent," Archer replied, now feeling a bit mortified.

Even as he hung up the call, he knew his three friends meant no harm by bringing up the obvious about his being unfairly disaster prone, but it settled on his mind irrepressibly for the rest of the day.

The stress was finally catching up to Archer. Apprehension first from his run-in with Marcus Dryden and his poison plot, and then from witnessing how the island people were being held captive at the factory – they'd managed to rescue them, and he felt a little relief by that at least – and now the harrowing incident with the Absol. All of this brought back lingering, horrific recollections of a prior enslavement that were worse still.

Which led at last to him saying "Fuck it" and ensconcing himself in the lounge of the hotel that evening with a bottle of wine and a mission.

Zoe went looking for Archer and found him there, at a table beside one of the wide windows overlooking the cityscape, pouring out yet another goblet of pinot noir. His Houndoom was loyally sitting at his feet but looking undeniably concerned for its trainer. The lounge was relatively quiet, with only the bartender drying glassware behind the counter and a Squirtle trying to help out, none of whom took an interest in Zoe as she went over to Archer's table.

"Zoe... I wondered how long it would be before you found me," he commented with a tired voice.

"How many drinks have you had?" she asked.

"Not enough yet. I want to get as absolutely wasted as I can for the rest of the night."

"Archer, you're going to get drunk."

"Is being sober better? ...Hey, my wine bottle," he protested mildly as she took it away.

"What if Giovanni sees you like this?" Zoe pursued, sitting down in the other chair at the table.

Archer frowned at the thought; the mere idea of displeasing Giovanni, who he held in such high admiration, made him reconsider his actions. "Well, if I'm not going to drink myself into oblivion, I need another vice. Maybe I could take up smoking."

Zoe's gaze softened, "What's wrong?"

"It's nothing important."

"It's important enough that you want to get drunk over it. Besides, I thought drunks were supposed to tell their woes to the bartender."

"Yeah, but the bartender will give them liquor when they ask for it, and you've confiscated my wine. No, you're right. I'm overdoing it, but I'm still not going to tell you a single thing."

Zoe put the bottle back in front of him and said, "I do wish you'd open up to me a bit more. I'm willing to listen, and I won't judge."

Archer gazed into the drink before him, mired in relentless memories. His thoughts were already growing hazy, and the thought of lying down in bed was starting to appeal to him.

He picked the bottle up and then as if rethinking it, put it back down and sighed.

Houndoom meanwhile observed him closely and wanting to remind its trainer of its presence, barked and lay a paw on his lap. Archer petted the dog.

Houndoom had been taken from him when he'd been captured and put through its own ordeal; his Pokémon could understand him perhaps better than anyone. However the recollection of that time didn't affect it as bad.

Almost as a perfectly on-cue example of this, Houndoom nudged at Archer until he produced its Poké Ball for it, and with another happy bark the dog poked the button with its nose. The Poké Ball's lid opened and Houndoom entered the capsule in a red flare.

He studied the sphere meditatively, so deep in thought it surprised him when Zoe laid her hand across his, and he looked up at her. "Archer, please tell me," Zoe coaxed.

Archer relented, and decided to tell her the story.

"Some time ago, Team Rocket was in the middle of a mob war. I was caught by an enemy of ours – like an animal, in a Poké Ball. Where I come from, by law Poké Balls have a safety mechanism added to prevent human beings from being caught. This one had been illegally manufactured without it, so it worked like the Pal Spheres on Palpagos Island."

Some part of recounting this was like prodding at a scab, all the more uncomfortable for Archer because he felt it should have healed by now. Zoe seemed to realize, and interjected:

"There shouldn't be this kind of stigma attached to being held hostage that way. It happened to me briefly. It happened to all those people we rescued who'd been forced to slave in Marcus' factory."

"Would it be only the indignity. At least those people preserved some sense of self," Archer said. "My captor used a Pokémon with psychic attacks so they'd know my thoughts, and if I had any that fell short of compliance it brought punishment."

He was briefly quiet.

"By the time they were through with me, I was willing to do anything they wanted. I'd roll over and beg if they demanded it, and if I wasn't fast enough or precise enough I'd willingly accept the torture that followed. The Poké Ball became a sanctuary from pain. I was so desperate to live, I didn't realize they'd succeeded in killing who I was," admitted Archer, his voice soft as he leant back.

"How did you get out?" asked Zoe.

"I saw a old family photograph," Archer reminisced. "I remembered everything at that moment. The first thing I did was try to shoot my 'trainer' – and miss. Someone else in Team Rocket got the asshole later."

He was gazing pensively out at the last faint flickers of sunlight below the horizon, and how they cast receding shades of orange and pink. Those sinister days and nights he'd spent locked in the capsule, called out to be commanded like a Pokémon; dull obedience interspersed with moments of unyielding terror, which ran into months that blended ceaselessly into an abyss...

He'd probably never truly get over the experience, although he'd learned to live with the toll it had invariably taken, and that was okay too...yet...

"Giovanni says I didn't fail our organization; not everyone can handle what I was put through. Personally I think he's trying to be kind and not admit I'm a coward. I'm afraid of being taken prisoner again, because I know they can break me if I'm put through that kind of hell once more."

"That's not being a coward," Zoe spoke up. "You know what you can take and can't. It's a different kind of strength to be able to accept your limits. Actually, I admire you now more than ever Archer."

He looked up at her in surprise. "Why?" he asked.

"You survived. Your mind and your determination were strong enough to fight back in the end."

He didn't know what to say to that. He was wondering if he should have even told her the anecdote; it was a horrible experience he rarely spoke about to anybody, but part of him was grateful she'd listened to it anyway. Then another part of him worried his preoccupation in the moment was mawkish.

"I guess you're right," Archer replied, "I hadn't thought about it in that way…until now."

"Sometimes it helps to tell someone your troubles," Zoe said, "Someone you trust...and I hope you trust me Archer, because I certainly trust you."

Archer looked at her and smiled. "Sure I trust you," he replied, "That's why I've told you my story...just don't go saying it around will you? Only close Team Rocket associates know about it."

"No worries Archer," Zoe said smiling back.

He wasn't sure if he imagined the delicate blush on her cheeks, or the way their eyes held each other's gaze for just long enough for a magnetic warmth to spread over him; the moment, if it had occurred, passed as swift as a Spearow.

"Zoe, I really am thankful of all the help you've given me...and of your friendship." He paused here and added, "I like you a lot."

Zoe looked in his eyes and replied, "...and I'm thankful I met you."

He stared at her briefly, then leaned over to her and kissed her gently on the lips, as a response. She returned the kiss and Archer gathered her in his arms and held her for along time. Eventually he whispered in her ear, "You know, I'm not staying on the island Zoe...and...I have no intentions of showing up with a wife in tow when I return home."

"I understand," she answered, "though, technically, my people did marry us according to their laws. So, I'll just tell them that we broke up when you leave Palpagos Island. Ever since Giovanni ordered them to be formally trained by Team Rocket they've begun adapting their ways."

"Well then...my room has plenty of privacy," he said.

"Yes it does," Zoe said, turning her face to look at him directly. "Take me there."

Without hesitation, he picked her up and carried her into the elevator and to his room, bolting the door behind him.

The world faded away in their togetherness, and for a while there was nothing else.

Chapter 25 - Three Times the Effort ✅

Archer was happy when they finally returned to Palpagos Island, though he was aware that they likely hadn't seen the last of Lumiose City. He was being called back for only a short period of time, to oversee the delegation's arrival and help out a bit with the new plasteel weapons that were being devised.

Zoe, to the contrary, seemed a little downhearted about leaving the mainland so soon. I guess she's grown to like it there, Archer thought.

Quasartico's connections with the island were intriguing, and certainly merited further investigation, but the delegation's signing was the most important thing right now. Their signed document would turn over the territory officially to Giovanni. Once this triviality was out of the way, then they'd see what to do about Marcus – and Jett.

The council's ecological delegation arrived on Palpagos Island only two hours after Archer and Zoe had returned.

They arrived via propeller airplane, which landed smoothly on the beach. Giovanni and several of the minions met them in civilian attire, of course, because they were very astute about keeping up appearances even if it was a sham and everyone knew they were Team Rocket. The delegation consisted of Professor Oak and Professor Rowan, both of whom had ample claim to be there as wildlife biologists.

It so happened this was the same day that a few more Team Rocket minions would be flying in too, bringing more supplies, as well as Giovanni's lawyer to notarize the documents, and Dr. Colress, a scientist who often worked with their organization in secret on the basis of scientific interest. They were instructed to land in a wooded clearing some distance from the beach so as not to arouse attention.

The two people on the delegation had been taken to the Team Rocket encampment and so was the group with the lawyer and Colress.

"Dr. Colress? What are you doing on this island?" asked Oak with surprise upon seeing him arrive at the campsite.

"I was invited by Mr. Delavita." The scientist gave a cordial dip of his head.

"Oh yes," said Rowan, with a hint of skepticism in his voice, "didn't you formerly work for Team Plasma...?"

"That was some time ago," Colress dismissed with ease, "In any case, Team Plasma and the civil war in Unova is past history now."

"I presume you're here for your own study on the wildlife?"

"Tangentially. My current research is focused elsewhere. That said, I'm aware the old literature has some fascinating implications," Colress noted. "Supposedly all the animals on this island have unique characteristics only observed here."

"Unfortunately at the same time modern taxonomical research was making strides, this region was cut off from mainland civilization," Oak explained, "so it was impossible to scientifically categorize the wildlife in proper terms. It will be interesting to finally observe them firsthand."

At this point, Archer walked up to the delegation. "Colress! Hello," he greeted the scientist with a handshake.

"Hello Archer, you're looking well," Colress replied.

"Doing my best as usual." Archer then added, "I hate to interrupt this reunion of sorts but Giovanni asks to speak with you, Dr. Colress."

"Indeed, well we mustn't keep him waiting. Lead the way Archer," the scientist motioned with a wave of his hand and Archer walked ahead to Giovanni's yacht.

At the meeting with Giovanni, Colress looked over the stolen weaponry blueprints and gave his opinions on them. Afterwards, he was invited by the Team Rocket don to dine aboard the yacht during the lunch hour.

The delegation in turn were offered an abundant luncheon at the future hotel site that was already partially built. It had a terrace overlooking the sea, which was where the food was served and where they were supposed to gather and sign documents.

Technically, of course, Rocket Enterprises should never have begun construction without the delegation's approval. They had to affirm any development would have little effect on the island cloistered environment with its unique Pokémon species or whatever it was they were supposed to protect. However, when had that ever stopped Team Rocket? For that matter, they weren't supposed to be out catching wildlife from the forest yet, but the grunts had already probably caught at least a hundred by now. Any complaint lodged by a delegation member to that effect would probably be the last they'd ever file.

Archer snickered slyly at the mere thought.

About a couple of hours had passed when he wandered outside and heard a commotion coming from the direction of the hotel site. Archer looked over with boredom. "What now?" he asked a Team Rocket minion who was walking by.

"The delegation is infighting," was the reply.

"Infighting? What the fuck! All they have to do is sign the damn papers Giovanni told them to! Are they suicidal?"

"Sir, it seems that the two professors don't see eye to eye on some issues." The minion saluted and walked on.

"I sure am curious to see what the fuck it's all about," Archer spoke aloud to himself.

"I'm heading there myself," said a familiar voice. Archer turned to see Colress behind him. "Come along if you like."

Archer had to see this for himself, so he followed Colress over to where the Pokémon professors were seated on the newly built seaside terrace. Zoe's pet Pengullet was sitting atop the coffee table in the middle, happily munching on some berries from the centerpiece basket.

Professor Oak was speaking. "These are regional forms and we need to classify them in taxonomy as such."

"In that you're incorrect," insisted Rowan. "They are distinct species."

"Professor Rowan, I agree they've developed natural adaptations to survive here, adaptations which also happen to have been observed in otherwise unrelated species. However, this does not make these animals distinct species."

"Granted, they may have hybridization somewhere along their meta-evolutional lines..."

"Oh, so now they're hybrids?" Oak challenged. He gestured towards Pengullet, which looked at him blankly. "That is quite clearly a form of Piplup."

Rowan was undeterred. "Piplup are native to the Sinnoh region where I have lived my whole life. That is not a Piplup. It lacks downy feathers."

"The Piplup we have known till now are only found in northern climates, so it stands to reason those that found themselves stranded in the tropics would, over time, lose their down to compensate for the temperature."

"Nonsense. It's simply another avian." Rowan replied firmly. "Professor Oak, you would not call a Meowth and a Purrloin regional forms of each other merely because they are both members of the cat family and inhabit the same position in their respective habitats?"

Oak frowned, but stood his ground. "The Meowth and Purrloin lines have entirely different classifications and appearance and diverged in prehistoric times. One could say their primary ancestor had more in common with Mew than either of them."

"If I might intrude," said Colress, straightening his eyeglasses, "why don't we simply do a genetic analysis of the creatures and compare them to known samples before debating the proper vernacular?"

Both Oak and Rowan scoffed at this.

"That wouldn't be nearly as fun as debating the issue," said Oak.

"Nor as philosophical," agreed Rowan.

"Perhaps, but it would be far more efficient," Colress replied.

Archer, far from defusing the situation, decided to add fuel to the fire. "Besides," interjected Archer with a smile, "...it's damn obvious what's what on the island." He placed a Pal Sphere on the coffee table.

"Would you say this is a Poké Ball?" he asked the professors.

"Now, let's not start another frivolous debate we all know the answer to," Rowan dismissed.

"Do we?" questioned Oak, raising an eyebrow.

"Anyway. Your little dispute here isn't going to impede the signing of Giovanni's documents, I trust," added Archer, glancing pointedly from one to the other.

"Oh certainly not," they both jumped to say.

They knew very well what Team Rocket expected of them. Archer was only a tad disappointed that he wouldn't have an excuse to beat someone up over being dumb.

Archer continued watching them bicker for a while longer. He really didn't know what to think of this show. Even considering his own personal convictions that the island animals had undeniable familiarity, after having watched this scientific spat go on fruitlessly between Oak and Rowan for practically the entire day they had been here, Archer was getting fed up with it and found himself wanting everyone to come to a truce and just agree Piplup and Pengullet were damned penguins.

In the midst of this, Kris came over to talk to the professors.

"Excuse me," she said, "Do any of you have an expertise in Pokémon breeding...?"

"Dear girl, we both can be considered as having expertise in all facets of Pokémon," Rowan said.

Kris didn't question the statement and jumped right in to say her piece. "My Eevee has been very friendly with one of the Cremis here on the island...I think it's a girl. My Eevee is a boy..."

"Well that makes sense," replied Oak, with a sideways glare at Rowan, "if they both perceive they are of equal species."

"Well, now they have an egg," Kris added.

That was all she had to say. The professors immediately dropped everything and ran to see her Pokémon. Archer followed at a more leisurely pace.

They found Cremis curled around an egg and a determined Eevee guarding them both. It growled when it saw the bunch of people approaching to warn them not to get too close.

"A-ha!" Oak exclaimed, "Definitive, conclusive proof that Cremis is a regional form of Eevee."

"Now now," Rowan rushed to reply, "this only shows that they happen to be categorized in the same egg group. Remember the Skitty and Wailord genetic study?"

"That was theoretical nonsense," countered Oak. "This is the real thing."

"It merits further investigation before we jump to any conclusions," Rowan insisted.

Archer meanwhile had dollar signs in his eyes. "This is excellent," he said, turning towards his sister. "Kris, bring the Cremis back to the mainland with us. If their kits inherit the shiny color, you keep breeding them and our organization will make a fortune."

Both Oak and Rowan shot to attention at this.

"You can't be considering selling these! Their offspring could be a potential scientific breakthrough!" Rowan protested.

"Whether they're regional forms or separate species, these are not common Pokémon," Oak added.

"Professors, might I remind you both who owns this island? ...and everything inhabiting it?" Archer posed a veiled threat.

His statement visibly made both of them meek, to Archer's contentment. They turned back to the egg.

"Has anyone other than you, Kris, tried to pet them?" asked Oak.

"Actually...no." Kris answered, "but you can try."

Oak bent down closer to the little animals and slowly tried to pet them. This made Eevee growl louder.

Rowan then tried his luck at petting them, and Cremis snapped at him. He jumped back rubbing his hand.

They all then glanced almost hopefully at Archer, who shook his head. "I'm not even going to try," he said.

Dr. Colress came by at the moment, and noticing the nest and the two Pokémon, reached in without hesitation and petted them both. Eevee and Cremis began to purr loudly.

"How come only Colress can examine them?" demanded Rowan.

Kris shrugged. "What can I say? They like Colress."

By late afternoon Giovanni summoned the delegation members, his lawyer who was acting as notary, and a few others to witness the document signing, which was required to make his purchase of the isle official. There was a table outside on the beach, under a cloth awning held up by four stakes in the ground; on the table was the document with six pens lined up in a row, a bottle of red wine with several goblets, and a small vase with hibiscus flowers that gave off a somewhat cheerful ambiance.

Everyone was silently waiting around here for Giovanni to give a signal of sorts to begin the event, and no one broke this uneasy vigil till he emerged from the office aboard his yacht accompanied by his private guards Jessie and James.

"Let's get this done," ordered the leader of Team Rocket. He motioned to the two professors and they approached the table. Giovanni handed Professor Oak a pen and his lawyer pointed to a spot on the paper for him to sign. He did so quickly. The same was done for Professor Rowan, who signed with a slight tremble of his hand. Next, Giovanni took a pen for himself and signed the document, which effectively made him responsible for the island and its upkeep, and then Jessie and James put their signatures to paper as the two required witnesses. Last but not least, the lawyer signed to officially recognize the entire transaction.

Giovanni opened the bottle of wine, poured drinks for everyone and raising his glass, offered a toast. "To the prosperous future of Rocket Enterprises. Saluté."

"Saluté," repeated everyone. The two professors shook hands with Giovanni and headed off to an awaiting helicopter that would take them home to the mainland, while everyone else went on with their day. As the sun began its descent in the evening sky, Giovanni and his lawyer returned to the don's office to discuss business.

Palpagos Island was now officially and legally Team Rocket territory, regardless of whatever claims Marcus Dryden may have still had to the contrary.

During the days Archer and Zoe had been in Lumiose, Marcus Dryden had not been sighted by Team Rocket or Syndicate scouting parties anywhere. A state of unease prevailed; everyone in Team Rocket knew they had not seen the last of their enemies and it was only a matter of time before there would be a hit.

Elsewhere, their plans had been proceeding without a hitch. They'd seized the town of Fisherman's Point from the PIDF soldiers guarding it, who put up a fight but were ultimately vanquished in a couple of days, and were currently locked in battle around Feybreak Cove; it was generally assumed that if Marcus was hiding out anywhere, it was there. In the meantime, as a result of the tumblestone and gold that were so easy to come by and the crude oil they were extracting in abundance, Team Rocket had a very good supply of plasteel by now; enough to not only produce the weapons outlined in the supply drop blueprints but also to start manufacturing Master Balls back home. Giovanni was pleased, and Archer was happy to see his godfather's longtime plans coming to fruition.

Archer had been busy all that next morning, so it was mid-afternoon when he was free of any pending duties and went to see what Colress was up to.

He found the scientist talking with Jessie, James, and Meowth about the results of testing done on prototype plasteel weapons devised from the stolen schematics. Archer joined the conversation, interested for an update.

"Looks like everything's been going well," James summarized the discussion. "The laser rifles work, the laser gatling guns work; about the only thing that's fucked up is the laser sword."

"Why is the sword fucked up?" Archer asked.

Colress adjusted his eyeglasses and explained in more detail. "Igniting the energy beam causes a forward burst of kinetic energy far greater than an average weapon's recoil, which can cause the user to lose their footing and accidentally strike themselves with the ray, to say nothing of the manual difficulty in wielding such an apparatus afterwards."

"So... what you're saying is we should spend our resources making the kick-ass rifles and gatling guns, and forego the swords. That's cool," Archer decided. "I'll inform Giovanni. He'll probably want to start munitions production as soon as possible."

All effort was hereby focused on making these weapons, an effort which James, Jessie, and Meowth commandeered with gusto. The weapons produced from this effort would be moved out of the camp.

"...to the oil rig?" Archer questioned dubiously when he'd first heard of the plan. "We'd be making three times the effort."

"For four times the payoff." Giovanni was already decided in this. "The oil rig is harder to reach, being isolated in the sea, and whenever our enemies have tried to attack us they come by land. The plasteel weapons should be safer out there until we have a sufficient stockpile for our use."

So it was that the first batch of weapons were moved out to the oil rig, a total of about ten prototype plasteel rifles, which were flown over during the night.

Archer meanwhile was tasked with organizing the hunting parties that routinely went out around noon. These were meant to catch wild Pokémon to be sold back on the mainland, yet they served a second purpose, which was patrolling the outlying woodland for any sign of their enemies.

As he and his little group set out for the woods that day, he caught sight of James and Jessie helping transport a crate of newly-crafted plasteel blocks from one side of the encampment to the other, with a supervising Meowth padding behind them and occasionally yowling some critique. Archer held himself back from some tongue-in-cheek comment.

At least if he had to be assigned somewhere other than the conquest of towns, it was to go hunting. There was only so much of the mundane Archer personally could stand at their encampment, of watching buildings being constructed and plasteel being crafted, before he got fed up and wanted some action. To him the charm of their activities on Palpagos Island was, ironically, the warfare; the vengeful impunity of shooting enemies with his trusty Pokémon by his side. Not having to play around laws like Team Rocket might have to do in a more civilized region meant they could be as vicious as they wanted to be here. The day-to-day monotony of materiel production was secondary entertainment at best and a boring necessity at worst.

That said, he knew the trio rather enjoyed the relative peace and quiet here at the encampment. To each his own, he figured.

Archer motioned to his hunting party, and they headed out.

All things considered, their hunting expedition started out smoothly. They followed the main trail out of the encampment, but soon veered off the path into the ferns and brambles where the wildlife might better conceal itself.

They hadn't gone very far into the forest before they spied their first Pal along the side of a thicket.

It looked like an autumn-coat Deerling, but it had a long bushy tail and a tuft of flame on its forehead. It was standing below a young tree, gnawing on small, low-hanging branches it was blackening with the low embers of its breath.

"We call that kind of Pal a Rooby," Zoe told him.

"All right," said Archer, readying a Poké Ball to throw, "that one, Frostallion. Try to weaken it."

Frostallion neighed and unleashed a powerful scythe of ice. The Rooby bounded away and the attack instead knocked squarely into the tree, which creaked and tumbled backwards. It crashed loudly into the bushes.

Frostallion looked ready to race into battle, but to its chagrin Archer held it back. "You battle instead," he ordered one of the minions, who dutifully sent out a Raticate.

The large rodent sprang at the deer, which swatted it back with a sharp burst of flame. Their sparring went on for about a minute before the Rooby had been sufficiently tired out, and a Poké Ball was flung at it; the sphere shook once or twice but marked a successful capture.

As the minion stepped forward to collect the Poké Ball, Archer was busy scowling at the fallen tree. He looked back at Frostallion, which had straightened its posture with undeniable pride in its power. "Okay, I know you've got a war-horse's pedigree, but we're going to have to practice measuring the strength of your attacks; otherwise I'll never be able to enter you in sporting battles. An attack that unrestrained might've killed the damn thing."

Frostallion snorted in reply.

"You might be good to take along on Team Rocket hits, though," Archer considered casually, which seemed to cheer up the horse. It began prancing about and shaking its icy mane.

As the afternoon progressed they managed to catch several species; some that Archer had seen before, and some new ones that he wasn't quite sure of – save for his usual summation of the creature by those traits he could find a mainland comparison to – but all of which Zoe was readily able to identify for him as per the island lingo.

The forest was calm as ever, and sunlight stretched beautiful warm rays through the leaves. As they wandered through the woods in search of wildlife, they came across a treasure chest lying in the middle of nowhere.

Houndoom, which Archer had sent out in lieu of Frostallion, got one look at the treasure chest and started barking at it.

"What the fuck is this?" asked one of the Team Rocket grunts, standing over the chest. It looked like it was made of some kind of ivory bearing a strange bronze sheen, its outline etched in the same blue hues of raw tumblestone. Most unique of all, two triangular protrusions rose from the top of the lid, seemingly resembling an animal's ears.

"This looks expensive," added a second minion, joining the first. "Or old. Or both."

"I think the word you're looking for is antique...?"

One of the other minions was poking it with a stick. "I bet some pirates left gold in that."

"You got one hell of an imagination, Jeanne."

"Well, what would you put in there? It's obviously a treasure chest."

Archer gave it a skeptical look. "Or it could be a mine," he pointed out dryly.

This did not dissuade the minions in the slightest. "There doesn't seem to be a lock on it," said one.

"Hey, Harold? See if you can whack it open."

This seemed to put Houndoom on high alert, and suddenly the Pokémon sprang in front of the chest growling to bar their way to it. A few of the minions stepped back nervously.

"Um... Archer. What's with your Houndoom?"

"I don't think Houndoom wants you people hitting that thing."

"Why? It's just an old chest of some kind."

"Or...it could be a fucking mine," Archer said with emphasis, "which the enemy put there knowing you're a bunch of imbeciles who'd try to open the damn thing."

Zoe wandered over. "That's a Mimog."

"What the hell is a Mimog?"

She placed some berries in front of it and motioned to them to retreat a short distance into the bushes.

They waited patiently. Sure enough the chest cracked open slightly, and then it seemed to spring to life, pulling little brown paws out from underneath itself as well as a matching, wagging tail. From inside both halves of its shell came a long tongue, with which it lapped up the berries with glee, and then tucked its paws and tail back inside and settled down again. The 'lid' of the treasure chest closed once more.

Archer turned to face Zoe. "Don't tell me. Just like we have land-sharks, this is a land-Shellder."

"They act more like little dogs," she said cheerfully.

"If you say so."

"They don't hurt anything. In fact, Mimog rarely even want to battle...they try to run first," Zoe explained.

He was debating the merits of throwing a Poké Ball at it versus laying a trail of berries back to the base, or whether they even needed one of these Mimogs at all, when he heard shooting from over the slope and turned sharply. "What was that?" and then, more urgently, "Where's Ray?"

One of the Team Rocket grunts was indeed missing, the one who had aided in catching the Rooby earlier. With realization, Archer darted out of the bushes towards the hill with Zoe and the others following him closely.

They reached the top of the hill in time to see what transpired; there was a battle between a group of at least ten trainers and their missing minion, which had culminated in one of the former pulling out a gun and shooting the latter dead.

His Raticate angled an ear back and, seeing its trainer fall to the ground, abandoned the fight in an attempt to flee. One of the others gave a shout, and an electric type creature – something like a small fairy wreathed in a misty grey thundercloud – attacked with a burst of electricity. Seized with paralysis the Raticate slumped to the grass, shivering.

Sheltered behind the cloak of bracken and trees, Archer, Zoe, and the rest of the hunting party watched every move of their enemies below. Interestingly enough, none of the trainers below wore the uniforms of PIDF infantrymen.

"Mercenaries no doubt," said Zoe, "there are always Pal tamers on Palpagos Island who seek fortune and can be hired."

"They're going to get more than they bargained for," Archer muttered as he watched them push the paralyzed Raticate into a cage. They took it with them as they proceeded down the road, unaware of their observers.

"Zoe, you and the others take Ray's body and head back to our encampment," Archer instructed, "Tell Giovanni what has happened. I'm going to follow those assholes and learn where their hideout is."

His Houndoom trotted along with him at his heels. The dog was as furtive as its trainer, bearing a natural subtlety inherent in all dark type Pokémon; it knew innately how to hide in the shadows. They trailed their enemies all the way to a sprawling meadow beside a creek, where a campsite had been set up.

Archer lingered at the boulders and tree-line, observing the activity below. It reminded him somewhat of the Syndicate's old encampment near their tower, with a campfire in the center and tents scattered about. These tents, however, were of a decidedly new fabric, and nothing there looked handmade but instead of the finest quality camping materials brought direct from the mainland regions.

The mercenary trainers entered the encampment, placing the cage with the stolen Raticate down on the grass. The scent of a stew wafted over from where a cooking pot was suspended over the campfire, and Archer could see other trainers in civilian garb who were lingering around the fire impatient for mealtime. Several Pals were also in the camp, protecting the area. Everyone gathered there looked like seasoned trainers and all the Pokémon they had out of their spheres looked to be at very high levels.

Marcus was nowhere to be seen.

Archer had about decided to head back to tell Giovanni where they were so they could launch an attack, when inexplicably he felt a chill like ice race up his spine.

Beside him, Houndoom had started growling. He did little more than turn and found himself surrounded by three strange creatures.

He didn't even quite know how to describe them – they were black, owl-like creatures, but seemed to have no feathers. They had a shell-like covering on their face similar to a Yamask and a slight sheen of energy that made him guess they must likewise be ghost types, but he wasn't sure.

For a moment Archer merely faced the creatures, which stared back at him with intentions concealed. Before he could make a move, they attacked.

Archer decided they were definitely related to Yamask. Their manner of attack was equal to the ghost type's evolution, but their form was even more grotesque. In the manner of a ghost Pokémon, or even a bug Pokémon, they suddenly produced many tendrils seemingly from nowhere and lashed at him with pincers, while their facial covering morphed into a crescent of pointed teeth. They sprang, snapping at him, while Archer had to jump back to avoid the monstrous beasts that were now howling as a group.

Without waiting for Archer's command, Houndoom unleashed an Inferno attack that spread outwards from its paws in a rush of fire. It hit against all three of the creatures at once; they backed away a short distance and redirected their attention away from Archer and onto Houndoom.

The commotion drew the attention of the enemy camp. Archer could hear orders being shouted, mostly in the island language, and running footsteps alongside weapons being loaded.

These damned things must have been sent by them to guard the forest perimeter, Archer thought, seeing how the ghostly creatures now spread out as if they were less interested in fighting him per se and more in preventing his escape.

Houndoom shot a second volley of fire at the Pals, causing them to bound out of the way before retaliating with their garish attacks. Archer could see how his Pokémon was faltering under the onslaught, and in a swift movement he was able to recall Houndoom to its Poké Ball and send out Frostallion.

"All right Frostallion," Archer ordered, "remember how I was telling you to restrain your power? That goes out the window here! Hit as hard as you can."

The Pegasus took one look at its multiple opponents and reared up whinnying, emboldened by the challenge. It raced forwards with ice on its outstretched wings, catching three of the ghost Pals and hurling them against the tree trunks before they could teleport away. One tried to bite, only to get kicked by Frostallion and fall with a whimper to the ground.

Archer meanwhile was marvelling at Frostallion's power and reminding himself that for all the Pal looked like an icy Rapidash with wings, it was classed as a Legendary here and had the strength that came with it. This must be the kind of fun Kris has commanding her Suicune, he reflected.

Within less than a minute the enemy creatures had been defeated. The mercenaries, who had come rushing over ready to fight, were now having second thoughts about their next actions – especially when Archer swung about towards them and Frostallion responded to the implicit order. It shot a single Ice Beam into the crowd, throwing them in disarray. One man was struck headlong with the attack and tumbled to the ground in a cloud of frost and ice, and Archer immediately snatched up the gun he'd held, and noticed the dead man was the same one who had killed Ray. "Divine justice," he said out loud.

Archer turned quickly to face the others but before he could shoot any of them, they threw up their hands disarmingly.

"Spare us! The PIDF put us up to this," one of them implored. "They offered us a good sum of gold if we could get rid of the outsiders."

"...you didn't spare Ray back there," Archer replied dryly.

"We'll give back the Pal we took and tell you everything we know."

For the moment at least, Archer decided to humor them, especially considering Team Rocket did lack information on the PIDF's movements and any bit of intelligence on that front would help. Frostallion looked eager to flatten the lot of them under a barrage of its ice attacks but instead it obediently paced back and forth, its wings flared as a threat, ensuring no one there tried anything.

So far, so good, thought Archer, who recalled the stolen Raticate to its Poké Ball as the cage was brought forth. He turned back towards the prisoners.

"Where is Marcus Dryden?" he asked.

"On his way with his army to raid your group."

Archer smirked. "He ought to know by now that our camp is too heavily guarded."

"Not the camp, the oil rig."

"The oil rig?"

"He spoke of weapons your group has made, which he wanted to steal," the mercenary said. "He knows these items were moved from your camp last night because he sent scouts to spy. He also knows that your leader Giovanni will be going on the oil rig today and plans to coincide with him there."

Fuck, thought Archer, If this is true, I've got to get back and let everyone know – fast.

Chapter 26 - Oil Rig Assault ✅

Archer raced towards the camp on Frostallion, as quick as he could, hoping to get there before Giovanni departed. When he got there, he first encountered Zoe.

"Archer, thank God you're back. I was worried," said Zoe, as he drew the horse to an abrupt halt before her.

"No need. Frostallion singlehandedly flattened all their Pokémon...or is it single-hoofed? Anyway, we got the Raticate back. Where's Giovanni?" he asked.

"By the time we got here he'd left for the oil rig," she replied. "James, Jessie, and Meowth went with him...I think your sister Kris did, as well."

"Damn it," Archer cursed. He surveyed the encampment swiftly; there were sufficient guards, however there were less than usual, and the squadrons that had been sent out to seize the towns had not returned yet. "...and this makes it even worse! We've only got about enough people here to defend the camp, not to come along with us for a counter-offensive."

Zoe blinked with confusion. "What's going on?"

"Marcus is planning to attack the oil rig," Archer related the information in a hurry. "He's taking the bulk of his army to try to raid the platform and steal the plasteel weapons we've got stashed there."

"The oil rig? But I thought that place was a floating fortress. Won't it be a losing battle?"

"Not if he has a strategy planned out, and from the sound of things he does. There's no time to waste," Archer declared. "If I get there fast enough, maybe I can warn Giovanni."

"I'm coming too," she told him, pulling herself up on Frostallion's back to sit behind Archer.

He started to protest, yet she was adamant.

"In case you don't get there fast enough," Zoe explained, "my Pals and I can help you as backup."

Archer gave a sharp nod; it made sense. "Frostallion, towards the seashore," he directed, and Frostallion, with a reciprocating neigh, stretched its broad wings and took flight.

If there was any outcome of Team Rocket's arrival that was truly a testament to both modern engineering and their undying quest for profit, it was their offshore oil rig.

Far enough from the island that it could not disturb any beach-goers, close enough that it could be seen like a figment upon the waves, it was in many ways the crowning glory of their regional conquest. They'd devised a fully functional structure in days that commonly took months to build, thanks to the fact Giovanni spared no expense in what he felt would be a profitable investment.

Archer and Zoe rode on Frostallion all the way over to the oil rig. As they were nearing the platform, they could see the deck sprawling before them with the massive derrick rising high, as well as two laser turrets that had been added on either end of the structure since they'd started manufacturing plasteel – they weren't strong enough to kill, but they'd give any unwanted visitors enough burns to make them second-guess their intrusion. A heliport on the far side accommodated either Giovanni's helicopter or a larger one to shuttle any workers who didn't have flying Pokémon to and from the island.

They also saw the cause of the distant glow and noise; everyone below was engaged in combat, with several Pokémon in the middle of a fight and people shooting at each other.

Frostallion whinnied and Archer looked up in time to see one of their own laser turrets charging and pointed at them.

"Down!" he cried, and the horse narrowly flew towards the sea as the laser blasted overhead trying to strike them. They crashed into the water, and Frostallion neighed a protest.

"Those bastards took over our own security system," scowled Archer, returning Frostallion to its Poké Ball.

"How are we going to get over there?" asked Zoe.

Archer evaluated the oil rig. From here they could hear the sounds of war on the deck yet no one seemed to realize they were in the water right below, wading about the massive pillars that held up the platform.

In the midst of him weighing a strategy, there was a sudden flash of light and what should appear by them but several Unowns. They squeaked a greeting to the couple.

Archer stared in surprise. "The Unowns? Why are you...no, nevermind..." he decided, and pointed up to the oil rig platform. "Can you get us up there?"

The Unowns squeaked again and, surrounding Archer and Zoe, instantly teleported them up to the platform.

As he'd expected – Marcus' PIDF forces. No sooner had Archer and Zoe warped there did one of the enemy soldiers notice them, and Archer in turn spied him right when he was aiming his rifle.

Archer pulled Zoe to the ground and she gasped as gunfire pelted the metal wall behind them. He opened a Poké Ball and sent out Houndoom.

"Faint Attack!" he cried, and Houndoom leapt with a snarl at the man. The dog tackled him backwards in a bright flare of violet energy, knocking the weapon from his hands.

The soldier's shout drew the attention of his comrades; Archer grabbed the whip from his belt right as Zoe sent out her Grizzbolt. At a single motion from Zoe, Grizzbolt sent forth a powerful barrage of electricity, while Archer struck out with his whip at the nearest enemy as he lifted a gun to fire at them. The lash cut across the soldier's face and caused him to misfire.

It provided enough of a commotion that Archer and Zoe were able to duck for cover behind a storage shed. Grizzbolt and Houndoom stood alongside each other, fighting together with the perfectly timed attacks one might see in a double battle on the mainland, albeit with more ferocity. In between electric bolts and fiery waves the two animals were able to keep all the enemy soldiers at bay.

A familiar sound caught their ears; the screech of a hawk. Archer first saw the streak of fire sweep past the derrick, and then as he followed its flight he was able to discern exactly what – who – it was.

It was Marcus Dryden, who was sitting astride his Faleris as they oversaw the battle from mid-air.

Looks like the colonel's here to command his army personally this time, thought Archer.

At any other time this would have filled him with a surge of excitement for the battle; now it only made him uneasy. There were so many enemies here, Archer imagined it must be the PIDF's entire army that had been sent to rid the island of them once and for all. Even with their own united numbers of both Team Rocket and Syndicate members, they seemed to be evenly matched at best.

Archer was starting to think that having asked the Unown to teleport him and Zoe up here was a bad idea. He'd initially wanted to reclaim the laser turrets, and then find Giovanni; his plans were quickly being shelved in favor of survival. They were being swamped.

"Suicune, Bubble Beam!"

He recognized his sister's voice right as a powerful stream of bubbles shot past, which collided with one of the enemy soldiers and knocked him off his feet.

He turned to see Kris running towards them with her Suicune. Suicune roared and sent forth another current of bubbles to push back the enemy soldiers as Kris reached his and Zoe's side.

"Need some help?" she smiled.

"Kris, thank God!" he exclaimed, "I've never been happier to see you and that Suicune of yours. Where's Giovanni?"

"He went to the chopper. You need to find Jessie and James; Giovanni sent them to defend our munitions stockpile, but there are so many invaders they're probably going to need help to chase them off. Meowth went to hit some kind of emergency button in the control room that shuts off the oil extraction, so that any fires up here won't reach the oil well and explode this whole place." She turned back to command her Pokémon on the battlefield. "Keep up the Bubble Beams, Suicune!"

Archer motioned to Zoe for her to follow him, and they recalled their Pokémon leaving the battle to Kris' Suicune while they made their way across the platform, keeping low behind the storage containers and evading gunfire when they were forced to dart into the open.

"The munitions chest is across from the heliport," Archer said, as they hid behind a stack of big industrial pipes, "We'll get there faster if we get up the stairwell to the uppermost level, and then skip across the tops of the storage containers there."

The stairwell in question was currently blocked by a group of battling Pals, a Direhowl against three Leezpunk; meanwhile their trainers, apparently having run out of bullets, were now grappling with each other using their fists. It was the energy blasts Archer was most worried about getting struck by; every time one of the animals dodged an attack, the flare would sear past and strike whatever happened to be behind them.

Archer grabbed Zoe's hand and they made a run for it right as the Direhowl tackled one of the Leezpunk and the other two sprang onto its back, and they managed to get past unnoticed and then race up the steps.

They emerged to the top level of the oil rig platform to find this area also in the midst of war. The stairwell opened out with a clear view of the heliport, but Giovanni's aircraft was nowhere to be seen as Archer and Zoe swiftly crossed over a railing and descended the nearby stack of storage containers. Part of the paramilitary training Team Rocket's admins went through taught them to leap skillfully across barriers in a gymnastic way like parkour, so for Archer this was second nature, but even considering Zoe's training had not delved so far she was surprisingly light on her feet and kept up with him easily.

Reaching the bottom row, Archer heard an explosion; he turned towards the sound and quickly spied Jessie and James.

They were poised on top of a shipping container, holding a bazooka on their shoulders. The explosion had come from the couple firing their weapon on a group of invaders who had, apparently without much forethought, thought they could rush them.

As he watched, he saw a flash of cream fur zip across the deck towards them; it was Meowth, who'd apparently been successful in his mission to hit the emergency cut-off button. The cat was running as fast as he could on all fours, and when he reached the edge of the blast area, he took a leap to clear the debris and landed right at James and Jessie's heels.

Archer and Zoe wove through the fray and joined the trio. "Archer, Zoe, we didn't expect to see you two here," Jessie remarked. "What, not enough excitement back at the camp?"

"We saw something was going on from the seashore and came flying over to see," explained Zoe.

"How did these people get aboard?" Archer asked.

"Overnight," replied James. "Apparently they used water Pokémon to swim across and grappling guns to rappel up here."

Meowth chimed in indignantly, "The dimwits who were supposed to be keepin' lookout at the laser guns decided to take a catnap on the job. The boss was really pissed when he was boarding the chopper and told us to dismiss 'em both as possible spies."

"We've dealt with it already," said Jessie simply.

Archer gave a brisk nod as he surveyed the platform before them. They appeared to be making some headway, at least on this part of the oil rig, but he could see another wave of enemies fighting across the way and trying to advance. "Besides stealing our new weapons, what is it they want? To explode the rig or capture it?"

"At this point, we think they just want to take it. If they'd wanted to blow the place up, they'd probably have bombs going off by now," said James.

Jessie, meanwhile, had been checking their provisions. "James, we're running out of ammo."

"Already...? Shit," he muttered.

Archer looked at them dumbfounded. "You've got a fucking munitions chest right there."

Meowth yowled. "Where'd ya think we got the rockets for our bazooka from?"

A screech split the air, and they looked up to see Marcus and Faleris had flown nearer to where they were. The large hawk had unleashed a Fire Spin attack; the whirlwind of fire had slammed directly into some smaller Pokémon trying to keep it at bay, and hurled them along with one of their trainers into the ocean below. The man screamed as he plummeted off of the oil rig.

"He's pretty bold coming out here himself," commented Jessie as they watched him circle around to assail the other trainers.

"Not bold; he just knows he can't be hit," said Archer.

Zoe elaborated, "Marcus has got some kind of a barrier that makes him impervious to attack."

"You mean his Faleris knows Protect," said James.

"No," Archer told them, "it looks like some sort of artificial Protect barrier, like the ones used at stadiums to protect the audience from stray Pokémon attacks. I've had clear shots of the bastard the past couple of times I've faced him in battle and haven't been able to break through it."

Jessie narrowed her eyes. "If it's an artificial shield, then all we have to do is get it away from him."

She motioned to James and Meowth, and they lifted the bazooka back onto their shoulders. The trio shot directly at Faleris.

Clouds of fire roared outwards in the impulse, yet Archer could make out the energy shield that glittered around Marcus to protect him from the blast, a honeycomb barrier shimmering in shades of gold.

The explosion pushed Faleris backwards. Marcus nearly lost his grip on the hawk; while trying to regain his balance, he dropped the shield device he'd had clipped to his vest pocket.

It was a small device, no bigger than the transceivers used as cell phones on the mainland. Before Marcus could snatch the shield back up from the ground, Meowth sprang to destroy it with a powerful swipe of claws. The cat's attack sheared the device in half.

Irate, Marcus redirected Faleris with a gesture to attack Meowth. As Faleris swooped down to strike with its talons, Meowth raced agilely out of the way; James and Jessie meanwhile tossed Poké Balls to send out their other two Pokémon, Arbok and Weezing, shouting orders to attack the bird.

While Marcus was contending with Jessie, James, and Meowth – and failing miserably in the endeavor – Archer sprang down to where the munitions chest was. Zoe joined him.

To think they'd thought the oil rig would be a good place to stash their plasteel weapons. They'd imagined the encampment would be raided, never this stronghold. In retrospect it had been shortsighted.

They only had a few working prototypes thus far; Archer flung open the chest lid and retrieved one of the laser rifles. It was a rectangular contrivance that looked objectively bulky to hold, yet it was surprisingly lightweight and the energy cartridges it used for ammunition snapped in smoothly.

"What better time to try this out," decided Archer, spinning around to face the oncoming onslaught of PIDF soldiers.

He aimed the rifle and fired. Bursts of orange light streaked outward in straight lines, hitting their enemies; it burnt straight through their armor, and they shouted as they collapsed. The animals advancing with them lingered back a distance to see this, but they fired their own energy attacks in response anyway. Archer pulled Zoe aside as brilliantly colored flares slashed past them and they flung out Poké Balls, summoning Houndoom and Grizzbolt again to battle. Houndoom's Protect shielded them from gunfire as Grizzbolt swatted one of the opponent Pals away, where it hit against one of the shipping containers and was immediately knocked out.

For a time, Archer and Zoe had gotten the advantage. At a distance, they could see James, Jessie, and Meowth at a stalemate against Marcus and Faleris; Arbok and Weezing's attacks were striking their mark, yet the colonel and his Pal were too strong for them to measurably weaken him, and Jessie and James were swift to recall their Pokémon whenever they were going to be hit directly in retaliation. Archer was planning to turn the laser rifle on Marcus as soon as they could beat their enemies back.

His plan was discarded when they ran out of energy cartridges for the laser rifle and were once again surrounded.

There were simply far too many of them to contend with, even with their own Pokémon trying to fight back. Archer stepped back apprehensively, cornered with the munitions chest behind him.

The sound of rotors slicing through the air made everyone turn to see the helicopter rising overhead, hovering above them with menace.

Archer smiled with dark knowledge.

Peering out of the helicopter's passenger window, Persian let out a hiss. His trainer Giovanni glanced nonchalantly at the pilot.

"Charge the cannons. Let's see what it can do."

"Yes sir," said the pilot firmly.

The laser flashed across the deck.

Archer had to shut his eyes from the glare. Heat blasted across his face; when the loud screech of the laser receded and he opened his eyes, all the enemies had been obliterated into ashes.

In the helicopter overhead, Giovanni grinned as he witnessed this and addressed the cat on his lap. "Five times as strong as a Hyper Beam. I think it's worth keeping…don't you agree, Persian?"

Persian purred.

Many on the ground had seen what Giovanni's helicopter was capable of. So had Marcus, who immediately directed his Pal's attention to a new target.

"Faleris, let's see what damage that combat helicopter can sustain. Aim for the tail rotor!"

Faleris dutifully obeyed and flew directly toward the helicopter, releasing a burst of fire as it swept past. The blast struck the tail rotor with such intensity that the boom sheared off and the helicopter lurched back.

Inside, Persian let out a caterwaul as Giovanni grabbed hold of his seat, the force of gravity pulling them hard to the side. The pilot scrambled to try to regain control of the aircraft, but wasn't fast enough before it twirled out of control.

Archer had turned away from the battle just in time to see the helicopter spinning violently in a wild, diagonal descent, a spectacle that ended when it crashed into the ocean and exploded.

He was stunned for a moment, and then he caught sight of Marcus flying overhead on Faleris, the spectre of mirth on his lips; any astonishment fled Archer at once and was supplanted by rage and vengeful hatred. The mere thought of his godfather Giovanni dying such a horrible, fiery death...!

"You bastard! You will pay for this!" he yelled at the top of his lungs, and sent out Frostallion.

"Archer – wait!" James said, but Archer had already mounted the horse and taken flight.

Marcus had turned Faleris about and was flying away from the oil rig and the helicopter's fiery wreckage, back towards Palpagos Island.

The asshole probably figures he got what he came for, Archer thought, Most likely he thinks that if Giovanni is dead, we'll back down. Clearly he doesn't realize how we operate... He owes me and Team Rocket now more than ever, and payment is overdue.

Chapter 27 - Ultimate Weapon ✅

Frostallion galloped over the ocean at Archer's behest, coursing on the sea wind like if it were a racetrack. Up ahead, Archer could see Marcus flying directly towards the island shore on Faleris' back.

"You think I'm letting you get away that easy, you asshole?" Archer muttered. He certainly wouldn't permit it; not after Marcus had killed his godfather. He was going to settle accounts once and for all.

As he neared his enemy, Archer had already planned out a battle strategy and had concluded the odds of victory as being greatly in his favor. Faleris was a bird; all flying types were weak to ice.

"Ice Beam," he commanded.

Frostallion opened its mouth and sent forth a frozen blast, which struck Faleris squarely across the wing.

The ice beam seemed to have no effect. The large hawk shook off the attack like snowfall and Marcus locked eyes with Archer.

Faleris must be a pure fire type, Archer realized with dread, …and that means we're the ones weak to it.

Marcus swung his arm upward, and Faleris immediately spun around to unleash a torrent of fire towards the ocean.

The water erupted into steam.

Frostallion whinnied and reared in mid-air. Archer searched the cloud desperately and reacted too late when he at last saw the outline of his foe in the mist.

Screeching a war-cry, Faleris struck out viciously with its talons as Archer nearly toppled from his mount; Frostallion struck back with its hooves and beating wings while Archer scrambled to keep hold of the horse's reins.

The whole world had become a tumult; sky and wind and water and feathers, all conspiring to cast him to his doom. He swung out with the whip, first once, then twice, and succeeded in entangling one of Faleris' legs in the lash.

Now it was Marcus' turn to struggle. Faleris squawked in protest, its wings flapping in an aimless and frantic attempt to get away; Frostallion tugged backward as Archer held on vengefully, putting all the effort his muscles could muster into not letting go.

When he saw Marcus pull out his revolver, Archer ducked against Frostallion's back. One gunshot rang out over him, then a second, then a third, then a fourth. Despite being so near to his target, Marcus could not get clear aim because of his own mount's desperation to get loose from where it was currently tangled.

He's only got two rounds left, Archer was thinking, the sound from the last shot still ringing in his ears from proximity.

The two creatures and their riders grappled futilely till at last exhaustion won out; Faleris collapsed onto the ground of Palpagos Island below. They had ended up in the ancient, forgotten city on the Astral Mountains.

Frostallion landed only a short distance away, still able to battle but just barely. The horse was heaving for breath as Archer watched his opponent like a wolf about to pounce, just waiting for Marcus to make a move.

When he didn't, evidently unsure how to either escape or regain the advantage, Archer got tired of waiting.

"Trample him into the ground, Frostallion," Archer ordered, as he whipped the reins for the horse to attack Marcus.

Marcus dove sideways as Frostallion forward, and the creature stumbled into a cluster of the red flowers and their dewy vines.

Archer tried to turn the horse to attack again, however the plants appeared to have a different idea. The vines had somehow wrapped themselves around Frostallion's hooves and inexplicably the fine dew they were covered in had become as unrelenting as glue.

Frostallion neighed and tried to lift into the air with its wings, but the vines entangled themselves further, almost as if they were actively trying to prevent it from fleeing, which only led to the horse getting frantic till Archer could calm it down.

Marcus took advantage of the distraction; he recalled Faleris to its Pal Sphere and ran away.

"You think this is over?" shouted Archer at his escaping enemy, "You owe Team Rocket, and we never write off debts."

He had to get down from the horse in order to untangle its hooves from the vines. The tendrils were surprisingly stubborn, and Archer was thankful they were all relatively young plants because they were small enough to rip through. With how tenacious these things are, I'd sure hate it if we'd stumbled into one of the bigger plants, Archer thought.

He flew back to the oil rig, mortified at how Marcus had gotten away from him and vowing to get revenge. It was only now that the magnitude of the helicopter crash was starting to sink in, and he felt miserable. What would become of Team Rocket without Giovanni?

His worries turned out for naught when he arrived and found his godfather on the platform with his Persian, entirely unharmed. He was accompanied by Jessie and James.

"Giovanni – you're okay! But how? I saw the helicopter explode!" Archer exclaimed with astonishment.

"The Unown appeared in the helicopter," Giovanni explained, "and teleported me, Persian, and the pilot down to safety."

As he spoke, he glanced over and Archer followed his gaze to see a cluster of happy Unowns nearby squeaking and twirling about.

"I gave chase after Marcus," Archer told him, "but Frostallion got caught in tendrils of those damn flower plants and the son of a bitch ran off!"

"We'll get him," Giovanni said confidently, "It's just a matter of time."

Archer looked around and said, "I see you eradicated everybody sent to attack us."

"We have another situation to deal with," Jessie spoke up. "All the prototype plasteel weapons were stolen in that battle."

Archer turned towards her with surprise. "How did that happen?"

"Distraction as a strategy," said James. "While our people were in battle, a select group stole them."

Giovanni frowned. "It was brilliantly executed, quite frankly." He faced Archer and added, "After you rest a bit from your ordeal, come to my office and give me a full report of what happened with Marcus. We need to start tracking him as soon as possible."

He turned and left, with Persian following. Archer looked around to the others, and just then noticed their ever-present cat was missing. "Where's Meowth?" he asked.

"Chatting with a Wooloo that defected," James replied.

"We have a defector?"

Meowth trotted over at that moment, accompanied by a round little sheep that looked intimidated by all the eyes now on it.

"Lamball here says they gots info on the PIDF's plans," Meowth yowled.

"Hopefully it's not a trick," Archer replied.

Meowth hissed at him. "Pokémon don't lie about this shit, unless we gots a good reason."

"But do Pals?" Archer prodded cynically. "If you'll forgive me from being skeptical, but I'm still sore about getting backstabbed by a monkey."

"Ffftt. That was a monkey. This is a sheep. And I'm a cat, so I'm perceptive."

"Okay, whatever," Jessie dismissed Archer's concerns with a wave as she turned back to the Lamball. "What've you got?"

"Marcus has what he feels is the ultimate weapon," the cat translated, "in addition to the Essence Condenser."

"Was the Pal Essence Condenser what Marcus had trapped the Unowns in?" James asked.

Archer jumped into the conversation. "Yeah, he said he was using it to draw energy from Pokémon and use it to power his ultimate weapon. The consensus was he wanted to increase Faleris' level that way. Probably a moot point now, since the Condenser has been destroyed."

"Lamball says that Marcus already did it," said Meowth, as the sheep went on bleating, "but it's not Faleris he wanted to make stronger. You're not going to believe what his so-called ultimate weapon is."

Jessie crossed her arms. "Try us."

"Little red flowers."

They all stared in confusion at the two animals, whereupon the Lamball tried to elaborate, and Meowth translated:

"Except when he zapped them with the energy he siphoned off all those Pokémon, they started growing into giant red flowers. He's planning to use 'em as his secret to victory. By the way, Marcus isn't on the island anymore."

"He's not?" Jessie asked in surprise.

"His plan was to swipe our plasteel lasers and fly directly to the Kalos region," the cat growled, "He thinks the plants over there should've grown big enough by this time to accomplish what he set out to do."

"I can't be the only one who doesn't understand what's the big deal with these plants. So what if they grow big? What does he expect, for them to overtake the city? or for all the Pokémon on the mainland to get ill from them? They're plants." Archer questioned.

"They're plants that eat things," the cat meowed.

"Are you saying they're carnivorous?" James asked.

"You got that right!" Meowth exclaimed.

"I better go talk to Giovanni," Archer said hurriedly, "He's waiting for me, but with this new information he's probably going to take action immediately."

Archer reached Giovanni's office as soon as he could run there, and his boss was surprised to see him arrive practically running. Nevertheless, Giovanni listened intently to all the new information and when Archer finished the account, he gave him his orders.

"Archer, your mission is to return to Lumiose. Take Zoe with you, and find Marcus Dryden... stop him once and for all."

"Yes sir."

Giovanni now turned to his Persian, which was sitting on his lap purring, and said, "Persian please summon associate Zoe Rayne...have her come to my office immediately, and bring the Unowns as well."

Persian meowed and leapt down from his lap, scampering off and returning within five minutes with both Zoe and the group of Unowns in tow.

"Zoe you're going on a mission as backup for Archer," Giovanni informed her, "He will fill you in on specifics."

The Unowns squeaked and circled around Archer and Zoe, warping them away to the Kalos region.

Jett hadn't been to her office at all that day.

She walked into the lobby of her office building to speak with the receptionist and check if she had any messages, and when she had done so, she released her Pansage, Tanzee, out of its Poké Ball. The grass type monkey appeared before her and very quickly grabbed a Sitrus Berry from a fruit bowl conveniently placed in the reception area for guests.

She addressed it, "Go up to the office. I'm going to come back with something special for you; it's a surprise."

Tanzee screeched happily and scampered off to the elevator. Swinging up by its tail, it poked the button itself for the penthouse level.

"Don't get into trouble while I'm out," she chided as the elevator door closed, and with an expectant glance at her Clefable was teleported out of the lobby.

Tanzee went up to Jett's office. The door was left ajar so her Pokémon could come and go easily.

In the short amount of time she'd been out, the plant had once again grown exponentially. Vines were starting to spread out of the large pot, weaving their way across the edge of her desk and cascading down akin to the gentle branches of a willow tree. The flower alone had grown to the size of a small bush around Tanzee's own height, and somehow looked all the more elegant in such grandeur; its three scarlet petals with black accents and the tall pyramid in the center, and the intoxicatingly sweet scent, the siren song of eternity.

Tanzee, captivated by the giant flower and its berry-like perfume, reached out to the petals with interest. The Pokémon's tail brushed against the dewy vines in the process.

Like in a jungle breeze, ever so softly, the leaves stirred.

The Stone Emporium was a boutique on Vernal Avenue, well-known for its high quality evolution stones and fine jewelry. This was where Jett had gone, and within half-an-hour was returning to her office carrying a little bag with her purchase.

Jett took the long way back, strolling down the street with Clefable skipping by her side and taking in the last of the afternoon breeze. The sun was already descending when she arrived at her company's headquarters, and found Corbeau waiting for her in the lobby.

"Corbeau. What a surprise, I didn't expect to see you so soon," she remarked.

"Jett, I have some urgent information to give you," Corbeau told her succinctly. "Where were you?"

"I bought a Leaf Stone for Tanzee."

"Tanzee...?"

"My Pansage," she replied. "I'm planning to evolve him. I know he's going to be thrilled when he sees this."

She noticed a frown on his face and began to worry what the urgent news was all about.

"What is so important that couldn't wait a couple of hours?" Jett asked.

"The plants are carnivorous."

She stared at him, and he proceeded to explain. "It's not a problem – if they're small. But these grow enormous. The scientist I had looking at them says it's because they've been irradiated with elemental energy."

"Marcus never said anything about that...Do you think he knows?"

Corbeau shrugged his shoulders. "I have no clue at this point as to whether he knows or not, but let me tell you the rest of what the scientist told me."

He took Jett by the arm gently and guided her to sit down, as he continued talking.

"They lure Pokémon to them with their scent," he said, "Large Pokémon eat the plants and get affected by the energy. Small Pokémon get ensnared by the vines and smothered in acid."
